('87', 0, 7, 9, 282) May 29, 1945
('87', 0, 8, 10, 295) MY DEAR C. R., Yours written on the train.
('87', 0, 8, 11, 338) I am overwhelmed with work.
('87', 0, 8, 12, 366) Hence the delay, if delay it may be called.
('87', 0, 8, 13, 410) I agree with you about the existence of the evil.
('87', 0, 8, 14, 460) My diffculty is as to the way to deal with it.
('87', 0, 8, 15, 507) I want you to depend upon me to do so as soon as I see the way.
('87', 0, 8, 16, 571) Nothing will then stop me.
('87', 0, 8, 17, 598) Nor am I unvigilant.
('87', 0, 8, 18, 619) I am glad you liked your stay in Mahabaleshwar.
('87', 0, 8, 19, 667) I hope Papa and Narasimhan came to you at once and that you are doing well.

('87', 1, 2, 3, 906) May 29, 1945

('87', 1, 6, 6, 1120) [PS.] Temple entry is not the only way to remove untouchability; it is one of the many ways all of which have to be taken.

('87', 4, 1, 2, 4191) 10. LETTER TO AMRITLAL V. THAKKAR
('87', 4, 2, 3, 4225) MAHABALESHWAR, May 29, 1945
('87', 4, 3, 4, 4253) BAPA, 1. I have your letter.
('87', 4, 3, 5, 4282) I cannot fall in line with Sir Puru shottamdas’s opinion.
('87', 4, 3, 6, 4340) The office should never be in Bombay.
('87', 4, 3, 7, 4378) How ever, I do not insist on anything.
('87', 4, 3, 8, 4417) It is you who have to think over it.
('87', 4, 3, 9, 4454) 2. It will be very good if some concrete work is taken up.
('87', 4, 3, 10, 4513) I have welcomed Devdas’s suggestion.
('87', 4, 3, 11, 4550) I have also said that he should demonstrate it in practice.
('87', 4, 3, 12, 4610) I have already expressed my opinion that “impatience dose not make a mango tree bear fruit’’ 1. The work is new.
('87', 4, 3, 13, 4723) It is like injecting life into a corpse.
('87', 4, 3, 14, 4764) 3. The farther the money is kept from the shadow of the Government, the better.
('87', 4, 3, 15, 4844) I have no objection if you keep it with some good firm.
('87', 4, 3, 16, 4900) 4. I do not want to interfere in small things and also in the schemes.
('87', 4, 3, 17, 4971) In fact I should have bothered myself only with the principles.
('87', 4, 3, 18, 5035) 5. What you write about Kamle is correct.
('87', 4, 4, 19, 5077) BAPU SHRI THAKKAR BAPA SERVANTS OF INDIA SOCIETY POONA CITY
('87', 4, 5, 20, 5137) From a copy of the Gujarati: Pyarelal Papers.
('87', 4, 5, 21, 5183) Courtesy: Pyarelal

('87', 5, 8, 18, 6450) 13. LETTER TO PIR ILAHIBUKSH May 29, 1945
('87', 5, 9, 19, 6492) BHAI PIR SAHEB, I have your letter 2. Perhaps you know that I know the Urdu script.
('87', 5, 9, 20, 6576) There is very little difference between Sindhi and Urdu scripts.
('87', 5, 9, 21, 6641) You must also be knowing that I call Hindustani that language which rural Hindus and Muslims of North India speak and which they write in the Nagari or Urdu scripts.
('87', 5, 9, 22, 6807) So, if I may advise you, I would suggest that you teach Hindustani to Hindu and Muslim boys in all the schools in both the scripts.
('87', 5, 9, 23, 6939) It is an old thing but did not make much progress.
('87', 5, 9, 24, 6990) Now an association has come into being which propagates this scheme.
('87', 5, 10, 25, 7059) Yours, From the Hindi original: Pyarelal Papers.
('87', 5, 10, 26, 7108) Courtesy: Pyarelal
('87', 5, 11, 27, 7127) 1 Santtilal, addressee’s brother.
('87', 5, 11, 28, 7161) 2 Asking what language should be taught in Sind and how 3 At the end there is the following instruction in Gujarati: “Give a reply on these lines and get my signature.”

('87', 7, 6, 13, 8896) 17. INTERVIEW TO DENTON J. BROOKS JR.
('87', 7, 7, 14, 8934) MAHABALESHWAR, [On or before May 30, 1945] 2
('87', 7, 8, 15, 8979) QUESTION: Gandhiji, is there any special message you would care to send to the Negro people of America?
('87', 7, 9, 16, 9083) ANSWER: My life is its own message.
('87', 7, 9, 17, 9119) If it is not, then nothing I can now write will fulfil the purpose.
('87', 7, 10, 18, 9187) When asked to comment on the probable trend of the race relations, Mr. Gandhi said: My faith burns brighter today, even brighter than it has in the
('87', 7, 11, 19, 9335) 1 According to the source, the interviewer, a Negro journalist, was Far Eastern correspondent of Chicago Defender, in which the interview appeared on June 10, 1945. Brooks reported: “ .
('87', 7, 11, 20, 9521) in the exclusive interview given to me last week .
('87', 7, 11, 21, 9572) Morarjee Castle, Mahabaleshwar .
('87', 7, 11, 22, 9605) Gandhiji was observing silence, with the exception of an hour after evening prayers.
('87', 7, 11, 23, 9690) I asked questions and he hurriedly jotted down his answers.” 2 Brooks reported that “later in the evening” he had attended the “prayers”.
('87', 7, 11, 24, 9828) Gandhiji reached Panchgani on May 31, 1945, in the evening.
('87', 8, 0, 1, 9888) VOL. 87: 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 9
('87', 8, 1, 2, 9928) past; we are fast approaching a solution to roublesome race problems.
('87', 8, 2, 3, 9998) This he feels will be accomplished in spite of present day discouraging symptoms.
('87', 8, 2, 4, 10080) And he still feels that the best weapon for use by underprivileged peoples is non violence.
('87', 8, 3, 5, 10172) Pointing to his recent statement 1 made at the beginning of the San Francisco Conference, he indicated that India’s freedom was closely identified with the welfare of all other under privileged peoples.
('87', 8, 3, 6, 10375) At that time he had said:
('87', 8, 4, 7, 10401) The freedom of India will demonstrate to all exploited races of the earth that their freedom is very near and that in no case will they be exploited.
('87', 8, 4, 8, 10551) The Hindu, 15 6 1945
('87', 8, 5, 9, 10572) 18. DRAFT FOREWORD TO “GITA ANI GITAI”
('87', 8, 6, 10, 10611) I have quite a few co workers who are more or less exclusively engaged in doing my work and who, therefore, have a claim on me.
('87', 8, 6, 11, 10739) However, such a claim should not be made in so many words; otherwise I would not be able to do the work which I ought to do.
('87', 8, 6, 12, 10864) Kundarji asked me to write a Foreword for Gitai ani Gitai and Gitadhyayasangati.
('87', 8, 6, 13, 10945) How could I say ‘No’ to him?
('87', 8, 6, 14, 10974) I agreed and so it became my duty to read Gitadhyayasangati and Kundarji’s Preface.
('87', 8, 6, 15, 11058) This took away one hour of my time.
('87', 8, 6, 16, 11094) The work will suffer if I let my hours go thus and the Gita will cease to be my spiritual dictionary.
('87', 8, 7, 17, 11196) The beauty of Gitai is that its meaning and music are rendered 3
('87', 8, 8, 18, 11261) in Marathi in such a way that those who do not know the original Gita can enjoy reading it as they would the original.
('87', 8, 9, 19, 11380) M. K. GANDHI MAHABALESHWAR, May 30, 1945
('87', 8, 10, 20, 11421) From a copy of the Hindi: Pyarelal Papers.
('87', 8, 10, 21, 11464) Courtesy: Pyarelal
('87', 8, 11, 22, 11483) 1 Vide “Staement to the Press”,17 4 1945. 2 Between this and the next paragraph, in the source, appears the Foreword to Gitadhyayasangati; the following item.
('87', 8, 11, 23, 11642) 3 By Vinoba Bhave
('87', 9, 0, 1, 11660) 10 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 9, 1, 2, 11701) 19. FOREWORD TO “GITADHYAYASANGATI”
('87', 9, 2, 3, 11737) Vinoba has been my co worker ever since the Ashram at Kochrab 1 was set up.
('87', 9, 2, 4, 11813) He has done plenty of work that I wanted him to do or that which was dear to me.
('87', 9, 2, 5, 11894) Take for instance Gitadhyay asangati.
('87', 9, 2, 6, 11932) I had asked for a little, Vinoba gave me much.
('87', 9, 2, 7, 11979) The readers should know that the idea of reciting the Gita in fourteen days and then in seven days first occurred to me in Yeravda Prison.
('87', 9, 2, 8, 12118) I told Vinoba of what I had in mind and asked for his approval and also his suggestions.
('87', 9, 2, 9, 12207) In reply he sent me Gitadhyayasangati.
('87', 9, 2, 10, 12246) By having this before him the reader who wants to concentrate on the Gita and put its teaching into practice will 2 be benefited.
('87', 9, 3, 11, 12376) MAHABALESHWAR, May 30, 1945
('87', 9, 4, 12, 12404) [From Hindi]
('87', 9, 5, 13, 12417) Gitadhyayasangati

('87', 11, 2, 3, 13791) May 30, 1945
('87', 11, 3, 4, 13804) VALJI, Bapa is very busy.
('87', 11, 3, 5, 13830) He is not like me.
('87', 11, 3, 6, 13849) If I don’t get a man, I can beg for services.
('87', 11, 3, 7, 13895) His eyes are weak.
('87', 11, 3, 8, 13914) He would need someone to write in Gujarati and Hindi.
('87', 11, 3, 9, 13968) If you or some boys or anybody else can help him, go and meet him and tell him so.
('87', 11, 3, 10, 14051) At present he is in the Servants of India Society of Poona.
('87', 11, 3, 11, 14111) The help is to be given there.
('87', 11, 3, 12, 14142) It would be better if someone who is known was available.
('87', 11, 3, 13, 14200) Please let me know if there is any book in Marathi or Gujarati on veterinary science.

('87', 11, 7, 19, 14474) 24. LETTER TO JAISUKHLAL GANDHI
('87', 11, 8, 20, 14506) May 30, 1945
('87', 11, 9, 21, 14519) JAISUKHLAL, I saw what you wrote at the bottom of Vinodini’s letter.
('87', 11, 9, 22, 14588) How did you get dysentery?

('87', 20, 1, 2, 23800) 40. LETTER TO RAMASWAMI
('87', 20, 2, 3, 23824) May 30, 1945
('87', 20, 3, 4, 23837) RAMASWAMI, I have not replied to two of your letters.

('87', 20, 3, 6, 23911) The postcard does not call for any reply.
('87', 20, 3, 7, 23953) You must have received money for the months of April and May.
('87', 20, 3, 8, 24015) I am sorry that there was some irregularity in sending the money.
('87', 20, 3, 9, 24081) I am responsible for that.
('87', 20, 3, 10, 24108) When your continuing became uncertain probably I was not able to make up my mind as to what should be the duty of the Ashram towards you.
('87', 20, 3, 11, 24246) I do not remember it well.
('87', 20, 3, 12, 24273) I am sorry that your parents were a little hurt.
('87', 20, 3, 13, 24322) Only the poor have true and pure ambition.
('87', 20, 3, 14, 24365) That certainly lifts them high and throws them into the hands of the demon.
('87', 20, 3, 15, 24441) This is the translation of “between the devil and the deep sea”.
('87', 20, 3, 16, 24506) What you say is not true.
('87', 20, 3, 17, 24532) When you feel that you are going to fall into the hands of Satan, you should give up that work.
('87', 20, 3, 18, 24628) I don’t think it proper to say more to you in this connection.
('87', 20, 3, 19, 24691) You must yourself realize your duty.
('87', 20, 3, 20, 24728) Do not blame the zemindar if you want the fame which you can acquire with your money.
('87', 20, 3, 21, 24814) Just as among the poor, there are also good and bad among them.

('87', 20, 3, 23, 24940) Ponder over the basic things while you are entering a new life.

('87', 21, 0, 1, 25243) 22 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 21, 1, 2, 25284) 41. FOREWORD TO “VARNAVYAVASTHA” 1
('87', 21, 2, 3, 25319) I do not have the time to read this book again.
('87', 21, 2, 4, 25367) I do not even wish to.
('87', 21, 2, 5, 25390) I have many other things to do.
('87', 21, 2, 6, 25422) In my opinion a man daily moves either forward or backward.
('87', 21, 2, 7, 25482) He never stands still.
('87', 21, 2, 8, 25505) The whole world is moving.
('87', 21, 2, 9, 25532) There is no exception to it.
('87', 21, 2, 10, 25561) I will be making a wrong statement if I say that I am today what I was yesterday and will remain the same in future.
('87', 21, 2, 11, 25678) In fact I should not even have such a desire.
('87', 21, 2, 12, 25724) It is right however that my writings and utterances should not be such as to confuse others.
('87', 21, 2, 13, 25817) I should not write things which can bear two interpretations.
('87', 21, 2, 14, 25879) That is to say I should always have an eye to truth and non violence while writing, speaking or doing anything.
('87', 21, 2, 15, 25991) I can say that I have been doing that ever since I gave my word to my mother.
('87', 21, 2, 16, 26069) In fact I became a devotee of truth ever since I reached the age of understanding.
('87', 21, 2, 17, 26152) This does not mean that I have had or even today have a full vision of truth and ahimsa.
('87', 21, 2, 18, 26241) But I do believe that my vision of truth and ahimsa is becoming clearer every day.
('87', 21, 2, 19, 26324) Therefore it would not be correct to say that my views on Varnashrama are the same as they were in the past.
('87', 21, 2, 20, 26433) I have said that the varnas and the ashramas are the gifts of Hinduism to the world, and I still adhere to that view.
('87', 21, 2, 21, 26551) But today neither the varnas nor the ashramas of my conception are in existence anywhere.
('87', 21, 2, 22, 26641) They should form a part of our religion.
('87', 21, 2, 23, 26682) But it can be said that these days the ashramas have disappeared altogether and varnas are found in the form of privileges.
('87', 21, 2, 24, 26806) The claim of being a Brahmin, a Kshatriya, a Vaishya connotes pride.
('87', 21, 2, 25, 26875) How can there be pride where there is religion?
('87', 21, 2, 26, 26923) And the Shudras are not taken into consideration at all!
('87', 21, 2, 27, 26980) Shudras are low and the Ati Shudras are the lowest of the low.
('87', 21, 2, 28, 27043) This is not religion but a negation of it.
('87', 21, 2, 29, 27086) Where are the four varnas of the Gita today?
('87', 21, 2, 30, 27131) Varna is entirely different from caste.
('87', 21, 2, 31, 27171) There are numerous castes.
('87', 21, 2, 32, 27198) I know of no authority for caste in the Gita or any other scripture.
('87', 21, 2, 33, 27267) The Gita has prescribed four varnas and they are based on one’s aptitudes and karma.
('87', 21, 2, 34, 27352) I am saying four just to give you an example.
('87', 21, 2, 35, 27398) There can be more or less varnas than that.
('87', 21, 2, 36, 27442) But there prevails only one varna today,
('87', 21, 3, 37, 27483) 1 Gandhiji wrote this under the title “Key to My Writings”.
('87', 22, 0, 1, 27543) VOL. 87: 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 23
('87', 22, 1, 2, 27584) that is, of Shudras’, or, you may call it, Ati Shudras’, or Harijans’ or untouchables.
('87', 22, 1, 3, 27671) I have no doubt about the truth of what I say.
('87', 22, 1, 4, 27718) If I can bring round the Hindu society to my view, all our internal quarrels will come to an end.
('87', 22, 1, 5, 27816) That will also put an end to communal riots between Hindus and Muslims, and the people of India will occupy a place of honour in the world.
('87', 22, 1, 6, 27956) Just as it is not dharma but adharma to believe in the distinctions of high and low, so also colour prejudice is adharma.
('87', 22, 1, 7, 28078) If a scripture is found to sanction distinctions of high and low, or distinctions of colour, it does not deserve the name of scripture.
('87', 22, 1, 8, 28214) One should approach the scriptures with the assumption that they would not say anything which is contrary to dharma.
('87', 22, 1, 9, 28331) Caste distinctions have taken such deep roots that they have infected the Muslims, Christians and others.
('87', 22, 1, 10, 28437) It is true that there are class destinations in more or less degree in all the religions, from which one has to conclude that that failing is inherent in every human being.
('87', 22, 1, 11, 28610) We can cleanse ourselves of that failing only by pure dharma.
('87', 22, 1, 12, 28672) I have not found sanction for such distinctions between high and low in any scriptures.
('87', 22, 1, 13, 28760) In the eyes of religion all men are equal.
('87', 22, 1, 14, 28803) An educated, intelligent and affluent man is no better than an ignorant, stupid and poor man.
('87', 22, 1, 15, 28897) If he is cultured, that is to say, if he has been purified by dharma, he will utilise his education, intelligence and money in the service of his illiterate, stupid and poor brethren.
('87', 22, 1, 16, 29081) And he will strive to give them, that is to say, the whole world, what he has got.
('87', 22, 1, 17, 29164) If that is true of religion, then in our present condition, devoid of religion our dharma lies in becoming Ati Shudras voluntarily.
('87', 22, 1, 18, 29296) A man should consider himself not the owner of his property but its trustee or custodian.
('87', 22, 1, 19, 29386) He will use it for the service of society.
('87', 22, 1, 20, 29429) He will accept only that much for himself as he has earned with his labour.
('87', 22, 1, 21, 29505) If that happens, no one will be poor and no one rich.
('87', 22, 1, 22, 29559) In such a system all religions will naturally be held equal.
('87', 22, 1, 23, 29620) Therefore all quarrels arising out of religions, caste and economic differences will be ended.
('87', 22, 1, 24, 29715) At this stage it is also necessary to ponder over one further point.
('87', 22, 1, 25, 29784) It is the foremost dharma of a subject nation to free itself of the bondage at the very first opportunity.
('87', 22, 1, 26, 29891) A subject is compulsorily an Ati Shudra.
('87', 22, 1, 27, 29932) It is immaterial whether he has been given titles, or whether he is made a judge or a peon of a judge or whether he is a king or a pauper.
('87', 22, 1, 28, 30071) The more titles one has the more abject is one’s condition under alien rule.
('87', 22, 1, 29, 30148) Thus by correlating freedom with dharma and making the latter widespread, we shall in the natural course of
('87', 23, 0, 1, 30256) 24 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 23, 1, 2, 30297) things arrive at the state described in the previous paragraph.
('87', 23, 1, 3, 30361) A man who wants to follow his dharma will not bother about the time when this may be realized.
('87', 23, 1, 4, 30456) If many people do so, it will not only end our subjection but there will not be any anarchy or confusion in our freedom.
('87', 23, 1, 5, 30577) This is the swaraj of my dreams.
('87', 23, 1, 6, 30610) I yearn for that.
('87', 23, 1, 7, 30628) I want to live for the attainment of it.
('87', 23, 1, 8, 30669) I am devoting every breath of my life to that effort.
('87', 23, 1, 9, 30723) The reader is therefore requested to discard anything in this book which may appear to him incompatible with my views given above.
('87', 23, 1, 10, 30854) In order to save me labour, a friend who has digested my views and has done so with great effort, has sent me a brief note of my present views.
('87', 23, 1, 11, 30998) Shri Kishorelal thought that I could save time if I could affix my signature to it.
('87', 23, 1, 12, 31082) I was free to make any corrections I liked.
('87', 23, 1, 13, 31126) But while going through it I found that Shri Kishorelal has, as is his wont, read through the whole book, has pondered over it and then has drafted a note as a testimony of my present views.
('87', 23, 1, 14, 31317) Even if I cannot sign it, it should be published along with this.
('87', 23, 1, 15, 31383) There is no incompatibility between his key and mine.
('87', 23, 1, 16, 31437) Shri Kishorelal’s note is based on the study of this book and therefore it would be more helpful to the readers.
('87', 23, 1, 17, 31550) May Truth alone triumph.
('87', 23, 2, 18, 31575) MOHANDAS KARAMCHAND GANDHI
('87', 23, 3, 19, 31602) MAHABALESHWAR, May 31, 1945

('87', 28, 7, 14, 37147) 50. NOTE FOR “GRAM UDYOG PATRIKA”
('87', 28, 8, 15, 37181) May 1945 A correspondent asks me to speak about other village industries as I do about khadi.
('87', 28, 8, 16, 37275) Khadi is the only handicraft which is widespread.
('87', 28, 8, 17, 37325) Besides, I have likened it to the sun, and the other industries to the planets.
('87', 28, 8, 18, 37405) 2 The sun is only one, while the planets are many and new ones are being discovered.
('87', 28, 8, 19, 37490) For the present, it will be enough if you concentrate on hand made paper, hand ground flour, hand pounded rice, ghani pressed oil, honey from live bees, hide from dead cattle and articles made from it in villages, village walking sticks, village buttons, palm gur, etc.
('87', 28, 8, 20, 37760) As a matter of fact agriculture is a village industry, hence grains,
('87', 28, 9, 21, 37829) 1 The addressee who was working among the tribes of Jaunsar and Bawer at Nagthat, near Mussoorie, built the Ashok Ashram and started a school and dispensary in memory of Kasturba Gandhi.
('87', 28, 9, 22, 38016) He opened the Ashram in July 1942, but was arrested a month after.
('87', 28, 9, 23, 38083) Having been released, he was developing it into a training centre for village industries.
('87', 28, 9, 24, 38173) 2 Vide “How to improve village industries”, 21 5 1945 .
('87', 29, 0, 1, 38229) 30 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 29, 1, 2, 38270) fruit and articles made from them can be village products.
('87', 29, 1, 3, 38329) In short, when villages are self contained, cities will be dependent on them.
('87', 29, 1, 4, 38407) As you can see, the tooth brush belongs to the cities, while datun belongs to the villages and is better; tooth powder is of the city while charcoal powder, chalk or salt are of the village.
('87', 29, 1, 5, 38598) When you become village minded in this way you will find numerous village articles useful to you.
('87', 29, 2, 6, 38696) From a copy of the Hindi: Pyarelal Papers.

('87', 31, 1, 2, 40261) 55. LETTER TO AMRITLAL V. THAKKAR
('87', 31, 2, 3, 40295) June 1, 1945
('87', 31, 3, 4, 40308) BAPA, I have your long letter.
('87', 31, 3, 5, 40339) It does not reveal your anger but your practical sense.
('87', 31, 3, 6, 40395) However, the practical sense suggests that you should not relinquish the post you have accepted.
('87', 31, 3, 7, 40492) I had often read in South Africa the letter Gokhale wrote on his return from England expressing his deep apology.
('87', 31, 3, 8, 40606) 1 One of the sentences in that letter was: “How can I give up the office under duress when I have not accepted it under duress?” You are in a similar situation.
('87', 31, 3, 9, 40767) The only difference is that there is no pressure at all on you.
('87', 31, 3, 10, 40831) So it will be sheer cowardice to give up the post and with that the freely available opportunity of rendering service.
('87', 31, 3, 11, 40950) The tongue that calls you a coward only condemns itself.
('87', 31, 3, 12, 41007) Moreover, to give up doing service means putting a burden on Mridula, that is, on the women.
('87', 31, 3, 13, 41100) Why should you do that?
('87', 31, 3, 14, 41124) Give it up when I tell you and if what I tell you appeals to you.
('87', 31, 3, 15, 41190) The fact is Mridula does not want to give up anything.
('87', 31, 3, 16, 41245) I feel that we should leave only when she has become competent enough to enable us to give up.
('87', 31, 3, 17, 41340) In the mean time, we should retain her and encourage her.
('87', 31, 3, 18, 41398) The words of mine you quote are the only true words.
('87', 31, 3, 19, 41451) She should not consider anything as passed by me unless it has received your independent approval.
('87', 31, 3, 20, 41550) However, if she does not do that, you should ignore it but should do what you want to.
('87', 31, 3, 21, 41637) About Rs. 2,000 I clearly remember having told her that she should not consider anything passed as long as Bapa had not considered and approved it independently.
('87', 31, 3, 22, 41799) If she has employed two or three women, I would certainly be in favour of retaining them.
('87', 31, 3, 23, 41889) But if you disapprove of it, I will do the same.
('87', 31, 3, 24, 41938) I do not feel that you are giving me trouble.
('87', 31, 3, 25, 41984) Whatever the trouble may be, it will end.
('87', 31, 3, 26, 42026) I will see to it.
('87', 31, 3, 27, 42044) What remains now is the question about the office.
('87', 31, 3, 28, 42095) It is in a large measure in your own hands.
('87', 31, 4, 29, 42139) 1 In 1897, before the Welby Commission in England, Gokhale made certain statements, based on letters he received from Poona on the plague operations in that city, relating to the conduct of British soldiers who were employed to evacuate compulsorily the infected houses.
('87', 31, 4, 30, 42410) But when the persons who supplied him with the information refused to substantiate the allegations, Gokhale had to withdraw and apologize for the statements which caused indignation in England and in India.
('87', 32, 0, 1, 42617) VOL. 87: 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 33
('87', 32, 1, 2, 42658) I will see what I can do about Bhavnagar and Kathiawar.
('87', 32, 1, 3, 42714) It is good that Anantrai 1 is here.
('87', 32, 1, 4, 42750) Come here only if you want change of air and not to know my mind or to explain to me.
('87', 32, 1, 5, 42836) Moreover, at the moment you want to work for Servants of India Society.
('87', 32, 1, 6, 42908) You may gladly do that.
('87', 32, 1, 7, 42932) I might, if I wanted, come to your help.
('87', 32, 1, 8, 42973) But I do not want to do that.
('87', 32, 1, 9, 43003) I have to curb many such good intentions.
('87', 32, 1, 10, 43045) Enough for now.

('87', 33, 1, 2, 44143) 57. LETTER TO KISHORELAL G. MASHRUWALA
('87', 33, 2, 3, 44182) PANCHGANI, June 1,1945
('87', 33, 3, 4, 44205) KISHORELAL, I have gone through your article.
('87', 33, 3, 5, 44251) You will find a reference 1 to it in my “Key”.
('87', 33, 3, 6, 44298) If you approve of it then let your article be published under your name.
('87', 33, 3, 7, 44371) I have changed pronouns and have deleted some portion of it—you will easily be able to find it.
('87', 33, 3, 8, 44467) I am sending my “Key” for your approval.
('87', 33, 3, 9, 44508) I have been at it since yesterday and completed it just now.
('87', 33, 3, 10, 44569) If you have changes to suggest I have to examine them.
('87', 33, 3, 11, 44624) If I have to, then send it back to me.
('87', 33, 3, 12, 44663) If there is no time, then I don’t see any harm if the book is published without my “Key”.

('87', 42, 7, 8, 56623) 76. DISCUSSION WITH SHRIMAN NARAYAN 1
('87', 42, 8, 9, 56661) PANCHGANI, June 2, 1945
('87', 42, 9, 10, 56685) QUESTION: To my mind one of the greatest problems confronting us at the present moment is that of combating the systematic plan of economic exploitation by flooding the market with foreign consumer goods.
('87', 42, 9, 11, 56890) This is bound to spell disaster to Indian industrialization whether small scale or large scale.
('87', 42, 9, 12, 56986) And the pity of it is that our own businessmen and industrialists seem to be vying with one another in becoming glorified agents of foreign manufacturers.
('87', 42, 9, 13, 57141) Do you not think that an urgent need of the hour is the rousing of public conscience against the matter of foreign goods?
('87', 42, 9, 14, 57263) I think constructive workers should take up this programme immediately.
('87', 42, 9, 15, 57335) A countrywide propaganda for the use of village manufactured and swadeshi goods can also prove to be a very elective and economic sanction against foreign domination.
('87', 42, 9, 16, 57502) What is your opinion and advice?
('87', 42, 10, 17, 57535) ANSWER: The difficulty cannot be met by carrying on propaganda, however wide and intensive.
('87', 42, 10, 18, 57627) The first thing is to demonstrate its economic fallacy.
('87', 42, 10, 19, 57683) Let us recognize that the industrialists are not conscious traitors.
('87', 42, 10, 20, 57752) They honestly believe that their plan will bring prosperity to the masses.
('87', 42, 10, 21, 57827) They are wrong.
('87', 42, 10, 22, 57843) But how to show that they are wrong save by patient study and publication thereof and by working so as to show that the masses respond to the work and actually prosper?
('87', 42, 10, 23, 58012) This demands hard thinking, hard study and harder constructive work among the masses.
('87', 42, 10, 24, 58098) They have to manufacture for their own use.
('87', 42, 11, 25, 58142) 1 Principal, Govindram Saxeria College, Wardha
('87', 43, 0, 1, 58189) 44 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 43, 1, 2, 58230) Just picture to yourself every village producing and manufacturing everything for its own use.
('87', 43, 1, 3, 58325) This must mean some surplus for the cities of India going from the villages.
('87', 43, 1, 4, 58402) This means also automatic stoppage of all exploitation and prosperity without having to exploit the outer world.
('87', 43, 2, 5, 58515) The Bombay Chronicle, 4 6 1945
('87', 43, 3, 6, 58546) 77. MESSAGE FOR BHARATI MEMORIAL 1
('87', 43, 4, 7, 58581) PANCHGANI, [Before June 3, 1945] 2
('87', 43, 5, 8, 58616) My blessings to efforts to perpetuate Bharati’s memory.

('87', 43, 7, 10, 58717) 78. DISCUSSION WITH HAREKRUSHNA MEHTAB 3
('87', 43, 8, 11, 58758) PANCHGANI, June 1/3, 1945
('87', 43, 9, 12, 58784) QUESTION: Do you think there has been any change in the country to warrant any change in the Congressmen’s attitude towards the war which they adopted in 1939?
('87', 43, 9, 13, 58944) If you think there is no change, then has it not come to this that, in your opinion, Congressmen should not go back to ministries in the present circumstances?
('87', 43, 10, 14, 59104) ANSWER: You ask for my personal opinion.
('87', 43, 10, 15, 59145) I give it for what it is worth.
('87', 43, 10, 16, 59177) Mine can in no sense be an authoritative opinion.
('87', 43, 10, 17, 59227) You should examine the Congress attitude not of 1939 but of 1942. So far as I am aware the Congress offered help in 1942 provided that certain conditions were fulfilled.
('87', 43, 10, 18, 59397) It is for the Congress to lay down the conditions for the present acceptance of office.
('87', 43, 10, 19, 59485) These must always be in terms of independence.
('87', 43, 11, 20, 59532) 1The Bombay Chronicle, 4 6 1945, reported that on June 3, C. Rajagopa lachari laid the foundation stone for the memorial building to house a library of the works of the Tamil poet, Subrahmanya Bharati, at his birth place, Ettayapuram, in Tamil Nadu.
('87', 43, 11, 21, 59782) Gandhiji wrote the message in Tamil.
('87', 43, 11, 22, 59819) 2 ibid 3 According to A. P. I. report, Harekrushna Mehtab released “written questions and answers” to the Press after “full discussion with Gandhiji for three days”.
('87', 44, 0, 1, 59985) VOL. 87: 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 45
('87', 44, 1, 2, 60026) There is no civil disobedience now and you have placed your manifold constructive programme before the country.
('87', 44, 1, 3, 60138) Do you approve of the following definition of the constructive programme—to tackle the immediate problems of the masses and to try to solve them on non violent lines as enunciated by you?
('87', 44, 1, 4, 60326) This definition includes the work of trying to check black marketing, profiteering and also the inflow of foreign consumer goods by insisting upon the use of swadeshi goods.
('87', 44, 1, 5, 60500) You have only a partial grasp of the constructive programme of my conception.
('87', 44, 1, 6, 60578) It is comprehensive and all pervading.
('87', 44, 1, 7, 60617) Stoppage of black marketing, profiteering and foreign consumer goods must precede construction.
('87', 44, 1, 8, 60713) They are not part of the programme, but the programme to be effective and universal has to do that weeding process.
('87', 44, 1, 9, 60829) The whole programme is swadeshi.
('87', 44, 2, 10, 60862) Would you ask Congressmen to seek co operation from other parties and even from Government agencies in the prosecution of the constructive work?
('87', 44, 2, 11, 61007) How can the constructive programme be prevented from being used for the purpose of consolidating the party position for elections and for other purposes?
('87', 44, 2, 12, 61161) I have been crying myself hoarse to persuade Congressmen to adopt whole heartedly the constructive programme without party motive or any other.
('87', 44, 2, 13, 61305) It is its own motive.
('87', 44, 2, 14, 61327) I seek the co operation of the whole nation and also of the Government in carrying out the programme, naturally, on our own terms.
('87', 44, 2, 15, 61458) If the latter give honest co operation, it must mean independence without violence and without fuss.
('87', 44, 2, 16, 61559) If the constructive programme is worked for electioneering purposes it will carry with it the seeds of its own disease.
('87', 44, 2, 17, 61679) Men can prevent vicious people from using the best things for the worst of purposes.
('87', 44, 3, 18, 61764) What should be the attitude of Congressmen towards all those who are now building up an organization which may come in clash with Congress at some stage or other in future?
('87', 44, 3, 19, 61937) The Congress position should be of complete non violent non co operation with those who will stab the country in the back.
('87', 44, 4, 20, 62060) The Bombay Chronicle, 4 6 1945
('87', 45, 0, 1, 62091) 46 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI

('87', 50, 0, 1, 67909) VOL. 87: 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 51
('87', 50, 1, 2, 67950) 88. STATEMENT ON SYRIAN LEBANESE QUESTION 1
('87', 50, 2, 3, 67994) PANCHGANI, [On or after June 3, 1945] 2
('87', 50, 3, 4, 68034) I have purposely refrained from saying anything on the Syrian and Lebanese question, not because I have felt less than others but because I have felt more.
('87', 50, 3, 5, 68190) The injustice is so obvious and glaring.
('87', 50, 3, 6, 68231) It pains me to think that our Muslim fellow countrymen feel that they can effectively ask for justice to the Syrians and Lebanese as fellow Muslims.
('87', 50, 3, 7, 68380) Syrians and the Lebanese are a mixed population.
('87', 50, 3, 8, 68429) 3 Their liberty is at stake not as Muslims but as a separate nation.
('87', 50, 3, 9, 68498) The struggle of Syria and Lebanon for independence should evoke the sympathy of the whole of India, and it must be made a national issue, instead of one of a particular section or community.
('87', 50, 3, 10, 68689) 4 Muslims should speak as Indians and should invite the cooperation of all India including members of all religions.
('87', 50, 3, 11, 68806) For instance the voice of Indian Christians speaking as Christians as apart from other Indians in international affairs must fall flat.
('87', 50, 3, 12, 68942) This is the lesson of history everywhere, but in India, to my mind, the Khilafat issue emphasizes the lesson which we seem to have forgotten.
('87', 50, 3, 13, 69084) The Muslims headed by the late Hakim Saheb sought the co operation of all India and the Khilafat question became a plank in the National Congress.
('87', 50, 3, 14, 69231) And it drew world attention.
('87', 50, 3, 15, 69260) Had the history of victorious Turkey been written differently, India would have taken an effective part in the settlement of the Khilafat question.
('87', 50, 3, 16, 69408) India divided against itself will have no effect on the council of the nations of the world.
('87', 50, 3, 17, 69501) The Bombay Chronicle, 8 6 1945; also The Hindu, 8 6 1945
('87', 50, 4, 18, 69558) 1 The nationalist movement in Syria and Lebanon had come into violent conflict with France which had been ruling the area under a mandate since 1923. France had called for negotiations and at the same time despatched two contingents of troops.
('87', 50, 4, 19, 69802) There were widespread clashes culminating in the French bombardment of Damascus on May 29 and 30. The statement was made in an “exclusive interview to the special representative of the Orient Press” of India.
('87', 50, 4, 20, 70011) 2 From the expression “our Muslim fellow countrymen feel”, presumably a reference to M. A. Jinnah’s statement of June 3, which assured Syrians and Lebanese of the support of “the hundred million Muslims of India”.
('87', 50, 4, 21, 70225) Jinnah had also warned that “not only the Middle East and Muslim India but also the whole of the Muslim world will flare up” if freedom was not granted.
('87', 50, 4, 22, 70378) 3 Being predominantly Christian 4 This paragraph is reproduced from The Hindu, 8 6 1945, in which it was reported independently under the date line “Panchgani, June 6”.

('87', 58, 1, 2, 78793) 102. LETTER TO P. C. GHOSH
('87', 58, 2, 3, 78820) PANCHGANI, June 4, 1945
('87', 58, 3, 4, 78844) BHAI PROFULLA, The Working Committee of the Kasturba Memorial Trust met at Mahabaleshwar.
('87', 58, 3, 5, 78934) Your objection to keeping the entire fund with the Head Office was put up to it.
('87', 58, 3, 6, 79015) I had told you that I would write to you and clarify the whole thing.
('87', 58, 3, 7, 79085) You know that the fund raised in Bombay is kept in the Head Office.
('87', 58, 3, 8, 79153) I feel that the same should be done with the money raised in Calcutta.
('87', 58, 3, 9, 79224) The committee which is formed now is to consider how the money will be spent in the villages.
('87', 58, 3, 10, 79318) Why should we argue over where the money should be kept?
('87', 58, 3, 11, 79375) Your duty is to submit a scheme and if it is accepted, to get it implemented.
('87', 58, 3, 12, 79453) You must be knowing that the committee for collecting the money and the committee for spending it are not the same.
('87', 58, 3, 13, 79569) It is true that the same three persons are on most of the committees.
('87', 58, 3, 14, 79639) But that is our misfortune.
('87', 58, 3, 15, 79667) There are very few workers and those who give the money claim the right to have a control over the spending of it.
('87', 58, 3, 16, 79782) When they are deserving, it may become our duty to have the donors on the committees.
('87', 58, 3, 17, 79868) What more can I write?
('87', 58, 3, 18, 79891) I would suggest that you explainmy view to the committee and write a satisfactory letter.
('87', 58, 4, 19, 79981) Blessings from BAPU [PS.] Hope you are well now.
('87', 58, 5, 20, 80030) SHRI PROFULLA CHANDRA GHOSH 14/8 GARIHA ROAD BALLYGUNGE CALCUTTA

('87', 62, 11, 17, 84404) Only then will he shine and succeed in hs effort.
('87', 62, 11, 18, 84454) I have read your statement.
('87', 62, 11, 19, 84482) Now ease your mind of the burden.

('87', 62, 11, 21, 84587) If you do only that much, though you have ceased to be Secretary, the management will remain in your hands, for your experience and patience are your own and cannot be transferred to anybody.
('87', 62, 11, 22, 84779) Those who wish may take them from you.
('87', 62, 11, 23, 84818) Even if they do there will be no diminution of your possession.
('87', 62, 11, 24, 84882) This is the meaning of the verse

('87', 65, 1, 2, 87750) 115. LETTER TO BHULABHAI DESAI
('87', 65, 2, 3, 87781) June 7, 1945
('87', 65, 3, 4, 87794) BHAI BHULABHAI, I have sat down to write this letter after the morning prayer, i.
('87', 65, 3, 5, 87876) e., at about 6 o’clock.
('87', 65, 3, 6, 87900) I saw your letter last evening.
('87', 65, 3, 7, 87932) I am writing this with the sole desire that you should retain the eminent position you occupy.
('87', 65, 3, 8, 88027) I hesitate to write because I write without any official authority.
('87', 65, 3, 9, 88095) There is a very big difference between yourlegal style and my own old fashioned one or rather between your legal knowledge and mine.
('87', 65, 3, 10, 88228) I am saying this deliberately and not through false modesty.
('87', 65, 3, 11, 88289) I learnt while studying law and practising it— and I have always acted upon the understanding—that a lawyer, having accepted the brief of an untruthful case should give it up as soon as he realizes its untruthfulness, that is, ask for a verdict against his client.
('87', 65, 3, 12, 88554) I know that there is a section of the bar which holds the opposite view.
('87', 65, 3, 13, 88627) They ask what the function of the judge would be if an advocate himself were to sit in judgment on his case.
('87', 65, 3, 14, 88736) I have always held, and hold even today, that that section is mistaken.
('87', 65, 3, 15, 88808) This is my own view.
('87', 65, 3, 16, 88829) I find the whole of your argument unconvincing.
('87', 65, 3, 17, 88877) It should be of no concern either to you or to me whether it is the question of League or the non League Muslims.
('87', 65, 3, 18, 88991) If the case of those who hold opposite views from ours is just, I would come forward to support it notwithstanding opposition from everybody else, but if a case is unjust I would not support it even if it were my own son’s.
('87', 65, 3, 19, 89215) I also believe that Bhai Khuhro’s brief should not be rejected merely on the ground that he is believed to be inciting the Hurs.
('87', 65, 3, 20, 89344) But, if after having accepted his brief and studied it, I felt that he was guilty, my moral sense would teach me that, if permitted by the client, I should plead guilty and take the punishment.
('87', 65, 3, 21, 89538) But if he should not permit me, I would request him to release me and engage another lawyer.
('87', 65, 3, 22, 89631) I remember having done that for two Muslim clients.
('87', 65, 3, 23, 89683) In one case I asked for a verdict against the client and in another admitted the client’s guilts and got his punishment much reduced and ultimately had him released after he had undergone some years of imprisonment.
('87', 65, 3, 24, 89899) I therefore do not hesitate to request you that if, after examining the papers of Khuhro’s case, you feel that he is innocent, you should fight for him, but if you feel that he is guilty, you should advise him to plead guilty or ask him to relieve you.
('87', 65, 3, 25, 90152) This is but a suggestion from me.
('87', 65, 3, 26, 90186) If, after weighing it carefully you do not approve of it, reject it.
('87', 65, 3, 27, 90255) Do not look to the person
('87', 66, 0, 1, 90281) VOL. 87 : 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 67
('87', 66, 1, 2, 90323) who has given advice; only think over the advice.
('87', 66, 1, 3, 90373) As desired by you, I am sending your letter to Choithram.
('87', 66, 1, 4, 90431) I feel that he should have written to you.
('87', 66, 1, 5, 90474) I also believe that he should not have formed prejudiced views.
('87', 66, 1, 6, 90538) But that is a characteristic not only of our life but of that of the whole world.
('87', 66, 1, 7, 90620) We have observed that even the most balanced men have not been able to shed this weakness.
('87', 66, 1, 8, 90711) Hence, do not pay attention to Choithram’s shortcomings.
('87', 66, 1, 9, 90768) If you find any substance in his otherwise faulty reasoning, accept it.
('87', 66, 1, 10, 90840) I have not explained to Choithram the argument I have put before you.
('87', 66, 1, 11, 90910) I amenclosing a copy of the letter I have written 1 to him.
('87', 66, 1, 12, 90970) I understand what you say regarding Chimur Ashti.
('87', 66, 1, 13, 91020) Please see to it that those prisoners are not hanged.
('87', 66, 1, 14, 91074) Blessings from BAPU
('87', 66, 2, 15, 91094) From the Gujarati original: Bhulabhai Desai Papers.
('87', 66, 2, 16, 91146) Courtesy: Nehru Memorial Museum and Library

('87', 66, 4, 19, 91289) I hope you have sent one to Satis Babu also or written to him.

('87', 72, 6, 8, 99191) 127. LETTER TO LORD SAMUEL 3
('87', 72, 7, 9, 99220) PANCHGANI, June 8, 1945
('87', 72, 8, 10, 99244) DEAR FRIEND, I had your letter of 25th July, 1944. Perhaps you are right that after this lapse of time it would not be very profitable to enter into a detailed discussion of the various points raised by your speech in the House of Lords.
('87', 72, 8, 11, 99482) There is one point in your letter however which challenges a reply.
('87', 72, 8, 12, 99550) You have adduced two passages from my writings in support of your remarks in the House of Lords that “When Mr. Gandhi called upon the British Government to quit India, he said it would be for the Congress to take delivery.” This, you have argued, connotes totalita rian spirit in the Congress.
('87', 72, 8, 13, 99844) I have seen the full text of the Harijan articles referred to in your letter.
('87', 72, 8, 14, 99922) Copies of these are enclosed for easy reference.
('87', 72, 8, 15, 99971) The passages cited by you are from the Harijan of June 15, 1940, and December 3, 1938, respectively.
('87', 72, 8, 16, 100072) You will not fail to observe that they have no relevancy to the point at issue.
('87', 72, 8, 17, 100152) The Congress decision in connection with its “Quit India” demand inAugust 1942
('87', 72, 9, 18, 100231) 1Vide “Telegram to Manager, Sevagram Ashram”, 7 6 1945 and “Letter to Balvantsinha”, 7 6 1945. 2 ibid 3 Herbert Louis Samuel, Liberal leader
('87', 73, 0, 1, 100372) 74 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 73, 1, 2, 100413) is embodied in the official declaration of its President, Maulana Abul Kalam Azad to which I have referred in my last letter 1 to you.
('87', 73, 1, 3, 100548) To that decision the Congress still stands committed and one fails to see what bearing my writings in Harijan have upon it.
('87', 73, 1, 4, 100672) The fact however is that the quotations given by you are incapable of bearing the totalitarian interpretation you have put upon them.
('87', 73, 1, 5, 100806) The British Government have often declared that they would gladly part with power if there was a body in India ready and fit to take charge.
('87', 73, 1, 6, 100947) What is wrong in the Congress trying to qualify itself for that onerous duty?
('87', 73, 1, 7, 101025) That it does not want power for itself but for the whole people of India is made absolutely clear by me in the course of the same article from which you have quoted.
('87', 73, 1, 8, 101191) Here is the relevant extract:
('87', 73, 2, 9, 101221) Its non violence forbids the Congress from standing aloof and riding the high horse as the opponents say.
('87', 73, 2, 10, 101327) On the contrary it has to woo all parties, disarm suspicion and create trust in its bona fides.
('87', 73, 2, 11, 101423) Is it not the normal goal of every party in a democratic State to aspire to convert the whole country to its view and to become its mouthpiece?
('87', 73, 2, 12, 101567) Does not the party in power in the House of Commons take delivery of the machinery of administration from the outgoing party—its predecessor?
('87', 73, 2, 13, 101709) And is not the formation of coalition cabinets under the party system of government an exception rather than the rule?
('87', 73, 2, 14, 101828) Then how can the refusal of the Congress to sacrifice or water down its ideal for the sake of securing unanimity with other parties be called totalitarian?
('87', 73, 2, 15, 101984) With regard to the second passage from the article on the Princes it is only necessary to point out that it was the British Government itself that called upon the Congress to secure an agreement with the States, at the Second Round Table Conference.
('87', 73, 2, 16, 102234) There could therefore be nothing wrong in its inviting the Princes to treat with it.
('87', 73, 2, 17, 102319) The essential fact to remember in this connection is that the Congress has no other sanction except that of persuasion and self suffering, any other being precluded by its creed.
('87', 73, 2, 18, 102498) On the other hand, is not violence, euphemistically called physical force, the basis and backbone of the totalitarian spirit?
('87', 73, 2, 19, 102624) If it is, and if you believe in
('87', 73, 3, 20, 102656) 1 Vide “Letter to Lord Samuel”, 15 5 1943.
('87', 74, 0, 1, 102699) VOL. 87 : 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 75
('87', 74, 1, 2, 102741) my bona fides about non violence and also of the Congress, youcannot accuse either Of the totalitarian spirit.
('87', 74, 2, 3, 102852) I a m , Yours sincerely, M. K. GANDHI Enclosures: 2

('87', 77, 1, 2, 106475) 133. LETTER TO MUNNALAL G. SHAH
('87', 77, 2, 3, 106507) PANCHGANI, June 8, 1945
('87', 77, 3, 4, 106531) MUNNALAL, I have read the accompanying letter 1. If what he writes is true, tell him this: “Do not go to Khadi Vidyalaya for training.
('87', 77, 3, 5, 106666) Stay here, do physical labour, have your daily meals and learn what you can.” If he can put m sufficient physical labour and if you feel inclined, keep him.
('87', 77, 3, 6, 106823) Do not give him a separate room.
('87', 77, 3, 7, 106856) He will rest wherever free space is available.
('87', 77, 3, 8, 106903) If we can discontinue the practice of assigning a room to each person, we shall be able to accommodate more people.
('87', 77, 3, 9, 107019) Do not keep him if he does not observe all the rules.
('87', 77, 3, 10, 107073) In this way we can even test whether such persons are sincere or not.
('87', 77, 3, 11, 107143) Ramaswami’s letter is enclosed.

('87', 81, 1, 2, 111171) 141. LETTER TO KIKIBEHN LALVANI
('87', 81, 2, 3, 111203) PANCHGANI, June 8, 1945
('87', 81, 3, 4, 111227) DEAR KIKIBEHN 1, Pyarelalji has received your letter.
('87', 81, 3, 5, 111281) Your English statements raise a big question in my mind.
('87', 81, 3, 6, 111338) When you cannot yourself write in English, what is the point of getting them written and then signing them?
('87', 81, 3, 7, 111446) At the most do as Ba did.
('87', 81, 3, 8, 111472) She narrated her anguish over Harilal’s behaviour to Devdas who translated it into English and gave it to the newspapers saying that it was almost a literal translation of what Ba had narrated to him.
('87', 81, 3, 9, 111673) You must have seen it.
('87', 81, 3, 10, 111696) Such writings will carry greater weight and with that the mother tongue will also gain in importance.
('87', 81, 3, 11, 111798) I will go to the extent of saying that whatever ideas occur to you, express them as they are either in Sindhi or Hindi.
('87', 81, 3, 12, 111918) Ultimately whatever is translated into English is as useless as fruit ripened artificially.
('87', 81, 3, 13, 112010) I am all right.
('87', 81, 4, 14, 112026) Blessings from BAPU SHRI KIKIBEHN LALVANI BHARAT KHADI BHANDAR BURUS ROAD, KARACHI

('87', 87, 1, 2, 118365) 152. A LETTER
('87', 87, 2, 3, 118379) [June 9, 1945] 1
('87', 87, 3, 4, 118396) I did have that in my mind.
('87', 87, 3, 5, 118424) Palme Dutt is a well known figure.
('87', 87, 3, 6, 118459) He will be able to give a fight to Amery.
('87', 87, 3, 7, 118501) Patel 2, I do not know.
('87', 87, 3, 8, 118525) Nor do I wish that too many Indians should stand for election.
('87', 87, 3, 9, 118588) This is going to be an important election.
('87', 87, 3, 10, 118631) It does not matter if he is defeated.
('87', 87, 3, 11, 118669) If, moreover, I give in this case the same opinion that I did in Patel’s, it might be interpreted to mean that I am refusing to support him because he is a communist.
('87', 87, 3, 12, 118836) I have no such thought in my mind.
('87', 87, 3, 13, 118871) The distinction is worth understanding.
('87', 87, 3, 14, 118911) If you do not follow it, ask me again.
('87', 87, 3, 15, 118950) If you don’t wish to post the letter today, it may be posted tomorrow.
('87', 87, 3, 16, 119021) It is more important that you should understand my idea.

('87', 88, 6, 18, 120450) 155. LETTER TO SHRIKRISHNADAS JAJU
('87', 88, 7, 19, 120485) PANCHGANI, June 9, 1945
('87', 88, 8, 20, 120509) BHAI JAJUJI, You must have seen Chi.
('87', 88, 8, 21, 120546) Narandas’s appeal.
('87', 88, 8, 22, 120565) If I can find a copy here I shall enclose it with this.
('87', 88, 8, 23, 120621) In my view it would be a great thing.
('87', 88, 8, 24, 120659) Labour is the basis of the bank here.
('87', 88, 8, 25, 120697) It can be a great thing if it can be done.
('87', 88, 8, 26, 120740) In my opinion we should fully take part in it.
('87', 88, 8, 27, 120787) And our part will consist only in accepting contributions.
('87', 88, 8, 28, 120846) We shall not give anything.
('87', 88, 8, 29, 120874) That is to say that we shall take the yarn from persons offering at least one hank of it for Narandas’s sutrayajna and give a receipt for it.
('87', 88, 8, 30, 121016) Then we have to send an account of it to Narandas every week or every month.
('87', 88, 8, 31, 121093) This does not involve much work on our part and it can bring in quite a lot.

('87', 93, 7, 15, 127066) 165. NEED FOR KHADI EDUCATION
('87', 93, 8, 16, 127096) PANCHGANI, June 10, 1945 Soon after the khadi activity was started, the need began to be felt for the workers to have a scientific knowledge of all the processes of khadi production.
('87', 93, 8, 17, 127279) Therefore, as early as 1927 ’28 a school was opened in the Sabarmati Ashram to teach spinning and weaving.
('87', 93, 8, 18, 127386) As the khadi activity grew and it became necessary to pay attention to other aspects such as making khadi attractive to look at and low priced, the lack of scientific knowledge of the subject began to be felt more and more every day.
('87', 93, 8, 19, 127620) A few workers were able, through their own individual efforts and experience, to gather many useful bits of knowledge.
('87', 93, 8, 20, 127739) The tools were experimented on and improved.
('87', 93, 8, 21, 127784) All the lovers of khadi know that the late Shri Maganlal Gandhi worked very hard in this connection.
('87', 93, 8, 22, 127885) It then became clear that it was very necessary for every khadi worker to learn the science of khadi.
('87', 93, 8, 23, 127987) I have from the very beginning emphasized this.
('87', 93, 8, 24, 128035) I prepared a questionnaire about the various things khadi workers ought to know.
('87', 93, 8, 25, 128116) In 1937, I also wrote three articles for the Harijan.
('87', 93, 8, 26, 128170) In an article dated February 13, 1937, I wrote : 1
('87', 93, 9, 27, 128221) In my opinion it should be made obligatory on every khadi worker engaged in any of the production centres of the A. I. S. A. to know the elements of this science.
('87', 93, 9, 28, 128384) Following this policy, khadi schools were later opened.
('87', 93, 9, 29, 128440) A khadi
('87', 93, 10, 30, 128448) 1 Vide “What Khadi workers should know”, 13 2 1937.
('87', 94, 0, 1, 128500) VOL. 87 : 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 95
('87', 94, 1, 2, 128542) school was opened by the Central Office [of the A. I. S. A.].
('87', 94, 1, 3, 128604) The syllabi for the “spinning workers”, “weaving workers” and “Khadi Prathama” were prepared and arrangements were made to impart instruction according to them.
('87', 94, 1, 4, 128765) It was also hoped then that all the workers of the Charkha Sangh would join these schools by turns,and complete their training.
('87', 94, 1, 5, 128893) In order to save workers from any kind of difficulties, it was arranged to pay them, over and above their regular salaries, travelling allowance and other allowances since it was thought that the workers would have to spend more on food in an unfamiliar place.
('87', 94, 1, 6, 129154) One regrets however that the workers have not shown any increased enthusiasm for learning the khadi science.
('87', 94, 1, 7, 129263) Now that the Charkha Sangh has taken up the new work it becomes obligatory on the part of khadi workers to train themselves in khadi science.
('87', 94, 1, 8, 129405) Without that it will be impossible to carry on the new khadi programme.
('87', 94, 1, 9, 129477) According to the new programme, the sales depots too will almost be like production centres.
('87', 94, 1, 10, 129570) Not only that; after some time we intend to convert all khadi production centres and sales depots into khadi education centres.
('87', 94, 1, 11, 129698) It will then be unnecessary to send workers to the schools for khadi training.
('87', 94, 1, 12, 129777) We have to train in the science of khadi all the workers, new as well as old.
('87', 94, 1, 13, 129855) Those in charge of the branches are therefore requested to scrutinize the list of workers to assess what training a particular worker needs and to make arrangements for such training to be given.
('87', 94, 1, 14, 130051) Lists of workers should in this way be made and forwarded to the Central Office.
('87', 94, 1, 15, 130132) In order to make the training obligatory, we should make the rise in salary dependent on the degree of khadi education possessed by the worker.
('87', 94, 1, 16, 130276) We should also accept the principle that the khadi worker has to pass an examination.
('87', 94, 1, 17, 130362) Those who fail should not be considered qualified.
('87', 94, 1, 18, 130413) So long as we do not seriously take up the question of khadi education, how can we hope to succeed?
('87', 94, 1, 19, 130513) I have said that if we are true khadi workers, we should have as much awareness, as much knowledge and as much alertness as is considered necessary for a member of the I. C. S.
('87', 94, 2, 20, 130690) M. K. GANDHI
('87', 94, 3, 21, 130703) From a copy of the Hindi: Pyarelal Papers.
('87', 94, 3, 22, 130746) Courtesy: Pyarelal

('87', 95, 6, 12, 131094) 167. LETTER TO HAMID KHAN
('87', 95, 7, 13, 131120) PANCHGANI, June 10, 1945
('87', 95, 8, 14, 131145) BHAI HAMID KHAN, I have your letter.
('87', 95, 8, 15, 131182) I knew Ganesh Shankar Vidyarthi 2 well.
('87', 95, 8, 16, 131222) I had great regard for him.
('87', 95, 8, 17, 131250) I have already given my view on the question of a memorial.
('87', 95, 8, 18, 131310) You must know it.
('87', 95, 8, 19, 131328) Go through it if you have not already done so.
('87', 95, 8, 20, 131375) You can’t raise a memorial by constructing a building or spending money.
('87', 95, 8, 21, 131448) A man thinks that having given the money he has done his duty.
('87', 95, 8, 22, 131511) Therefore, in my opinion, it will be a true memorial to Ganesh Shankar Vidyarthi if, at least in Kanpur, and as far as possible throughout India, Hindus and Muslims should unite and instead of cutting each other’s throats be prepared to lay down their lives for each other.
('87', 95, 8, 23, 131785) If this comes about, let me know and then ask for my blessings.
('87', 95, 8, 24, 131849) What is there in merely collecting money?
('87', 95, 8, 25, 131891) Let me also know who are on the Committee?
('87', 95, 8, 26, 131934) And what are the grounds for believing that what has not been achieved so far will be achieved now?
('87', 95, 8, 27, 132034) I have seen the aim of the Memorial Committee.
('87', 95, 8, 28, 132081) That will not make the memory of the deceased immortal, only bring ridicule to it.
('87', 95, 8, 29, 132164) Two or three rich men can jointly put up such buildings, give jobs to a few persons and thus deceive themselves and others that they haveraised a memorial to Vidyarthiji.
('87', 95, 8, 30, 132335) But I will regard it as a mockery.

('87', 96, 9, 21, 133446) 169. SPEECH TO RASHTRA SEVA DAL MEMBERS, PANCHGANI 1
('87', 96, 10, 22, 133499) June 10, 1945
('87', 96, 11, 23, 133513) Gandhiji congratulated the volunteers for having walked down to Panchgani from Wai in spite of the rain.
('87', 96, 11, 24, 133618) He was sorry he could not invite them all to theprayer hall.
('87', 96, 11, 25, 133679) The hall belonged to a school.
('87', 96, 11, 26, 133710) That they allowed him, a rebel, to hold a prayer meeting in their hall was the essence of the prayer.
('87', 96, 11, 27, 133812) He knew that the volunteers did
('87', 96, 12, 28, 133844) 1 According to the A. P. I. report, this is “the authorized version” of Gandhiji’s speech to about 300 volunteers at a function organized by Dr. B. D. Savant in Parsi Girls High School.
('87', 96, 12, 29, 134030) Gandhiji spoke in Hindustani which was rendered into Marathi.
('87', 97, 0, 1, 134092) 98 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 97, 1, 2, 134133) not all pray.
('87', 97, 1, 3, 134147) He had been in close touch with volunteer organizations in India ever since 1919. Yet he had not been able to make them prayer minded.
('87', 97, 1, 4, 134282) He had failed to create in them an enthusiasm for prayer.
('87', 97, 2, 5, 134340) Again he had explained to them right from the beginning that a volunteer must always serve the people and serve them only through truth and non violence.
('87', 97, 2, 6, 134494) Yet there were very few men and women amongst them who had accepted truth and non violence as their creed.
('87', 97, 2, 7, 134601) He was convinced that real swaraj, that is, swaraj for the rich and the poor alike, could not be won except through truth and non violence.
('87', 97, 3, 8, 134741) They had just seen the end of a terrible war.
('87', 97, 3, 9, 134787) It had made people doubt if truth really counted in this world.
('87', 97, 3, 10, 134851) The Allies had won, but their victory had been the result of superior arms and superior man power.
('87', 97, 3, 11, 134950) He could not enthuse over it as a victory of truth over falsehood.
('87', 97, 3, 12, 135017) At the same time he wanted to make it clear to them that a victory for the Axis would have been far worse.
('87', 97, 3, 13, 135124) The Axis had accepted violence as their creed.
('87', 97, 3, 14, 135171) The Allies had not done so.
('87', 97, 3, 15, 135199) They at least paid lip service to peace and freedom, and truth and non violence.
('87', 97, 3, 16, 135280) It was true that their actions belied their profession.
('87', 97, 3, 17, 135336) A major part of humanity today consisted of oppressed and enslaved nations.
('87', 97, 3, 18, 135412) It was his conviction that, if India could win swaraj through truth and non violence, she would be able to bring deliverance to all the other oppressed nations.
('87', 97, 4, 19, 135573) Many of the volunteers were not clad in khadi.
('87', 97, 4, 20, 135620) He had called the spinning wheel the symbol of truth and non violence and therefore also of swaraj.
('87', 97, 4, 21, 135720) That was why it had found a place in the national flag.
('87', 97, 4, 22, 135776) Therefore he exhorted them all to spin and produce khadi for their own clothes.
('87', 97, 4, 23, 135856) Thus they would help to combat the cloth shortage in the country and help the naked poor.
('87', 97, 5, 24, 135946) Lastly he asked them all to learn Hindustani.
('87', 97, 5, 25, 135992) Hindustani was the language that Hindus and Mussalmans of North India spoke and which was written in Nagari and Urdu scripts.
('87', 97, 5, 26, 136118) All those who spoke Hindustani did not know both the scripts.
('87', 97, 5, 27, 136180) But those who wished to serve all should make it a point of honour to learn both the scripts.
('87', 97, 5, 28, 136274) The Bombay Chronicle, 11 6 1945
('87', 98, 0, 1, 136306) VOL. 87 : 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 99
('87', 98, 1, 2, 136348) 170. SILENCE DAY NOTE TO BHULABHAI DESAI 1
('87', 98, 2, 3, 136391) June 11, 1945 Considering all that is happening around us, I see danger in this partnership with the League.
('87', 98, 2, 4, 136500) One thing is definite, namely, that until the members of the Working Committee are freed and can express their opinion, nothing can be done in the name of the Congress.
('87', 98, 2, 5, 136669) It is also definite that if the Chimur Ashti prisoners and other such prisoners are hanged, the situation will become impossible.
('87', 98, 2, 6, 136799) Unless the League’s attitude shows a change without any expectation of gain I will have no deal with it even if the Congress Working Committee consents.
('87', 98, 2, 7, 136952) This is for you yourself to think over and decide.
('87', 98, 2, 8, 137003) You are in a better position to understand the truth than anybody else.
('87', 98, 2, 9, 137075) The distinction that is being made between the League Muslims and the others seems to me dangerous from every point of view.
('87', 98, 2, 10, 137200) I don’t think it safe to countenance any such position.
('87', 98, 2, 11, 137256) Think carefully over what you said last night regarding this.
('87', 98, 2, 12, 137318) Will the 40 per cent Congress quota include any representatives of the Hindu Mahasabha or of Harijans?
('87', 98, 2, 13, 137421) What about the Sikhs, Parsis, Christians, etc.?
('87', 98, 2, 14, 137469) Whether you have discussed this with the League or not is irrelevant here.
('87', 98, 2, 15, 137544) When the time for final decision comes, the Congress will have to consider all these points.
('87', 98, 2, 16, 137637) The Congress will not be in the same position as the League.
('87', 98, 2, 17, 137698) It will have to take into account all the interests in the country, whereas the League is concerned with the interests only of the Muslims supporting it.
('87', 98, 2, 18, 137852) You will have to be ready to face all these complications.
('87', 98, 2, 19, 137911) You will definitely not be able to bring the ship to port by disregarding the parties other than the League.
('87', 98, 2, 20, 138020) Please understand my limitations fully before you proceed further.
('87', 98, 2, 21, 138087) As I have explained, my temper is progressively becomingmore uncompromising.
('87', 98, 2, 22, 138164) I use the word “uncompromising”
('87', 98, 3, 23, 138196) 1 “In Mahatma Gandhi—The Last Phase, Vol. I, Book One, p.
('87', 98, 3, 24, 138254) 120, Pyarelal explains: “The rejection of the appeal for mercy on behalf of the Ashti Chimur prisoners at this stage hardened Gandhiji’s attitude.
('87', 98, 3, 25, 138401) Extremely sensitive to the slightest variation in the moral atmosphere around him, he became more and more insistent on the ‘present tense’.
('87', 98, 3, 26, 138542) This was very much in evidence when Bhulabhai met him at Mahabaleshwar.”
('87', 99, 0, 1, 138615) 100 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 99, 1, 2, 138657) in a good sense, so take it in that spirit.
('87', 99, 1, 3, 138701) Against my indifference to the Parliamentary scheme and my increasing faith in non violent non co operation, you can safely place my loyalty to you.
('87', 99, 1, 4, 138850) It will not let myself go beyond the limits of what I have given you in writing.
('87', 99, 1, 5, 138931) But it is difficult even for me to say where my uncompromising spirit will take me, for I am coming to put ever increasing faith in the Unseen Power and, therefore, I think very little about tomorrow.
('87', 99, 1, 6, 139132) I started writing this before 6 and it is 6.30 now.

('87', 102, 0, 1, 142538) VOL. 87 : 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 103
('87', 102, 1, 2, 142581) 176. TWO POSERS [On or before June 12, 1945] 1
('87', 102, 2, 3, 142628) Shri Sailendra Nath Chattopadhyaya of the United Press puts the following posers before me: “Why do you wish to live for 125 years, and what is Ram Rajya?” The questions are so apt and reasonable that, contrary to my wont these days, I want to answer them.
('87', 102, 2, 4, 142885) Many visitors and correspondents put the same questions.
('87', 102, 2, 5, 142942) I take this opportunity therefore and once for all, I hope, of answering them to the best of my ability.
('87', 102, 2, 6, 143047) The idea of 125 years’ life flashed across my mind, while I was speaking on the 8th August, 1942, to the meeting of the A.I.C.C. in Bombay.
('87', 102, 2, 7, 143187) I might have mentioned the same thing before in private conversation.
('87', 102, 2, 8, 143257) If I did, I have no recollection.
('87', 102, 2, 9, 143291) I am a constant student of the Ishopanishad which contains only eighteen mantras.
('87', 102, 2, 10, 143373) The first half of the second mantra means: “Only doing works of service on this earth, you should wish to live 120 or 125 years.” The word in the original denoting the number is translated by the word ‘hundred’, but I had seen just then a com mentary which took the number to mean 120 or 125. I purposely used the highest figure at the meeting, as signifying the intense wish to live the longest in order to fulfil my allotted work.
('87', 102, 2, 11, 143806) In expressing the wish I only followed my old habit of wishing to act according to the best of my belief.
('87', 102, 2, 12, 143912) Moreover, as a naturopath, I believe in the feasibility of living the full span of life.
('87', 102, 2, 13, 144001) I know that, medically speaking, the chances are against me for I have not always followed nature’s way.
('87', 102, 2, 14, 144106) I began to adopt it fairly strictly in South Africa in 1903 or there about.
('87', 102, 2, 15, 144182) Want of brahmacharya in early married life must also weigh against the full span.
('87', 102, 2, 16, 144264) My conception of nature cure, like everything else, has undergone progressive evolution.
('87', 102, 2, 17, 144353) And for years I have believed that, if a person is filled with the presence of God and has thus attained the state of dispassion, he can surmount handicaps against long life.
('87', 102, 2, 18, 144528) I have come to the conclusion, based on observation and scriptural reading, that when a man comes to that complete living faith in the Unseen Power and has become free from passion, the body undergoesinternal transformation.
('87', 102, 2, 19, 144753) This does not come about by mere wish.
('87', 102, 2, 20, 144792) It needs constant vigilance and practice.
('87', 102, 2, 21, 144834) In spite of both, unless God’s grace descends upon one, human effort comes to naught.
('87', 102, 3, 22, 144920) 1 The article appeared under the date line “Panchgani, June 12”.
('87', 103, 0, 1, 144985) 104 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 103, 1, 2, 145027) Conquest of passion—passion here does not signify animal appetite; of course, it presupposes full control over such appetite—is more difficult to attain.
('87', 103, 1, 3, 145181) If it were otherwise, complete non violence would be easy of achievement.
('87', 103, 1, 4, 145255) With all my knowledge of, and effort at, non violence, I have conquered my passion only to the stage of suppression.
('87', 103, 1, 5, 145372) This involves great strain on both body and mind.
('87', 103, 1, 6, 145422) Subjugation is the real need.
('87', 103, 1, 7, 145452) It does not involve absence of feeling.
('87', 103, 1, 8, 145492) He who identifies himself with every living creature must feel for every kind of woe and yet remain unaffected by it.
('87', 103, 1, 9, 145610) Action proceeding from such equableness is far reaching, pervasive and quickest in its effect.
('87', 103, 1, 10, 145705) Naturally, it is wholly non violent.
('87', 103, 1, 11, 145742) Difficulty of attainment need cause no worry.
('87', 103, 1, 12, 145788) For, being on the right track leads one nearer to the goal.
('87', 103, 1, 13, 145848) Thus, though I wish and even hope to live up to 125 years, what does it matter, if I die tomorrow?
('87', 103, 1, 14, 145947) There is no sense of regret or frustration in me.
('87', 103, 1, 15, 145997) And there will be no anguish in me over an early death.
('87', 103, 1, 16, 146053) Nor does the wish imply slackness of effort, in view of the prospect of a longer life.
('87', 103, 1, 17, 146140) The wish, to be capable of being fulfilled, implies readiness to leave this body without a moment’s notice.
('87', 103, 1, 18, 146248) It connotes an easy fulfilment, from day to day, of the daily duty.
('87', 103, 1, 19, 146316) All strain is an anticipation of death.
('87', 103, 1, 20, 146356) Death does not mean an end of all effort.
('87', 103, 1, 21, 146398) The Eternal Law which we term God will be a mockery, if death were the end of such an effort.
('87', 103, 1, 22, 146492) ‘Hereafter’ is a mystery into which we may not peep.
('87', 103, 1, 23, 146545) We should have enough faith to know that death, after life truly lived, is but a prelude to a better and richer life.
('87', 103, 1, 24, 146663) Now for Ram Rajya.
('87', 103, 1, 25, 146682) It can be religiously translated as Kingdom of God on Earth; politically translated, it is perfect democracy in which, inequalities based on possession and non possession, colour, race or creed or sex vanish; in it, land and State belong to the people, justice is prompt, perfect and cheap and, therefore, there is freedom of worship, speech and the Press—all this because of the reign of the self imposed law of moral restraint.
('87', 103, 1, 26, 147112) Such a State must be based on truth and non violence and must consist of prosperous, happy and self contained villages and village communities.
('87', 103, 1, 27, 147256) It is a dream that may never be realized.
('87', 103, 1, 28, 147298) I find hap piness in living in that dreamland, ever trying to realize it in the quic kest way.
('87', 103, 1, 29, 147393) The Hindu, 12 6 1945
('87', 104, 0, 1, 147414) VOL. 87 : 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 105

('87', 107, 6, 16, 151946) 183. LETTER TO PREMA KANTAK
('87', 107, 7, 17, 151974) PANCHGANI, June 12, 1945
('87', 107, 8, 18, 151999) PREMA, I have your long letter.
('87', 107, 8, 19, 152031) I have explained the ideal to you.
('87', 107, 8, 20, 152066) You yourself can, by keeping it before you, answer all the questions in the same way as every student of geometry can draw a line by keeping Euclid’s ideal line in his mind.
('87', 107, 8, 21, 152240) Now try to understand.
('87', 107, 8, 22, 152263) I know the ideal, and I will, therefore, utilize the services of educated women only for the realization of the ideal.
('87', 107, 8, 23, 152382) If necessary, I will pay them enough for their livelihood.
('87', 107, 8, 24, 152441) But they will give more than what they take.
('87', 107, 8, 25, 152486) If they do not, they will be of no use.
('87', 107, 8, 26, 152526) If it becomes necessary to run a camp to train them as teachers, I will do so.
('87', 107, 8, 27, 152605) Whether I give six months or twelve months or even more to the backward class women will depend on experience.
('87', 107, 8, 28, 152716) Won’t it?
('87', 107, 8, 29, 152726) I shall not bother about that, for, since they will be learning through thecrafts, they will be paying their expenses, or will be fit to do so in the shortest possible period.
('87', 107, 8, 30, 152902) What if people believe that I have failed?
('87', 107, 8, 31, 152945) My failure is not the
('87', 107, 9, 32, 152967) 1 Addressee’s son, Kanu Gandhi 2 Vide the preceding item.
('87', 108, 0, 1, 153025) VOL. 87 : 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 109
('87', 108, 1, 2, 153068) And how can a man who is progressing towards the ideal be regarded to have failed?
('87', 108, 1, 3, 153151) Does the fact that you yourself, though you have lived in the Ashram, are not able to live up to the ideal prove that the ideal is impossible to attain or that you are unworthy?
('87', 108, 1, 4, 153329) If the admission of uneducated women to the camp makes it impossible to run it, then it will be impossible to effect progress in villages.
('87', 108, 1, 5, 153468) Even if it is proved that Acharya Bhagwat has failed or even if he shares your view, I will not be deterred.
('87', 108, 1, 6, 153577) Our mettle will be proved by our making possible what seems impossible today.
('87', 108, 1, 7, 153655) Sushila Pai is here.
('87', 108, 1, 8, 153676) I will give her this letter.
('87', 108, 1, 9, 153705) She will write further.
('87', 108, 1, 10, 153729) And now the next point.
('87', 108, 1, 11, 153753) I stick to what I told you concerning Bhulabhai.
('87', 108, 1, 12, 153802) He is here just now.
('87', 108, 1, 13, 153823) It is 6.40 in the morning.
('87', 108, 1, 14, 153850) He will leave at 10. I don’t know that those who are in prison will be released.
('87', 108, 1, 15, 153931) It will of course be good if they are.
('87', 108, 1, 16, 153970) If people are angry with Bhulabhai, they should be angry with me, too.
('87', 108, 1, 17, 154041) For he will not pursue his plan, which I know, if I disapprove of it.
('87', 108, 1, 18, 154111) I do not believe what the members of the Working Committee are supposed to have said.
('87', 108, 1, 19, 154197) And if they have in fact said that, they have done so without authority.
('87', 108, 1, 20, 154270) What do prisoners know about conditions outside?
('87', 108, 1, 21, 154319) According to my principle, they have no right even to try and know.
('87', 108, 1, 22, 154387) And even if they differ from me, what does it matter?
('87', 108, 1, 23, 154441) They will be free to do what they like after they are released.
('87', 108, 1, 24, 154505) I have no right at all to vote.
('87', 108, 1, 25, 154537) Am I not only an adviser?
('87', 108, 1, 26, 154563) Don’t ever believe what the newspapers say.
('87', 108, 1, 27, 154607) Of what good is it anyway?
('87', 108, 1, 28, 154634) If I knew that I should die tomorrow, such knowledge of the future could only do harm.
('87', 108, 1, 29, 154721) The same is true in this case.
('87', 108, 1, 30, 154752) Yes, I will say this much: Bhulabhai does not know what the newspapers know.
('87', 108, 1, 31, 154829) If so, how am I likely to know?
('87', 108, 1, 32, 154861) How can I or anyone else say what I would do in certain circumstances?
('87', 108, 1, 33, 154932) If you can guess about the future from what I am doing today, you may do so.
('87', 108, 1, 34, 155009) I cannot do even that, for I am daily coming to realize more clearly that we ruin our lives by forming views about hypothetical matters.
('87', 108, 1, 35, 155146) There is meaning only in what we do concerning what is actual.
('87', 108, 1, 36, 155209) All else is meaningless.
('87', 108, 2, 37, 155234) Don’t you still know my limitations and my approach?
('87', 108, 2, 38, 155287) Didn’t Kumarappa resign only after consulting me?
('87', 108, 2, 39, 155337) Wasn’t I a party to the offer of military help in the resolution of August 1942?
('87', 108, 2, 40, 155418) What does it
('87', 108, 3, 41, 155431) 1 What follows is in Gujarati.
('87', 109, 0, 1, 155462) 110 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 109, 1, 2, 155504) matter if, while I do one thing, the others do the opposite and I let them?
('87', 109, 1, 3, 155580) And what else could I do?
('87', 109, 1, 4, 155606) I would tell you only this: that after having been with me for so long, and later staying away from me, you now behave as if you were still with me.
('87', 109, 1, 5, 155755) Even then I would advise you to observe my actions and the views I express, think over them and then do what seems to you best, feeling certain that you will have my support in what you do.
('87', 109, 1, 6, 155945) For I do not wish to make everybody like me.
('87', 109, 1, 7, 155990) My teaching is that everybody should be true to himself.
('87', 109, 1, 8, 156047) Anybody who has digested my teaching will never fall into doubt but will ever go forward.
('87', 109, 1, 9, 156137) Manibehn also is here.
('87', 109, 1, 10, 156160) I have left the rest to Sushila Pai.
('87', 109, 2, 11, 156197) Blessings from BAPU [PS.] Read the letter carefully.
('87', 109, 2, 12, 156250) Ask me again if you do not understand any point.
