('87', 115, 7, 9, 163780) 195. LETTER TO AMRITLAL V. THAKKAR
('87', 115, 8, 10, 163815) PANCHGANI, June 13 1945
('87', 115, 9, 11, 163839) BAPA, I have received a pile of papers from Mridulabehn.
('87', 115, 9, 12, 163896) One of those is of course about her office.
('87', 115, 9, 13, 163940) I am writing in that connection just now in the morning.
('87', 115, 9, 14, 163997) I had forwarded your remarks about the office to her.
('87', 115, 9, 15, 164051) She has raised an objection.
('87', 115, 9, 16, 164080) It is justified.
('87', 115, 9, 17, 164097) She says that if the minutes cannot be amended, then her office should really be shifted to Wardha for the time being.
('87', 115, 9, 18, 164216) I have already expressed the opinion that it is not necessary to do so.
('87', 115, 9, 19, 164288) She can keep her office wherever she wants.
('87', 115, 9, 20, 164332) If this attitude is correct, and according to me it is, then it should be included in the minutes.
('87', 115, 9, 21, 164431) If it is not included, then her office should be shifted to Wardha till the next meeting of the Executive Committee.
('87', 115, 9, 22, 164548) It is clear to me that that can’t be done.
('87', 115, 9, 23, 164591) And it should also be clear to you, because I have said that Mridulabehn can keep her office wherever she likes.
('87', 115, 9, 24, 164704) We must accept that her demand to get that change or addition incorporated in the minutes is justified.
('87', 115, 9, 25, 164808) If she raises her objection constitutionally, I as President cannot deny what I said in the Executive Committee meeting.
('87', 115, 9, 26, 164929) I want to get the work done somehow 1 because the main thing is that the work should be done.
('87', 115, 9, 27, 165023) For the sake of truth it is better to incorporate the change, if Shyamlal has not already done so, and amend the minutes.
('87', 115, 9, 28, 165145) Otherwise we should incorporate it at my instance when the minutes come up for signing.
('87', 115, 9, 29, 165233) By doing so we can wriggle out of the constitutional requirement.
('87', 115, 10, 30, 165299) 1 Literally, “I would have the rice boiled in any water that is available.”
('87', 116, 0, 1, 165375) VOL. 87 : 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 117
('87', 116, 1, 2, 165418) Otherwise I, as President, must say that it is not obligatory on the part of Mridulabehn to take her office to Wardha along with Bapa’s.
('87', 116, 1, 3, 165555) If we do so, we shall not then need any more money for the time being because as long as another resolution is not passed, the office can be retained in the Scindia House without making any payment and she should manage with as many paid workers as there are today.
('87', 116, 1, 4, 165821) We shall do as you want.
('87', 116, 1, 5, 165846) The first proposal accords more with truth, while the second is more in conformity with the requirements of the situation.
('87', 116, 1, 6, 165969) In order to enable you to understand the whole thing better I am sending you Mridulabehn’s letter even though it is marked personal.
('87', 116, 1, 7, 166102) In this connection I have to raise yet another question.
('87', 116, 1, 8, 166159) Do you in your inmost heart feel that it would be better if Mridulabehn gave up the office?
('87', 116, 1, 9, 166251) If you say that she should not leave, then we should have some clear cut decision in writing so that this confusion is cleared once and for all.
('87', 116, 1, 10, 166396) Draw up a draft in accordance with what you have in mind or leave it to me and I shall make it and send it to you for modification.

('87', 119, 11, 19, 171215) 203. LETTER TO PURUSHOTTAMDAS TANDON
('87', 119, 12, 20, 171252) PANCHGANI, June 13, 1945
('87', 119, 13, 21, 171277) BHAI PURUSHOTTAMDAS TANDONJI, I received your letter 1 yesterday.
('87', 119, 13, 22, 171343) If I understand correctly what you write, you and other lovers of Hindi should welcome my new viewpoint and help me.
('87', 119, 13, 23, 171460) But this is not happening.
('87', 119, 13, 24, 171487) People in Gujarat are in a dilemma and are asking me what they should do.
('87', 119, 13, 25, 171561) A son of my
('87', 119, 14, 26, 171573) 1 In his letter of June 8, the addressee had said that he saw no contradiction between the work of the Hindi Sahitya Sammelan and Hindustani Prachar Sabha and requested Gandhiji to reconsider his decision to withdraw from the Hindi Sahitya Sammelan.
('87', 119, 14, 27, 171823) Vide also “Letter to Purushottam Das Tandon”, 25 7 1945.
('87', 120, 0, 1, 171880) VOL. 87 : 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 121
('87', 120, 1, 2, 171923) own nephew and many others like him are doing both Hindi Prachar work and Hindustani Prachar work.
('87', 120, 1, 3, 172022) This creates difficulties.
('87', 120, 1, 4, 172049) You know Perinbehn.
('87', 120, 1, 5, 172069) She wants to work for both.
('87', 120, 1, 6, 172097) But the time has now come for one of the two to be given up.
('87', 120, 1, 7, 172158) If what you say is right, then the need for this should never arise.
('87', 120, 1, 8, 172227) In my view, it should be possible for a person to be the President or Secretary of both the Hindustani Prachar Sabha and the Hindi Sahitya Sammelan.
('87', 120, 1, 9, 172376) That he may not be able to do so because the work would be too heavy is a different matter.
('87', 120, 1, 10, 172468) And if your letter means, as it should mean what I also say, then there can be no reason for any difference of opinion and I shall be greatly delighted.
('87', 120, 1, 11, 172621) I have gone through your statement that you sent me.
('87', 120, 1, 12, 172674) In my view the Hindustani Prachar Sabha is doing only your work and therefore deserves your thanks.
('87', 120, 1, 13, 172774) And you at least should become a member of it.
('87', 120, 1, 14, 172821) I had requested you to be its member but you refused saying that you would keep out so long as Dr. Abdul Haq did not come in.
('87', 120, 1, 15, 172947) Now my request is that if what I write is correct and if we both are of the same view, then this should be clarified by the Hindi Sahitya Sammelan.
('87', 120, 1, 16, 173095) If this is not necessary I shall not insist on it.
('87', 120, 1, 17, 173146) But at least it should be made clear that there is no difference of opinion about it between you and me.
('87', 120, 1, 18, 173251) It is no light matter for me to get out of the Hindi Sahitya Sammelan.
('87', 120, 1, 19, 173322) But just as I withdrew from the Congress in order to serve it the better, in the same way if I leavethe Sammelan it will be to serve the Sammelan, that is, Hindi, the better.
('87', 120, 1, 20, 173497) What you call my new ideas are not really new.
('87', 120, 1, 21, 173544) It would be more correct to say that I am now only putting into practice what I had said when I first became the President of the Sammelan and what I clarified further when I became its President for the second time.
('87', 120, 1, 22, 173761) I shall decide finally after receiving your reply.
('87', 120, 2, 23, 173812) Yours, M. K. GANDHI [From Hindi]
('87', 120, 3, 24, 173845) Rashtrabhashake Prashnapar Gandhiji aur Tandonjika Mahatvapurna Patra Vyavahar, pp.
('87', 120, 3, 25, 173929) 4 5; also Rajarshi Abhinandan Granth, p.

('87', 128, 4, 8, 183320) 218. LETTER TO KRISHNACHANDRA
('87', 128, 5, 9, 183350) PANCHGANI, June 14, 1945
('87', 128, 6, 10, 183375) KRISHNACHANDRA, I have your long letter from Nagpur.
('87', 128, 6, 11, 183428) As for Balkoba, all that can be said is that there has been no steady gain from parpati.
('87', 128, 6, 12, 183517) Now we have to see how he can regain his strength.
('87', 128, 6, 13, 183568) It will be good if he does not find it too hot to be taken back into the room.
('87', 128, 6, 14, 183647) I still abide by whatever I wrote about railways, etc., in Hind Swaraj.
('87', 128, 6, 15, 183719) But that applies to an ideal state.
('87', 128, 6, 16, 183755) It is possible that we may never reach that state.
('87', 128, 6, 17, 183806) Let us not worry about it.
('87', 128, 6, 18, 183833) It is for this reason that I have said that if we do not have railways and other such facilities, we should not feel unhappy.
('87', 128, 6, 19, 183959) We should never make it our duty to multiply such facilities.
('87', 128, 6, 20, 184021) At the same time we should also not make a duty of giving up these things.
('87', 128, 6, 21, 184096) We should have a free and easy attitude in such matters.
('87', 128, 6, 22, 184153) We must use these facilities as little as possible.
('87', 128, 6, 23, 184205) There will be all types of people in our society.
('87', 128, 6, 24, 184255) There certainly are today.
('87', 128, 6, 25, 184282) We have to live with them.
('87', 128, 6, 26, 184309) Non attachment is the only proper dharma under these circumstances.
('87', 128, 6, 27, 184377) The only thing we must be careful about is that we do not deceive ourselves.
('87', 128, 6, 28, 184454) Your statement that trains, etc., should be shunned even as theft, adultery and falsehood is not correct.
('87', 128, 6, 29, 184560) The important reason for this is that even society considers theft, etc., to be immoral.
('87', 128, 6, 30, 184649) Trains, etc., have not been, nor need they be so considered.
('87', 128, 6, 31, 184710) All that we may say is that we shouldnot consider trains, etc., as means of enjoyment.
('87', 128, 6, 32, 184797) I have repeatedly pointed out in my articles where to draw the line.
('87', 128, 6, 33, 184866) Read them and if you give a little thought you will easily be able to draw the line.
('87', 129, 0, 1, 184951) 130 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 129, 1, 2, 184993) Some small books have been written as an aid to the study of Das Kapital.
('87', 129, 1, 3, 185067) Reading them would help.
('87', 129, 1, 4, 185092) Do not worry about the discharge.
('87', 129, 1, 5, 185126) You can stop worrying by intelligently observing the rules [of brahmacharya].

('87', 133, 1, 2, 190494) 225. LETTER TO JAGANNATHDAS 1
('87', 133, 2, 3, 190524) PANCHGANI, June 15, 1945 All handicraft or arts which can be worked in village homes can be and should be taught even though the products of such crafts and arts may be and can only be profitably used for city people.
('87', 133, 2, 4, 190742) Thus carpentry, joinery, drawing, painting, sculpture, brick laying, scientific washing etc., have their proper place in the institute.
('87', 133, 2, 5, 190878) These should not be taught merely mechanically.
('87', 133, 2, 6, 190926) But the why and the wherefore should be explained to the pupils, so that their intellect is fully drawn out and disciplined in the act of learning and working the respective crafts and arts.
('87', 133, 2, 7, 191117) Thus they should be educated morally and intellectually through these.
('87', 133, 2, 8, 191188) Secondly, if the first is carried out to the letter and in the spirit, the whole institution must be self supporting through the sales of work turned out.
('87', 133, 2, 9, 191343) For, in it there would be little or no overhead charge, the idea being to man the insitution from top to bottom through its erstwhile pupils, now turned experts in their respective departments.
('87', 133, 3, 10, 191537) M. K. GANDHI
('87', 133, 4, 11, 191550) From a copy: Pyarelal Papers.
('87', 133, 4, 12, 191580) Courtesy: Pyarelal
('87', 133, 5, 13, 191599) 226. NOTE TO VALLABHBHAI PATEL 2
('87', 133, 6, 14, 191632) PANCHGANI, June 15, 1945 I have thought about your diet.
('87', 133, 6, 15, 191689) I am of the view that you should not eat anything fibrous.
('87', 133, 6, 16, 191748) Hence, among vegetables you should eat gourd and similar other things in which there would be very little of indigestible matter.
('87', 133, 6, 17, 191878) The main diet should consist of milk, glucose,honey and, if you can digest it, butter.
('87', 133, 6, 18, 191965) I think even vegetables with seeds such as brinjals, tomatoes, should be avoided.
('87', 133, 6, 19, 192047) They have sent me from Coimbatore yeast made from bajra, which may be good.
('87', 133, 6, 20, 192123) The point is that you should eat only such food as will not impose a burden on your intestines, and only a small quantity at a
('87', 133, 7, 21, 192250) 1 Of Harijan Industrial School 2 In the source, Manibehn Patel explains: “Vallabhbhai was released from Yeravda Jail on June 15, 1945, in the morning.

('87', 134, 3, 8, 192891) 227. STATEMENT TO THE PRESS
('87', 134, 4, 9, 192919) PANCHGANI, June 15, 1945 On the purely political aspect of the Viceregal statement 1 I prefer to say nothing, now that the members of the Working Commit tee of the Congress are free.
('87', 134, 4, 10, 193102) I can only give them my advice and it is they who have to shape the policy of the Congress and speak and act with authority.
('87', 134, 4, 11, 193227) As soon as I read the broadcast I sent a wire 2 to His Excellency the Viceroy drawing his attention to the fact that I have no locus standi as the “recognized representative of the Congress”.
('87', 134, 4, 12, 193419) That function belongs to the President of the Congress or whoever may be appointed to represent the Congress on a particular occasion.
('87', 134, 4, 13, 193554) For several years I have acted unofficially as an adviser to the Congress whenever required.
('87', 134, 4, 14, 193647) The public will remember that I went with the same unrepresentative character for my talks 3 with Qaid e Azam Jinnah; and I can take up no other position with the British Government, in this instance represented by the Viceroy.
('87', 134, 4, 15, 193875) There is one expression in the Viceregal broadcast which certainly offends my ear and, I hope, will offend that of every poli tically minded Hindu.
('87', 134, 4, 16, 194023) I refer to the expression “caste Hindus”.
('87', 134, 4, 17, 194065) I claim that there is no such person, speaking politically, as a “caste Hindu”,let alone the Congress which seeks to represent the whole of India which is yearning after political independence.
('87', 134, 5, 18, 194259) Does Veer Savarkar or Dr. Shyama Prasad or Dr. Moonje of the Hindu Mahasabha represent caste Hindus?
('87', 134, 5, 19, 194360) Do they not represent all Hindus without distinction of caste?
('87', 134, 6, 20, 194423) 1 Vide Appendix “ Speech broadcast by the Viceroy”, 14 6 1945. 2 This was sent to Private Secretary to the Viceroy, vide “Telegram to Private Secretary to the Viceroy”, 14 6 1945. 3 In September 1944. 4 Vide also “Telegram to Lord Wavell”, 15 6 1945.
('87', 135, 0, 1, 194674) 136 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 135, 1, 2, 194716) Do they not include the so called untouchables?
('87', 135, 1, 3, 194764) Do they themselves claim to be caste Hindus?
('87', 135, 1, 4, 194809) I hope not.
('87', 135, 1, 5, 194821) Of all politically minded Hindus, I know that even the revered Pandit Malaviyaji, though he observes caste distinctions, will refuse to be called a caste Hindu, as distinguished from the other Hindus.
('87', 135, 1, 6, 195022) The modern tendency in Hinduism is to abolish all caste distinctions and this I maintain in spite of my knowledge of reactionary elements in Hindu society.
('87', 135, 1, 7, 195178) I can only hope, therefore, that H. E. the Viceroy has alloowed himself to make use of the expression in utter ignorance.
('87', 135, 1, 8, 195300) I want to acquit him of knowingly wounding the susceptibilities of Hindu society or dividing it.
('87', 135, 1, 9, 195397) I would not have dwelt on this matter but for the fact that it touches the political mind of Hindus in its sensitive spot and carries with it political repercussions.
('87', 135, 1, 10, 195564) The proposed conference can do much useful work if it is put in its proper political setting and is at the very outset rendered immune from any fissiparous tendency.
('87', 135, 1, 11, 195730) Undoubtedly all invitees might appear as Indians conjointly bent on achieving India’s natural goal and not as persons representing several sections of Indian society.
('87', 135, 1, 12, 195897) That is how I have viewed Bhulabhai Liaqat Ali understanding 1 which I suppose laid the foundation for the forthcoming Viceregal conference.
('87', 135, 1, 13, 196038) Shri Bhulabhai Desai’s proposal has no such colouring as the Viceregal broadcast would seem to have.
('87', 135, 1, 14, 196139) I am not ashamed of the part I have played in advising 2 Shri Bhulabhai Desai when he consulted me about his proposal.
('87', 135, 1, 15, 196258) Shri Bhulabhai Desai’s proposal, as I understood it, attracted me as one interested in solving the communal tangle, and I assured him that I would use my influence with the members of the Working Committee and give my reasons for acceptance of his proposal and I have no doubt that if both parties to the proposal correctly represent their constituents and have independence of India as their common goal, things must shape well.
('87', 135, 1, 16, 196688) At this point I must stop and the Working Committee has to take up the thread.
('87', 135, 1, 17, 196767) It is for its members to declare the Congress mind on the impending questions.
('87', 135, 1, 18, 196846) The Bombay Chronicle, 16 6 1945
('87', 135, 2, 19, 196878) 1 Vide Appendix “Desai Liaqat pact”.
('87', 135, 2, 20, 196915) 2 Vide “Silence day note to Bhulabhai Desai”, 11 6 1945.

('87', 138, 1, 2, 198858) 234. LETTER TO LORD WAVELL
('87', 138, 2, 3, 198885) ‘DILKHUSHA’, PANCHGANI, June 16, 1945
('87', 138, 3, 4, 198923) DEAR FRIEND, I thank you for your telegram 1 of yesterday received at 3.45 p.m.
('87', 138, 3, 5, 199003) My second telegram 2, acknowledging your kind telegraphic invitation, evidently crossed yours.
('87', 138, 3, 6, 199098) I am sending you this letter in reply, instead of wiring, because I am anxious that you should understand my position thoroughly.
('87', 138, 3, 7, 199228) However, I am sending you a wire 3 intimating the despatch of this letter.
('87', 138, 3, 8, 199303) For ready reference, I am enclosing herewith a copy of my Press message 4 which was issued yesterday in the morning.
('87', 138, 3, 9, 199420) I would like you to go through it.
('87', 138, 3, 10, 199455) While it is true that my position is technical, the reality of it is truer.
('87', 138, 3, 11, 199531) My official and legal connection with the Congress was deliberately, and with the consent of the All India Congress Committee, severed 5 in order to enable me all the better to serve the common cause.
('87', 138, 3, 12, 199732) This position therefore cannot be changed at will.
('87', 138, 3, 13, 199783) In the forthcoming official conference, I can have no official position.
('87', 138, 3, 14, 199856) My presence in it will change the official colour, unless I become an official representative of the Congress.
('87', 138, 3, 15, 199967) But if you think that my helpis desirable and that without being a member of the conference I am likely to be useful, I shall make it a point to be at your service before and even during the conference proceedings, assuming, of course, that the Working Committee wishes likewise.
('87', 138, 3, 16, 200247) I want to cite an analogy.
('87', 138, 3, 17, 200274) You may have known the late Deenabandhu, as C. F. Andrews was affectionately called by us.
('87', 138, 3, 18, 200365) He severed his official connection with the Cambridge Mission and the Church in order to serve religion, India and humanity better.
('87', 138, 3, 19, 200497) The position he occupied as a valuable link between India and England, whether official or non official and, between all classes and parties, grew as days went.
('87', 138, 3, 20, 200658) If I can, I would love to occupy such a position.
('87', 138, 3, 21, 200708) It may never come to me.
('87', 138, 3, 22, 200733) Man can but try.
('87', 138, 4, 23, 200750) 1 Vide 5th footnote, “Telegram to Privte Secretary to Viceroy”, 14 6 1945. 2 Vide “Telegram to Lord Wavell”, 15 6 1945. 3 Vide “Telegram to Lord Wavell”, 16 6 1945. 4 Vide “Statement to the Press”, 15 6 1945. 5 In October 1934.
('87', 139, 0, 1, 200978) 140 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 139, 1, 2, 201020) You have suggested further consideration and consultation, both of which I have done.
('87', 139, 1, 3, 201106) I am within an easy distance of Yeravda Central prison, where Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel and Shri Shankarrao Dev were recently transferred from Ahmednagar Fort.
('87', 139, 1, 4, 201265) Almost immediately after their discharge from the jail yesterday they motored to Panchgani and are still with me.
('87', 139, 1, 5, 201379) I have shown them all the necessary papers and they concur with me in what I am writing.
('87', 139, 1, 6, 201468) In the task you have undertaken, of which I fully appreciate the difficulty and delicacy, you certainly need the assistance and goodwill of all the parties.
('87', 139, 1, 7, 201625) The Congress help you naturally cannot have without the Congress being officially represented at your table.
('87', 139, 1, 8, 201734) The first and also perhaps the main purpose of the discharge of the remaining members of the Working Committee will be frustrated unless you secure the presence at your table of the President of the Congress or whomsoever he and his Committee may appoint for the purpose.
('87', 139, 1, 9, 202006) If my supposition is correct, my immediate advice is that you should invite the President of the Congress.
('87', 139, 1, 10, 202113) I expect that the ban on the Congress had been or will be lifted to the extent it still exists.
('87', 139, 2, 11, 202209) I am, Yours sincerely, Enclosure: 1 M. K. GANDHI
('87', 139, 3, 12, 202258) H. E. THE VICEROY THE VICEROY’S HOUSE NEW DELHI Gandhiji’s Correspondence with the Government, 1944 47, pp.

('87', 150, 7, 12, 214072) PANCHGANI, June 18, 1945
('87', 150, 8, 13, 214097) USHA, I have your postcard.
('87', 150, 8, 14, 214125) Your demand is crazy.
('87', 150, 8, 15, 214147) My going to Simla is uncertain and even if I go it will only be for work.
('87', 150, 8, 16, 214221) It is therefore not proper to take children along.
('87', 150, 8, 17, 214272) It is a different thing if there is some occasion.

('87', 150, 8, 20, 214473) You should therefore stand first in that.

('87', 152, 1, 2, 215717) 257. STATEMENT TO THE PRESS
('87', 152, 2, 3, 215745) PANCHGANI, June 18, 1945 This is perhaps an opportune moment to release the text of a letter 1 I wrote to the British Prime Minister during my stay at Panchgani last year.
('87', 152, 2, 4, 215917) The letter was written in the small hours of the night on July 17 at the same time that I wrote my Gujarati note 2 to Qaid e Azam Jinnah and duly posted to be sent through H. E. the Viceroy.
('87', 152, 2, 5, 216108) Unfortunately the letter miscarried.
('87', 152, 2, 6, 216145) Having waited for a long time, on September 10, 1944, during my visit to Bombay for the meeting with Qaid e Azam, I sent a letter 3 of enquiry out of curiosity, for the psychological moment had passed.
('87', 152, 2, 7, 216347) To my surprise, the Private Secretary to the Viceroy wrote in return on September 13 that the letter in question was not received by him.
('87', 152, 2, 8, 216485) As I attached importance to that letter, I sent 4 him a copy of the missing letter on September 17, 1944, repeating the request that it might be sent to the Prime Minister.
('87', 152, 2, 9, 216658) My letter of July 17 to Mr. Churchill, in my estimation, was of a sacred character not meant for the public eye, but I could contemplate an occasion or time when it might call for publication without losing the sacred character.
('87', 152, 2, 10, 216887) I, therefore, requested the Viceroy on December 3, 1944, 5 to enquire from the Prime Minister whether I had his permission to publish it in case of need.
('87', 152, 2, 11, 217041) He replied through his Secretary that thePrime Minister agreed to the publication of my letter subject to the fact that it was duly acknowledged.
('87', 152, 2, 12, 217187) The following is the text of the letter:
('87', 152, 3, 13, 217228) ‘DILKHUSHA’, PANCHGANI, July 17, 1944 DEAR PRIME MINISTER,
('87', 152, 4, 14, 217287) You are reported to have a desire to crush the simple “Naked Fakir” as you are said to have described me.
('87', 152, 4, 15, 217393) I have been long trying to be a “Fakir”
('87', 152, 5, 16, 217433) 1 Vide “Letter to Winston Churchill”, 17 7 1944 and “Letter to M.A. Jinnah”, 17 7 1944. 2 ibid 3 Vide “Letter to Viceroy”, 10 9 1944. and “Letter to Sir Evan M. Jenkins”, 17 9 1944. 4 ibid 5 ibid
('87', 153, 0, 1, 217629) 154 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 153, 1, 2, 217671) and that naked—a more difficult task.
('87', 153, 1, 3, 217709) I, therefore, regard the expression as a compliment though unintended.
('87', 153, 1, 4, 217780) I approach you then as such and ask you to trust and use me for the sake of your people and mine and through them those of the world.
('87', 153, 1, 5, 217914) Your sincere friend, M. K. GANDHI The Bombay Chronicle, 19 6 1948
('87', 153, 2, 6, 217980) 258. INTERVIEW TO THE PRESS
('87', 153, 3, 7, 218008) PANCHGANI, June 18, 1945
('87', 153, 4, 8, 218033) QUESTION: What did you mean when you said that the Desai Formula 1 had no such colouring as the Viceroy’s would seem to have, and how do you think that the Desai Formula would help to solve the communal tangle?
('87', 153, 5, 9, 218244) ANSWER: Bhulabhai’s proposals have no colouring of caste.
('87', 153, 5, 10, 218302) There is the 50 per cent basis as between two political bodies.
('87', 153, 5, 11, 218366) If Bhulabhai’s proposals are the same as the Viceroy’s, then I am greatly mistaken.
('87', 153, 5, 12, 218450) I did not read the proposals in that light.
('87', 153, 5, 13, 218494) According to that Formula, if the Congress chose, it could appoint 50 per cent of any community, non Hindus, caste Hindus and non caste Hindus.
('87', 153, 5, 14, 218638) If the Congress is obliged to choose only caste Hindus or even casteless Hindus then it ceases to be Indian National Congress.
('87', 153, 6, 15, 218765) Asked if he was satisfied with the clarification offered by the Viceroy 2 and the Secretary of State 3 about the question of independence, he said that it was a question for the Working Committee to answer.
('87', 153, 6, 16, 218972) He had his own opinion but he did not wish to anticipate or influence the Working Committee by speaking to the public.
('87', 153, 7, 17, 219091) Q. What is your opinion about Lord Wavell’s personal efforts in solving the political deadlock?
('87', 153, 8, 18, 219187) A. No one will know unless Lord Wavell chooses to write himself as to what part he has played in this connection.
('87', 153, 9, 19, 219301) Q. What do you think about the omission of the Hindu Mahasabha?
('87', 153, 10, 20, 219365) A. I have not thought over it, but as you prompt me I begin to think.
('87', 153, 10, 21, 219435) I do not know whether it is the method of putting the Congress
('87', 153, 11, 22, 219498) 1 Vide Appendix “Desai Liaqat pact”.
('87', 153, 11, 23, 219535) 2 Vide Appendices “Telegram from Lord Wavell”, 16 6 1945 and “Telegram from Lord Wavell”, 18 6 1945. 3 Vide Appendix VII.
('87', 154, 0, 1, 219657) VOL. 87 : 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 155
('87', 154, 1, 2, 219700) in the place of the Hindu Mahasabha and treating it as a sectional or a Hindu body and if it is that, which I hope it is not, the Congress will be one to avoid the whole show.
('87', 154, 1, 3, 219876) But there is another construction also to be put upon that omission, namely, that the British Government wants to avoid the conference being based on religious distinction and, therefore, for examining the proposal they have invited political representatives only.
('87', 154, 1, 4, 220141) Against this favourable assumption has undoubtedly to be put the parity between Muslims and caste Hindus.
('87', 154, 1, 5, 220247) But I have publicly announced 1 that I believed that this mistake, however grave, is one of ignorance.
('87', 154, 1, 6, 220350) If my assumption is right, the mistake would be corrected.
('87', 154, 1, 7, 220409) Thinking along the same lines I account for the omission of the Muslim Majlis or the Jamiat ul Ulema and similar bodies.
('87', 154, 1, 8, 220530) I must not also omit to mention that the composition of the conference is a very great advance upon all similar bodies, for, in all previous conferences convened by the British Government, members have been nominated by the Government principally.
('87', 154, 1, 9, 220778) This time the members of the conference are under no obligation to the Government for their nomination and they need not vote or speak merely to placate the Government.
('87', 154, 1, 10, 220947) The Congress Premiers, for instance, are under obligation only to the Congress as those belonging to the Muslim League are answerable only to the League.
('87', 154, 1, 11, 221101) So far as I can recall there has been no such conference before.
('87', 154, 2, 12, 221166) Q. Why do you think the Maulana was omitted in the first instance?
('87', 154, 3, 13, 221233) A. Because the Viceroy thought that I represented the Congress and the people had given him cause to think so.
('87', 154, 3, 14, 221344) But I must say the moment I pointed 2 out the mistake he saw it at once and rectified it.
('87', 154, 4, 15, 221434) The Bombay Chronicle, 19 6 1945
('87', 154, 5, 16, 221466) 1 Vide “Statement to the Press”, 15 6 1945. 2Vide “Telegram to Privte Secretary to Viceroy”, 14 6 1945 and “Telegram to Lord Wavell”, 15 6 1945.
('87', 155, 0, 1, 221611) 156 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 155, 1, 2, 221653) 259. SPEECH AT PRAYER MEETING, PANCHGANI
('87', 155, 2, 3, 221694) June 18, 1945
('87', 155, 3, 4, 221708) Mahatma Gandhi addressing a prayer gathering on the eve of his departure from here said he had planned to stay at Panchgani till the end of the month but man proposes and God disposes.
('87', 155, 4, 5, 221893) He thanked Principal Batha of the Parsi Girls’ High School for allowing the use of the school hall for holding prayer meetings and the girl students who sweetly chanted prayers from the scriptures in the evenings.
('87', 155, 5, 6, 222107) To him the hall had become a prayer house where he found peace every evening and got over the mental fatigue of the day’s work.
('87', 155, 5, 7, 222235) He had nothing to give them in return except his blessings.
('87', 155, 6, 8, 222295) They should know, he continued, that he was going away for the same purpose for which he had come up to the hills.
('87', 155, 6, 9, 222410) That purpose was the winning of India’s independence.
('87', 155, 6, 10, 222464) If he wanted to live for 125 years, or if he died that very moment, or if he went to the hills for recouping his health, it was the same thing to him so long as his very breath was dedicated to that aim.
('87', 155, 7, 11, 222668) His conception of swaraj was not mere political independence, He wanted to see dharmaraj—establishment of the Kingdom of Heaven on earth—the reign of truth and non violence in every walk of life.
('87', 155, 7, 12, 222864) That alone was independence to the starved masses of this vast country.
('87', 155, 8, 13, 222936) He hoped that those who attended his prayers did not come there for the sake of fun.
('87', 155, 8, 14, 223021) They came to call the name of God so as to be able to do His work.
('87', 155, 8, 15, 223088) To work for the independence of his hope was God’s work.
('87', 155, 9, 16, 223145) To remain in slavery was beneath the dignity of man.
('87', 155, 9, 17, 223198) A slave who was conscious of his state and yet did not strive to break his chains was lower than the beast.
('87', 155, 9, 18, 223306) He who prayed from his heart could never accept slavery as his lot.
('87', 155, 10, 19, 223374) Everyone said that this time at last the chance had come for bringing India’s independence nearer.
('87', 155, 10, 20, 223473) He was a trusting man by temperament and he took statements at their face value.
('87', 155, 10, 21, 223554) Nevertheless, they should repose their faith in prayer more than in a man’s work.
('87', 155, 10, 22, 223636) Let them also know that we were all slaves of our passions.
('87', 155, 10, 23, 223696) If we conquered them, we could easily overcome the slavery under foreigners or our own conquerors.
('87', 155, 10, 24, 223795) The Bombay Chronicle, 20 6 1945
('87', 156, 0, 1, 223827) VOL. 87: 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 157
('87', 156, 1, 2, 223869) 260. INTERVIEW TO P. RAMCHANDRA RAO
('87', 156, 2, 3, 223905) PANCHGANI, [Before June 19, 1945] 1
('87', 156, 3, 4, 223941) QUESTION: Is there a “Gandhian Plan”, as Prof.
('87', 156, 3, 5, 223988) Agrawal 2 will have it, apart from the Gandhian programme?
('87', 156, 3, 6, 224047) A plan necessarily involves a time schedule within which to attain definite objectives.
('87', 156, 3, 7, 224135) You have yourself formulated no such plan?
('87', 156, 4, 8, 224178) ANSWER: For me there is neither a Gandhian plan nor Gandhian programme.
('87', 156, 4, 9, 224250) But it would be too pedantic for me to object to a friend’s use of the word “Gandhian”.
('87', 156, 4, 10, 224338) Your objection to the word “plan” is technically valid.
('87', 156, 4, 11, 224394) But I am inclined to say there is no substance in the objection.
('87', 156, 5, 12, 224459) The basis of the Gandhian programme is decentralization.
('87', 156, 5, 13, 224516) But the core of planning is centralization.
('87', 156, 5, 14, 224560) Can planning and Gandhism go together?
('87', 156, 5, 15, 224599) I must dissent from the view that the core of planning is centralization.
('87', 156, 5, 16, 224673) Why should not decentralization lend itself to planning as well as centralization?
('87', 156, 6, 17, 224756) Economic planning, says Prof.
('87', 156, 6, 18, 224786) Agrawal, necessitates the least amount of State control.
('87', 156, 6, 19, 224843) Yet the plan he unfolds by no means envisages a Government which will govern least because the emphasis throughout is on State action—“the responsibility of the State is very great”.
('87', 156, 6, 20, 225026) Necessarily, communications, public health, education, trade and commerce, banking and currency, etc., must be State controlled.
('87', 156, 6, 21, 225155) And the plan clearly supports the nationalization of key and basic large scale industries.
('87', 156, 6, 22, 225246) How do these incompatible ideas fit in?
('87', 156, 6, 23, 225286) I detect no incompatibility in the idea of decentralizing, to the greatest extent possible, all industries and crafts, economically profitable in the villages of India, and centralizing or nationalizing the key and vital large industries required for India considered as a whole.
('87', 156, 6, 24, 225566) Agrawal has taken illustrations from the present.
('87', 156, 6, 25, 225616) When we have independence cum predominance of village industries in the place of city industries as at present, those who live to see that, as I hope youand I will, will face another and much healthier atmosphere and we shall see clearly what Prof.
('87', 156, 6, 26, 225865) Agrawal and we see today only darkly.
('87', 156, 6, 27, 225903) Today everything is controlled by a foreign State.
('87', 156, 6, 28, 225954) Tomorrow the State will be controlled by the people (a very vital change in itself,) and if
('87', 156, 7, 29, 226046) 1 Gandhiji left Panchgani on June 19; vide the preceding item.
('87', 156, 7, 30, 226109) 2 Shriman Narayan; his “Gandhian Plan of economic Development for Free India” was published in 1944.
('87', 157, 0, 1, 226210) 158 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 157, 1, 2, 226252) Agrawal’s plan (pardon the word) fructifies, then it is obvious that the State control, though it appears to be big, will in reality be least.
('87', 157, 1, 3, 226395) Just project in your mind’s eye 700,000 villages of India dominating the centre with its few towns required in the interests of the villages.
('87', 157, 2, 4, 226537) The Gandhian programme is essentially a resuscitation of village communities, ensuring the maximum utilization of human power.
('87', 157, 2, 5, 226664) It is an evolutionary process.
('87', 157, 2, 6, 226695) Is it not opposed to a definitive State planning, unless, of course, cottage industrialization is content to be complementary to nationalization of industries which the problems of a post war India may make imperative ?
('87', 157, 2, 7, 226915) You have correctly described the programme standing in my name.
('87', 157, 2, 8, 226979) You have lifted the term nationalization from its present setting and then put a perplexing question.
('87', 157, 2, 9, 227081) I suggest your correcting yourself and examining the contents of the term in its new village setting.
('87', 157, 2, 10, 227183) The ideal is too comprehensive for our modernized mind.
('87', 157, 2, 11, 227239) Mine may be all a day dream never destined to be realized.
('87', 157, 2, 12, 227298) But that would be merely begging the question.
('87', 157, 2, 13, 227345) We see that in a single generation we have the so called impossible of yesterday become the possible of today.
('87', 157, 3, 14, 227456) You have recently declaimed 1 against the big interests who speak loud against the Government and give the lie by their support of it for the crumbs that fall to them.
('87', 157, 3, 15, 227624) It is answered that Congress itself has not been averse to befriend these big interests who exploit the Congress for their ends.
('87', 157, 3, 16, 227753) Can you not stop such exploitation?
('87', 157, 3, 17, 227789) The Congress has never been, and I hope never will be, averse to the big interests so long as it hopes to convert them to national use instead of being itself converted by them in the process.
('87', 157, 3, 18, 227982) My very declamation referred to by you shows that the big interests have to be on the right line, if they are to subserve the interests of the masses in the end.
('87', 157, 3, 19, 228144) Today they are relatively serving the foreign ruler whilst they themselves merely get the crumbs from his table.
('87', 157, 3, 20, 228257) It is unfortunate.
('87', 157, 3, 21, 228276) But all will never think and be alike.
('87', 157, 3, 22, 228315) In non violence, there is mutual conversion instead of coercion.
('87', 157, 4, 23, 228380) The Hindu, 23 6 1945
('87', 157, 5, 24, 228401) 1Vide “Statement to the Press”, 6 5 1945.
('87', 158, 0, 1, 228443) VOL. 87: 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 159

('87', 161, 6, 9, 232011) 268. LETTER TO VILAS KATJU
('87', 161, 7, 10, 232038) BOMBAY, June 21, 1945
('87', 161, 8, 11, 232060) VILAS, I have your letter.
('87', 161, 8, 12, 232087) I cannot congratulate you on your Devanagari writing.
('87', 161, 8, 13, 232141) You do not write English in such a bad hand, do you?
('87', 161, 8, 14, 232194) It is our mother tongue that is to blame, I suppose.
('87', 161, 8, 15, 232247) I am returning your letter in order to teach you and show you how untidy and how clumsy it is.

('87', 162, 3, 9, 232964) It is another matter that I may change it out of consider ation for somebody, but then it will not express what I feel.
('87', 162, 3, 10, 233084) In the first place, the term ‘minorities’ includes, along with the Muslims, all the accepted minorities.
('87', 162, 3, 11, 233189) This has been my own preo ccupation from childhood.
('87', 162, 3, 12, 233241) And if you are concerned solely about Muslims, I would like to say that sometimes when a Muslim was wanted he was chosen not because he was the best Congressman among Indians but because he was the best Congressman among Mus lims and represented Muslims.
('87', 162, 3, 13, 233496) I should be grieved if you did not know this, because you are a highly experienced man and a journalist.

('87', 168, 2, 3, 240576) [Before June 24, 1945] 1
('87', 168, 3, 4, 240601) 1. The fact that Congress and some of its organizations are still in jail acts as a piece of coercion to compel co operation on part of Congress.
('87', 168, 3, 5, 240747) 2. Principle of Communalism being an evil cannot be extended beyond the life of the interim temporary Govt.
('87', 168, 3, 6, 240855) [and] cannot be used as a precedent for the future and has no application in considering the services.
('87', 168, 3, 7, 240958) Congress represents all parties and the people without distinction of class, caste or creed.
('87', 168, 3, 8, 241051) 3. Number of non Scheduled Hindus should not exceed that of Muslims drawn from all parties including Shias.
('87', 168, 3, 9, 241159) 4. Implication of Provincial Coalitions 5. Recruitment of services and commitments 6. Method of appointment 7. Financial implications of defence 8. Indian army its freedom 9. Indian States Princes and people 10. External Affairs Department 11. Commercial Safeguards.

('87', 169, 1, 2, 241749) 283. LETTER TO ABUL KALAM AZAD
('87', 169, 2, 3, 241780) [After June 24, 1945] 1
('87', 169, 3, 4, 241804) DEAR MAULANA SAHEB, It was by mere chance that Pyarelal happened to see you.
('87', 169, 3, 5, 241881) But what you told him, if his report of the talk is accurate, is startling.
('87', 169, 3, 6, 241957) The Working Committee has not given you the right or the permission to form a cabinet.
('87', 169, 3, 7, 242044) You yourself told me that you could not do it without the Working Committee.
('87', 169, 3, 8, 242121) That is my view too.
('87', 169, 3, 9, 242142) That was why I had said that you should form a small committee with the assistance of the Working Committee, which could be given that right and then act through that committee or the Working Committee itself.
('87', 169, 3, 10, 242352) Since you did not react favourably to either of the proposals, I can only conclude that I do not understand or do not know the stand of the Working Committee in the matter.
('87', 169, 3, 11, 242525) 2 I understand from what Jamnalalji says that you are going to summon the Working Committee anyhow.
('87', 169, 3, 12, 242625) I consider it improper.
('87', 169, 3, 13, 242649) I would not wish you to be guilty of such a grave error at this juncture.
('87', 169, 3, 14, 242723) I do not know what you have done and how you could persuade the Viceroy.
('87', 169, 3, 15, 242796) Even if you have committed yourself it is, in my view, your duty to inform him that a mistake has been committed.
('87', 169, 3, 16, 242910) So much for the matter between you and the Working Committee.
('87', 169, 3, 17, 242972) Another thing I would like to tell you is that in anything you do, you should take with you the Congress who are present and you should put everything in writing.
('87', 169, 3, 18, 243135) The third is a personal matter.
('87', 169, 3, 19, 243167) Ever since I first heard the Viceroy’s proclamation 3, that is, while I was still at Panchgani, I have been shouting that the Congress cannot accept the principle of parity between Muslims and non Harijan Hindus, an organization of Hindus alone.
('87', 169, 3, 20, 243413) Even if I am the only one among crores to do so, I shall refuse to be a party to it.
('87', 169, 3, 21, 243498) I do not care if the negotiations break down on this, for I know and believe that the moment you try to form a national government at the centre in this way you will be laying a wrong
('87', 169, 4, 22, 243682) 1 From the contents it is evident that this was written during Gandhiji’s stay at Simla where he had talks with the Viceroy, Lord Wavell, regarding constitutional negotiations.

('87', 173, 6, 15, 248215) 290. LETTER TO JAWAHARLAL NEHRU
('87', 173, 7, 16, 248247) ‘‘MANOR VILLE’, SIMLA, June 25, 1945
('87', 173, 8, 17, 248284) JAWAHARLAL, There are several names in the Kasturba Memorial Trust.
('87', 173, 8, 18, 248352) When the Trust was formed, I had expressed a desire that your name and Sardar’s should be included.
('87', 173, 8, 19, 248452) All the Trustees were agreeable that the names of you two should be included when you were released.

('87', 184, 0, 1, 262309) VOL. 87: 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 185
('87', 184, 1, 2, 262351) 310. DRAFT OF SPEECH AT PRAYER MEETING, SIMLA 1
('87', 184, 2, 3, 262399) [June 27, 1945] 2
('87', 184, 3, 4, 262417) Addressing the prayer meeting Mahatma Gandhi said that the object of attending prayers was to commune with God and turn the searchlight inwards so that with the help of God they could overcome their weaknesses.
('87', 184, 3, 5, 262628) He believed that one imbibed pure thoughts in the company of the pure.
('87', 184, 3, 6, 262699) Even if there was one pure man in that gathering, the rest would be affected by that one man’s purity.
('87', 184, 3, 7, 262802) The condition was that they came with that intention.
('87', 184, 3, 8, 262856) Otherwise, their coming to the prayers was meaningless.
('87', 184, 3, 9, 262912) He went further and maintained that even if all had their weaknesses but came to the meeting with the intention of removing them, their co operative effort made day to day would quicken the progress of reform.
('87', 184, 3, 10, 263122) For even as co operation was necessary, in the economic or the political field so was co operation much more necessary on the moral plane.
('87', 184, 3, 11, 263261) That was the meaning of the prayer meetings he had been holding since his return to India.
('87', 184, 4, 12, 263352) Therefore, he appealed to them to sit absolutely quiet, with closed eyes, so as to shut themselves off from outward thoughts for a few minutes at least.
('87', 184, 4, 13, 263505) This co operative prayer needed no fuss, no advertisement.
('87', 184, 4, 14, 263564) They must be free from hypocrisy.
('87', 184, 5, 15, 263598) From the original: C.W. 4208. Courtesy: Amrit Kaur.
('87', 184, 5, 16, 263650) Also G.N. 7844

('87', 185, 3, 4, 264109) DEAR FRIEND, Some hangings—an aftermath of the disturbances of 1942— are impending.
('87', 185, 3, 5, 264193) I have some cases given to me by Dr. Rajendra Prasad of the Working Committee.
('87', 185, 3, 6, 264272) The Chimur cases you perhaps know.
('87', 185, 3, 7, 264307) I do not quite know how the last stages of the conference are shaping.
('87', 185, 3, 8, 264378) Be that as it may, I suggest that all such hangings be commuted to life sentences without further public appeal or agitation and whether judicial proceedings are going on or not.
('87', 185, 3, 9, 264557) If you think that this is beyond you, may I suggest that these be postponed so as to be dealt with by the national government that is coming into being?

('87', 187, 1, 2, 267210) 317. LETTER TO G. B. PANT
('87', 187, 2, 3, 267236) ‘MANOR VILLE’, June 29, 1945
('87', 187, 3, 4, 267265) BHAI GOVIND BALLABH PANT 1, Yesterday I came to know that you had gone to Rajaji’s house and there all of a sudden felt giddy.
('87', 187, 3, 5, 267392) I was given to understand that in any case you were not feeling too fit and that partly I was responsible for it.
('87', 187, 3, 6, 267506) That should not be so.
('87', 187, 3, 7, 267529) I am very firm in my view and I should be so.
('87', 187, 3, 8, 267575) There may be occasions when you do not agree with my views.
('87', 187, 3, 9, 267635) So what?
('87', 187, 3, 10, 267644) All of us, if we want to serve the country, should have our own opinions.
('87', 187, 3, 11, 267718) Only then can the country forge ahead and a way be shown to the people.
('87', 187, 3, 12, 267790) I firmly believe that you should not work at the cost of your health.
('87', 187, 3, 13, 267860) Stop worrying and do not feel unhappy that you do not agree with my views.
('87', 187, 3, 14, 267935) The more I think the more convinced I become that if the Working Committee tries to select as many Hindus as there areMuslims then the communal poison will spread throughout the country and we will never be able to win freedom.
('87', 187, 3, 15, 268163) What is the harm if the Congress is reduced from a majority to a minority?
('87', 187, 3, 16, 268238) Must we do a wrong thing to maintain our majority?
('87', 187, 3, 17, 268289) Will not the Congress become a communal organization by selecting as many Hindus as there are Muslims?
('87', 187, 3, 18, 268392) If the Congress takes the fewest of Hindus, and as many as possible from the other communities, the communal poison will be removed and it will succeed in bringing freedom nearer.
('87', 187, 3, 19, 268572) I quite see that now the first step towards freedom has to be taken through the Government.
('87', 187, 3, 20, 268664) The course should be straight so far as we are concerned.
('87', 187, 3, 21, 268722) If people do not accept this, then let the reins of Government be passed to those whom the people approve.
('87', 187, 3, 22, 268829) Everything will be all right even if there are only a few straightforward persons.
('87', 187, 3, 23, 268912) This is my opinion and I can never give it up.
('87', 187, 4, 24, 268959) 1 (1887 1961); Advocate, Allahabad High Court; in 1928, during demons tration against Simon Commission at Lucknow, suffered lathi blows from which he never fully recovered; was leader of Swaraj Party in United Provinces Legislative Council, 1923 30, and U. P. Premier, 1937 39; Chief Minister of Uttar Pradesh, 1946 55; Home Minister, Government of India, 1955 61.
('87', 188, 0, 1, 269324) VOL. 87: 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 189
('87', 188, 1, 2, 269366) You have taken for granted that the Working Committee at Bombay has accepted the principle of parity.
('87', 188, 1, 3, 269468) I have rejected it.
('87', 188, 1, 4, 269488) Please get well.
('87', 188, 2, 5, 269505) Blessings from BAPU

('87', 188, 4, 8, 269587) 318. INTERVIEW TO PRESTON GROVER
('87', 188, 5, 9, 269620) SIMLA, June 29, 1945
('87', 188, 6, 10, 269641) In reply to my questions, Gandhiji said be was feeling well and that the 7,000 foot altitude of Simla had not affected him so far, although he was watchful that he did not overstrain his heart.
('87', 188, 7, 11, 269835) Answering an initial request that he should give a report on the negotiations as they stood at the moment, Mahatma Gandhi said: I wish I could, but I am here only as an adviser.
('87', 188, 7, 12, 270013) I have, for many years, been advising the Congress.
('87', 188, 7, 13, 270065) But now, I have constituted myself as an adviser both to the Congress and to the Viceroy, too, and through him of the British people.
('87', 188, 7, 14, 270199) You see, that makes my position exceptionally delicate.
('87', 188, 7, 15, 270255) The only information I have is what my colleagues bring when they come to me.
('87', 188, 7, 16, 270333) Frankly speaking, I do not know in what position the conference exactly is today.
('87', 188, 7, 17, 270415) It has never been my habit to cry out of curiosity.
('87', 188, 8, 18, 270467) It was suggested that the Congress representatives should keep him advised almost hourly, to which he replied: They do, and they do not.
('87', 188, 8, 19, 270604) Unless the Viceroy wants my advice, I would know nothing as to what is happening at that end.
('87', 188, 8, 20, 270698) But, if things go on smoothly, he does not need my advice.
('87', 188, 8, 21, 270757) On our side too, while they do come to me, it need not be from day to day or hour to hour.
('87', 188, 8, 22, 270848) While, therefore, I cannot tell you what exactly the situation in the conference is, I can only share with you my hope and prayer that things will come right both for India and Great Britain.
('87', 188, 8, 23, 271040) I say for both, because I do not know that, even if a settlement is pulled through, it will be on right lines.
('87', 188, 8, 24, 271151) But I give you a tip.
('87', 188, 8, 25, 271173) I was not joking when I made a statement 1
('87', 188, 9, 26, 271216) some time back in answer to Sir Feroz Khan Noon at San Francisco,
('87', 188, 10, 27, 271282) 1 Vide “Statement to the press”, 4 5 1945.
('87', 189, 0, 1, 271325) 190 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 189, 1, 2, 271367) that Pandit Jawaharlal Nehru is my heir.
('87', 189, 1, 3, 271408) He has got ability, knowledge and close touch with the public here and can interpret India’s mind.
('87', 189, 1, 4, 271507) I have already, as I wrote 1 to Lord Linlithgow, taken him as my guide in international affairs.
('87', 189, 1, 5, 271604) He can interpret India’s mind to the outside world as no one else can.
('87', 189, 1, 6, 271675) This much I can say, that Congress can never become sectional organization.
('87', 189, 1, 7, 271751) Not that there are not communal minded people in it, but the Congress can never work communally.
('87', 189, 1, 8, 271848) Therefore, normally speaking, the parity principle should be distasteful to everybody.
('87', 189, 2, 9, 271935) Turning to the composition of the current conference, Gandhiji declared it was “political in its complexion” and not communal.
('87', 189, 2, 10, 272062) This was in direct contradiction to the Muslim League argument that the whole conference was chosen on communal basis.
('87', 189, 2, 11, 272181) If they wanted various groups to be represented communally, they should have invited the Hindu Mahasabha and not the Congress, which has always been, and is now, a purely political body trying to think and act in terms of the whole nation.
('87', 189, 2, 12, 272421) It cannot belie its entire history at this critical moment.
('87', 189, 3, 13, 272481) Asked if an acceptance of invitation to work for an interim government was in the belief that it was a step towards independence, Gandhiji replied: The acceptance of the invitation was a recognition of the fact that it was a step towards independence.
('87', 189, 3, 14, 272733) But this was subjectto explanation and clarification of what was in the Viceroy’s mind.
('87', 189, 3, 15, 272821) It was like sitting on the top of a volcano which might erupt.
('87', 189, 3, 16, 272884) I took that risk.
('87', 189, 4, 17, 272902) Toward the end of the interview, it was suggested that Mr. Jinnah, President of the Muslim League, was reported to be somewhat resentful that Gandhiji had withdrawn from the conference.
('87', 189, 4, 18, 273088) If Mr. Jinnah wants me there, he can take me there.
('87', 189, 4, 19, 273140) We shall both go arm in arm.
('87', 189, 4, 20, 273169) He can help me up the hill and save strain on my heart.
('87', 189, 4, 21, 273225) Such a gesture on Mr. Jinnah’s part would mean that he wants a settlement even in the teeth of the differences and obstacles that face the conference.
('87', 189, 4, 22, 273376) You can tell him that I am quite willing to be taken to the conference by him.
('87', 189, 5, 23, 273455) I suggested that not only Mr. Jinnah, but Lord Wavell, most of India and all observers at the conference looked upon Gandhiji as head of the Congress regardless of the technicality that he was not a member, and that no settlement would be reached
('87', 189, 6, 24, 273702) 1 Vide “Letter to Lord Linlithgow”, 14 8 1942.
('87', 190, 0, 1, 273749) VOL. 87: 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 191
('87', 190, 1, 2, 273791) without his consent.
('87', 190, 1, 3, 273812) Gandhiji replied: That is both right and wrong.
('87', 190, 1, 4, 273860) That impression has been created because generally my advice is accepted.
('87', 190, 1, 5, 273934) But technically and substantially it is wrong.
('87', 190, 1, 6, 273981) The conference is legally representative and, therefore, I can have no place in it.
('87', 190, 2, 7, 274065) To my insistence that his was the controlling voice in the Congress, Gandhiji replied: Not even that.
('87', 190, 2, 8, 274167) They can shunt me out at any time, brush aside my advice.
('87', 190, 2, 9, 274225) If I tried to override them, I might succeed for once.
('87', 190, 2, 10, 274280) But the moment I try to cling to power, I fall, never to rise again.
('87', 190, 2, 11, 274349) That is, not in my temperament.
('87', 190, 3, 12, 274381) The Hindu, 1 7 1945

('87', 194, 4, 8, 279276) 327. INTERVIEW TO ASSOCIATED PRESS OF INDIA
('87', 194, 5, 9, 279320) SIMLA, June 30, 1945
('87', 194, 6, 10, 279341) GANDHIJI: I have registered your claim but have nothing to say.
('87', 194, 6, 11, 279405) I generally don’t speak during day but for your sake I am speaking to you as a special case.
('87', 194, 6, 12, 279498) You have to prompt me.
('87', 194, 7, 13, 279521) CORRESPONDENT: What will be the composition of the interim government if you have your way?
('87', 194, 8, 14, 279613) G. (Laughing) The interim government will consist of top men, irrespective of caste, creed or colour.
('87', 194, 8, 15, 279715) If I became the Viceroy of India, I would startle the world with my list and yet make it acceptable.
('87', 194, 9, 16, 279816) I asked Mahatmaji to explain what he meant by top men, and he amplified his remark by saying that he meant men and women who are fittest to do the work the country needs.
('87', 194, 9, 17, 279987) The Mahatma said: Of course, nobody will take the trouble of appointing me the Viceroy of India nor of electing me as President of the Congress—for I am not even a four anna member of the Congress to be eligible for election—with full authority to appoint the new government.
('87', 194, 10, 18, 280263) Mahatma Gandhi said that he would not hesitate to leave out anyone at present in the Congress, if he felt that better men were available outside who would work in their respective spheres so as to bring full independence at the earliest time possible.
('87', 194, 10, 19, 280515) I next asked:
('87', 194, 11, 20, 280529) In the course of your correspondence with the Viceroy on his proposals, you objected to the term “caste Hindus” in the matter of parity of representation for Hindus and Muslims, adding that if this parity between caste Hindus and Muslims was

('87', 195, 2, 3, 281224) According to the reports, the Congress delegates to the Conference have accepted parity between Hindus other than Scheduled Classes and Muslims.
('87', 195, 2, 4, 281369) Have you any comment to make on this?
('87', 195, 2, 5, 281407) If Congressmen have accepted parity, it cannot be in the sense you imagine.
('87', 195, 2, 6, 281483) I interpret the Viceregal pronouncement 2 to mean that neither community can ask for more representation than the other in the national cabinet.
('87', 195, 2, 7, 281628) Thus Hindus other than the Scheduled Classes can, if they wish, be less but not more than the Muslims.
('87', 195, 3, 8, 281731) Do you approve of the procedure suggested by Lord Wavell yesterday at the leaders’ conference for the selection of the new Executive Council, namely, that all parties should submit separate panels of names to the Viceroy first and that thereafter he would consult Party leaders before making his final selection and place the personnel finally selected by him before the conference for approval?
('87', 195, 3, 9, 282127) The procedure suggested by Lord Wavell is, in my opinion, good inasmuch as the Viceroy does not seek to impose his will on the conference.
('87', 195, 3, 10, 282266) The Viceroy has said in his opening remarks to the delegates that the various elements represented in the conference should regard him, the Viceroy, as their leader.
('87', 195, 3, 11, 282432) It is a good and dignified expression that Lord Wavell has used.
('87', 195, 3, 12, 282497) He thus acts at the conference as its leader and not as the agent of Whitehall.

('87', 198, 6, 12, 286227) 334. DRAFT OF REVISED PHOENIX TRUST DEED
('87', 198, 7, 13, 286268) SIMLA, July 2, 1945 In or about the year 1902, I, Mohandas Karamchand Gandhi, then of Johannesburg, Attorney, bought a piece of property about 100 acres in two lots, popularly known as the Phoenix Settlement, for benevolent purposes.
('87', 198, 7, 14, 286502) Not wishing to have anything in my name as sole owner, I converted it into a trust and had it duly registered at Pietermaritzburg, Natal.
('87', 198, 8, 15, 286640) All the trustees, except Lewis Walter Ritch of Johannesburg, Attorney, and I as settlers’ trustee, have died.
('87', 198, 8, 16, 286750) The settlers under the Trust have all retired from the Phoenix Settlement.
('87', 198, 8, 17, 286825) My son, Manilal Gandhi, together with his wife, Sushila behn Gandhi, and their children have lived on the Settlement and managed the property and the weekly newspaper Indian Opinion, founded by me.
('87', 198, 8, 18, 287023) Now it is my intention to broaden the Trust and appoint new trustees.
('87', 198, 8, 19, 287093) Therefore the conditions of the present Trust shall be: 1. As long as possible to conduct the newspaper, Indian Opinion, in English and Gujarati and other Indian and even African
('87', 198, 9, 20, 287272) 1 Vide “Letter to A.E. Chotabhai”, 4 5 1911 and “The Phoenix Trust Deed”, 14 9 1912.
('87', 199, 0, 1, 287357) 200 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 199, 1, 2, 287399) languages according to felt necessity and convenience including reso urces but never at a loss.
('87', 199, 1, 3, 287495) Any profits made from the newspaper after the deduction of running expenses shall be returned to the Settlement.
('87', 199, 1, 4, 287608) 2. The Press Department may undertake job work and the sale of literature approved by the Trust in the interest of and healthy instructions of the public.
('87', 199, 1, 5, 287763) 3. The Trust may found a public library and school, subject to rules made by the trustees and built from donations given by the public.
('87', 199, 1, 6, 287899) These shall be named after my deceased wife, Kasturba.
('87', 199, 1, 7, 287954) 4. The trustees may also found nature cure establishments and undertake all activities that may educate Indians morally, socially, economically and hygienically.
('87', 199, 1, 8, 288116) 5. All decisions of the trustees shall be by majority.
('87', 199, 1, 9, 288171) For the purposes aforesaid I appoint the following trustees during life or at my discretion: (i) The said Lewis Walter Ritch, (ii) Manilal Mohandas Gandhi, (iii) Parsi Jalbhai Rustomji, (iv) Surendrarai Medh, [and a] (v) [A] Muslim.
('87', 199, 1, 10, 288404) The said Manilal Gandhi shall be the Managing Trustee and, while he is manager of the Trust and editor of Indian Opinion, shall draw not more than one hundred pounds per month with free lodging on the Settlement for himself, his wife and children.
('87', 199, 1, 11, 288652) The said Manilal Gandhi shall maintain proper books of account for the management of the Trust property and the newspaper, Indian Opinion.
('87', 199, 1, 12, 288791) Separate accounts shall be maintained in respect of Indian Opinion and the management of the Trust property.
('87', 199, 1, 13, 288900) The said accounts shall be audited every six months.
('87', 199, 1, 14, 288953) In the event of any of the trustees being dead, resigning or being displaced by me, the remaining trustees may appoint another instead, my consent being considered necessary during my life.
('87', 199, 2, 15, 289143) WITNESS :

('87', 203, 6, 15, 293725) 341. SPEECH AT PRAYER MEETING, SIMLA
('87', 203, 7, 16, 293762) July 2, 1945
('87', 203, 8, 17, 293775) Mahatma Gandhi drew the attention of the people to the new rule of the A. I. S. A. according to which payment for khadi had to be made partly in yarn.
('87', 203, 8, 18, 293926) This rule had come into force from the first of July in Simla.
('87', 203, 8, 19, 293989) People had said to him that Simla Khadi Bhandar sold khadi to all sorts of people who came up for short or long visits.
('87', 203, 8, 20, 294109) Most of them could not spin and the sales of the Bhandar would go down if part payment of the price of khadi in yarn was insisted upon.
('87', 203, 8, 21, 294245) He did not mind such a result, untoward though it would be.
('87', 203, 9, 22, 294305) There was a time, Gandhiji said, when they aimed at promoting the sale of khadi to help the poor to supplement their income.
('87', 203, 9, 23, 294430) But deep thought, especially during his recent incarceration, had convinced him that if khadi was to serve as a means of bringing swaraj, its scope and meaning had to be extended.
('87', 203, 9, 24, 294610) He could not keep a mighty organization like the A. I. S. A. merely for producing and selling khadi for the sake of providing economic relief.
('87', 203, 9, 25, 294753) Any other occupation could be utilized for that purpose.
('87', 203, 9, 26, 294810) If khadi was to bring swaraj through non violence, millions had to spin with the full consciousness of its implication in terms of ahimsa and independence.
('87', 203, 9, 27, 294966) The A. I. S. A. had started by asking for yarn worth only two pice for every rupee worth of khadi sold.
('87', 203, 9, 28, 295070) If he could carry conviction, he would insist upon the full payment being made in yarn.
('87', 203, 9, 29, 295158) If they loved freedom, they should not find it burdensome to do that much—those who did not wish to be free had no business to
('87', 203, 10, 30, 295285) 1 The reference is to Jawaharlal Nehru; ‘jawahar’, literally, means jewel.
('87', 204, 0, 1, 295360) VOL. 87: 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 205
('87', 204, 1, 2, 295402) come to the prayers.
('87', 204, 1, 3, 295423) A man of prayer could never accept slavery as his lot.
('87', 204, 2, 4, 295478) If all had taken to spinning in the way he wanted it, Gandhiji said, they would have had swaraj without any further effort.
('87', 204, 2, 5, 295602) He would not have had to come up to Simla.
('87', 204, 2, 6, 295645) But society was made of all kinds of people.
('87', 204, 2, 7, 295690) Therefore he had to come in common with others for the conference to see whether it was possible through the conference [to find a] way to further the progress towards independence.
('87', 204, 3, 8, 295872) As for the yarn to be given in exchange for khadi it should be either spun by the individual concerned or by members of his family.
('87', 204, 3, 9, 296004) The farthest the A. I. S. A. could go was to let them take yarn spun by their servants whom they should treat as members of the family.
('87', 204, 3, 10, 296140) Yarn bought from the black market could not serve the purpose in view.
('87', 204, 3, 11, 296211) Also, if Bhandars began to sell yarn to prospective purchasers of khadi, that would defeat the very purpose for which the new rule was being enforced.
('87', 204, 3, 12, 296362) The Hindu, 4 7 1945
('87', 204, 4, 13, 296382) 342. LETTER TO LORD SAMUEL
('87', 204, 5, 14, 296409) [After July 2, 1945] 1
('87', 204, 6, 15, 296432) DEAR LORD SAMUEL 2, I have your letter of 2nd July.
('87', 204, 6, 16, 296484) I am sorry that you are still unconvinced.
('87', 204, 6, 17, 296527) The ground of your objections seems to be that whilst the Congress may sincerely wish to embrace all parties and is trying to do so, it has not yet been able to achieve it and that its ultimate achievement is problematical, while the taking of the delivery is to be immediate and certain.
('87', 204, 6, 18, 296816) This objection again overlooks the very relevant fact to which I have twice drawn your attention, namely, that the Congress through its president has invited the Government to transfer full power to the League and ask it to form a truly national government, in which it would have the loyal co operation of the Congress.
('87', 204, 6, 19, 297137) This offer was reiterated at Simla.
('87', 204, 6, 20, 297173) But I am sorry to have to say it was again turned down.
('87', 204, 6, 21, 297229) I still adhere to my statement that “there cannot be Swaraj without an understanding with the Muslims.” My contention is and has been that the presence of the third party is the greatest stumbling block in the way of this understanding.
('87', 204, 6, 22, 297466) So long as one community in the country enjoys the power of vetoing all political progress there can be no reasonable settlement.
('87', 204, 6, 23, 297596) In India this anomalous power is
('87', 204, 7, 24, 297629) 1 This was in reply to the addressee’s letter dated July 2, 1945. 2 Herbert Louis Samuel, Liberal leader
('87', 205, 0, 1, 297734) 206 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 205, 1, 2, 297776) assured to the League by the British Government which supererogates to itself the right of arbitrating and holding the balance of power between the various communities.
('87', 205, 1, 3, 297945) In the absence of an agreed solution, a just solution through impartial arbitration is held to be the only feasible alternative in civilized society, but in India the absence of an agreed solution is strangely held to be a justification for retention of power by an alien Government over a nation of 400 millions !
('87', 205, 1, 4, 298260) ‘Quit India’ can be the only reply to such a claim.
('87', 205, 1, 5, 298312) It seemsstrange that you should see in this cry a manifestation of totalitarian spirit instead of the anguished despair of an enslaved people to be free from totalitarian foreign rule which has in the past demonstrably sabotaged all their efforts to achieve unity in order to be free and spurned their united and unanimous demands for political advance.
('87', 205, 2, 6, 298666) From a copy: Pyarelal Papers.
('87', 205, 2, 7, 298696) Nehru Memorial Museum and Library.
('87', 205, 2, 8, 298731) Courtesy: Beladevi Nayyar and Dr. Sushila Nayyar

('87', 214, 7, 21, 310253) I take it that you will order commutation of sentence or stay till the proposed Executive is able to deal with it.
('87', 214, 8, 22, 310368) Yours sincerely, M. K. GANDHI, H. E. THE VICEROY SIMLA Gandhiji’s Correspondence with the Government, 1944 47 p.

('87', 216, 1, 2, 311851) 367. LETTER TO SURESH CHANDRA DAS
('87', 216, 2, 3, 311885) SIMLA, July 9, 1945

('87', 229, 0, 1, 325855) 230 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 229, 1, 2, 325897) 398. SPEECH AT PRAYER MEETING, SIMLA 1
('87', 229, 2, 3, 325936) July 12, 1945
('87', 229, 3, 4, 325950) Mahatma Gandhi referred to the serious inconvenience experienced by his host due to unruly crowds.
('87', 229, 3, 5, 326049) Some of them had invaded the house opposite to ‘Manor Ville’, which belonged to Rajkumari Amrit Kaur’s brother and had smashed flower pots and damaged the railing of the verandah.
('87', 229, 3, 6, 326229) When checked by the Rani Saheba they had been rude to her.
('87', 229, 3, 7, 326288) All this hurt him deeply.
('87', 229, 3, 8, 326314) He would have liked to run away.
('87', 229, 3, 9, 326347) But after all, wherever he went the crowds would go with him.
('87', 229, 3, 10, 326409) He could not run away from them.
('87', 229, 3, 11, 326442) He was their servant and he lived to serve them.
('87', 229, 4, 12, 326491) Some came to the prayers, Gandhiji said, simply to have his darshan.
('87', 229, 4, 13, 326560) He had told them often enough that he was not a mahatma.
('87', 229, 4, 14, 326617) He was just one of them, an ordinary human being.
('87', 229, 4, 15, 326667) He must, however, confess that he called the name of God with every breath of his life and in everything that he did he proceeded with God as hiswitness.
('87', 229, 4, 16, 326821) But that should not make him a mahatma.
('87', 229, 4, 17, 326861) Every human being should act as he claimed he did.
('87', 229, 4, 18, 326912) That was what distinguished man from beast.
('87', 229, 4, 19, 326956) Those who came to the prayers should at least have decent manners.
('87', 229, 4, 20, 327023) Even the soldiers in arms observed discipline and behaved in an orderly fashion.
('87', 229, 4, 21, 327104) These who came to pray should have better manners, not worse.
('87', 229, 4, 22, 327166) The object of coming to prayers was to praise God and for doing that, purity of thought was a necessary pre requisite.
('87', 229, 4, 23, 327285) If they could not control their minds, they should pray to God that he should enable them to have pure thoughts at least during prayers.
('87', 229, 4, 24, 327422) Gradually and with practice they would be able to control them at all times.
('87', 229, 4, 25, 327499) The Hindu, 14 7 1945

('87', 232, 1, 2, 329242) 404. INTERVIEW TO SAILENDRA NATH CHATTOPADHYAYA 1
('87', 232, 2, 3, 329292) [On or before July 15, 1945] 2
('87', 232, 3, 4, 329323) Prayer is even more essential for the well being of the soul than is food for the maintenance of the body.
('87', 232, 3, 5, 329430) It becomes necessary to give up food on occasions in order to benefit the body.
('87', 232, 3, 6, 329510) But prayer may never be abandoned.
('87', 232, 3, 7, 329545) If we provide food for the body which is perishable, then, surely, it is our primary duty to provide food for the soul which is imperishable and such sustenance is found in prayer.
('87', 232, 3, 8, 329726) The real meaning of prayer is devoted worship.
('87', 232, 4, 9, 329773) S. N. CHATTOPADHYAYA: Why do you never look at your face in a looking glass ?
('87', 232, 5, 10, 329851) GANDHIJI: Since everyone who meets me sees my face, what need is there for me to employ a mirror?
('87', 232, 6, 11, 329949) Why do you not use a thick mattress?
('87', 232, 6, 12, 329986) I do all I can to merge myself into the poor millions of India.
('87', 232, 7, 13, 330050) Why do you always travel third class on the railway?
('87', 232, 7, 14, 330103) The answer to this is embodied in the above.
('87', 232, 8, 15, 330148) Why not take salt and spices with your food?
('87', 232, 8, 16, 330193) Why should I take anything which is not essential for my bodily needs?
('87', 232, 9, 17, 330264) The Hindu, 17 7 1945

('87', 233, 6, 8, 330911) 407. LETTER TO LORD WAVELL
('87', 233, 7, 9, 330938) ‘MANOR VILLE’, SIMLA WEST, July 15, 1945
('87', 233, 8, 10, 330979) DEAR FRIEND, I thank you for your note of the 14th instant.
('87', 233, 8, 11, 331039) It gladdens me to think that you have appreciated my effort to advance the common cause.
('87', 233, 8, 12, 331128) As you perhaps know, I have arranged to leave here tomorrow.
('87', 233, 8, 13, 331189) A special from Kalka will carry me to Wardha by the kind courtesy of the authorities concerned.
('87', 233, 8, 14, 331285) It grieves me to think that the conference which began so happily and so hopefully should have ended in apparent failure—due exactly, as it would seem, to the same cause as before.
('87', 233, 8, 15, 331466) This time you have taken the blame on your own shoulders.
('87', 233, 8, 16, 331524) 1 But the world will think otherwise.
('87', 233, 8, 17, 331562) India certainly does.
('87', 233, 8, 18, 331584) I must not hide from you the suspicion that the deeper cause is perhaps the reluctance of the official world to part with power, which the passing of the virtual control into the hands of their erstwhile prisoners would have meant.
('87', 233, 8, 19, 331816) Be that as it may, what a pity that the moral height which the British, if not even the Allied Powers, would have occupied by the suc cess of the conference cannot be theirs, at any rate, for the time being.
('87', 233, 8, 20, 332024) I must not close this without a reminder about the Bihar case.
('87', 233, 8, 21, 332087) Your passing remark that it was one of ordinary dacoity, calling for the heavy hand of law, disturbed me.
('87', 233, 8, 22, 332193) This was not such
('87', 233, 9, 23, 332211) 1 The Viceroy had announced the failure of the conference at its final sitting on July 14.
('87', 234, 0, 1, 332302) VOL. 87: 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 235
('87', 234, 1, 2, 332344) dacoity.
('87', 234, 1, 3, 332353) The young man who is under sentence of death is no professional dacoit.
('87', 234, 1, 4, 332425) He is a misled Congressman under twenty five years (I think.) with a young wife of twenty years.
('87', 234, 1, 5, 332522) I do hope that all such death sentences will be commuted to life sentences.
('87', 234, 1, 6, 332598) It seems tobe the least demand of humanity, if not also of high politics.
('87', 234, 2, 7, 332672) Yours sincerely, M. K. GANDHI H. E. THE VICEROY SIMLA

('87', 235, 1, 2, 333752) 409. LETTER TO SHANTA PATEL July 16, 1945
('87', 235, 2, 3, 333794) SHANTA, I got your letter yesterday.
('87', 235, 2, 4, 333831) I am writing this after the morning prayer.
('87', 235, 2, 5, 333875) Address your reply at Sevagram.
('87', 235, 2, 6, 333907) You have remained as crazy after becoming a communist and a mother as you were as a child.
('87', 235, 2, 7, 333998) Which Ashram has boycotted you?
('87', 235, 2, 8, 334030) Where is the Ashram?
('87', 235, 2, 9, 334051) Who has boycotted you?
('87', 235, 2, 10, 334074) Many communists have stayed with me.
('87', 235, 2, 11, 334111) In the same way you also can stay.
('87', 235, 2, 12, 334146) You know that Jayanti 1 had stayed with me.
('87', 235, 2, 13, 334190) You should know that I have received many complaints, but I have not acted on any of them.
('87', 235, 2, 14, 334281) I am in correspondence with the Secr etary 2. He had asked me for my permission to publish the letters and I have granted it.
('87', 235, 2, 15, 334407) Whether he has published them or not I do not know.
('87', 235, 2, 16, 334459) The Working Committee 3 has taken no step.
('87', 235, 2, 17, 334502) There has been no time to consider the matter.
('87', 235, 2, 18, 334549) If Jawaharlalji goes against them, all the communists will have to sit up and think.
('87', 235, 2, 19, 334634) For he has a soft corner for the Party but he will not tolerate anything unworthy.
('87', 235, 2, 20, 334717) I myself have not been able to come to a final decision.
('87', 235, 2, 21, 334774) I have received quite a few complaints.
('87', 235, 2, 22, 334814) I have sent them to the Head office.
('87', 235, 2, 23, 334851) You have written your letter without thinking.
('87', 235, 2, 24, 334898) If you calm down and think before writing, you can help the communist cause.
('87', 235, 2, 25, 334975) You must learn to distinguish between communism and commu nists.
('87', 235, 2, 26, 335040) Besides, Marx stands for one thing, Lenin for another and Stalin for a third.
('87', 235, 2, 27, 335118) The followers of the last are again divided into two groups.
('87', 235, 2, 28, 335179) Gandhi is one thing, Gandhism is another and Gandhi ites are a third thing.
('87', 235, 2, 29, 335255) There are always, and will remain, such differences.
('87', 235, 2, 30, 335308) Immature people may identify themselves with one or the other group.
('87', 235, 3, 31, 335377) Blessings from BAPU From a photostat of the Gujarati: G.N. 6639. Also C.W. 4287. Courtesy: Shanta Patel
