('87', 237, 0, 1, 337467) 238 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 237, 1, 2, 337509) 412. “A THOUGHT THE DAY” 1
('87', 237, 2, 3, 337536) April 25, 1945 A man does not become a satyagrahi by styling himself as such.
('87', 237, 2, 4, 337614) The observance of pure truth alone makes him a satyagrahi.
('87', 237, 2, 5, 337673) April 26, 1945 Is only that unclean which appears to the eye as unclean?
('87', 237, 2, 6, 337746) If there is even a little dirt on what is white, we feel annoyed; but the black may have any amount of dirt on it and we care not at all!
('87', 237, 2, 7, 337884) April 27, 1945 We consider the black impure and the white pure.
('87', 237, 2, 8, 337948) But black, in its natural setting, is as much a virtue; as white, out of place, is a vice.
('87', 237, 2, 9, 338039) April 28, 1945 How strange that one who claims not to fear death fears it the most, and seeks every means to avoid it!
('87', 237, 2, 10, 338158) April 29, 1945 A son’s obeisance to his parents is undoubtedly a form of prayer.
('87', 237, 2, 11, 338239) What homage, then, must we pay to Him who is the Eternal Father of us all?
('87', 237, 2, 12, 338314) Prayer may not be interpreted here in a narrow sense.
('87', 237, 2, 13, 338368) April 30, 1945 “A Thought for Today,’, published in today’s The Times of India, appealed to me.
('87', 237, 2, 14, 338464) Its purport is: “Believe in Truth, think Truth and live Truth.
('87', 237, 2, 15, 338527) Howsoever triumphant untruth may seem to be, it can never prevail against Truth.”
('87', 237, 3, 16, 338609) 1 Originally written in Hindi, these ‘thoughts, were translated and published under this title by Anand T. Hingorani, who explains in the Preface that after the death of his wife, Vidya, on July 20, 1943, during his eight week stay in Sevagram from September 30, 1944, Gandhiji would greet him “every morning, after the prayer .
('87', 237, 3, 17, 338938) speak words of sympathy and solace, and .
('87', 237, 3, 18, 338980) write down something .
('87', 237, 3, 19, 339003) to meditate upon.
('87', 237, 3, 20, 339021) From October 13, 1944, onwards he wrote continuously for a fortnight, and then off and on.
('87', 237, 3, 21, 339112) .” Before leaving Sevagram for nature cure treatment at Bhimavaram, Hingorani had requested Gandhiji to write something for him daily, which Gandhiji began to do from November 20, 1944, vide In June 1946, when Hingorani sought Gandhiji’s permission to publish the ‘thoughts, in a book form, Gandhiji remarked: “What is there about them that you are so keen on publishing them?
('87', 237, 3, 22, 339489) If, however, you wish to publish them, do so after my death.
('87', 237, 3, 23, 339550) Such writings are generally never published during the lifetime of their authors.
('87', 237, 3, 24, 339632) Who knows, I may not be able to live up to what I have written !
('87', 237, 3, 25, 339697) But if I live up to it till the last breath of my life, then alone will it be worthwhile to publish these thoughts.” Gandhiji, however, discontinued the practice by the end of 1946, as he put it, “for the sake of my Noakhali mission, I renounced practically everything .
('87', 237, 3, 26, 339968) gave up the Ashram, all my companions and even writing for the Harijan.
('87', 238, 0, 1, 340040) VOL. 87: 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 239
('87', 238, 1, 2, 340082) May 1, 1945 Where there is hypocrisy, even if there is something good along with it, do not go there even for the sake of picking up that good only.
('87', 238, 1, 3, 340231) If you do, it could be co operation with evil which must not be offered: May 2, 1945 Just as we throw away milk if there is poison in it, so must we reject any good which has got the poison of hypocrisy mixed with it.
('87', 238, 1, 4, 340449) May 3, 1945 Says Confucius: “In a well ordered State, progress is not measured in terms of wealth.
('87', 238, 1, 5, 340548) The purity of the People and their leaders alone constitutes the true wealth of the nation.” May 4, 1945 Minds are of two kinds: one kind elevates, the other debases.
('87', 238, 1, 6, 340715) Let us constantly reflect over this and learn to distinguish one from the other.
('87', 238, 1, 7, 340796) May 5, 1945 Just as only others can see a man’s back while he himself cannot, we too cannot see our own errors.
('87', 238, 1, 8, 340908) May 6, 1945 Is not death, in every case, a release from too much suffering?
('87', 238, 1, 9, 340984) If so, why lament when it comes?
('87', 238, 1, 10, 341017) May 7, 1945 Life is likened to a rose; because life, too, is full of thorns.
('87', 238, 1, 11, 341094) May 8, 1945 Verily, there should be only one fear—the fear of doing something mean or untrue.
('87', 238, 1, 12, 341188) May 9, 1945 Slipshod work is like half baked bread, fit only to be thrown away.
('87', 238, 1, 13, 341268) May 10, 1945 Why is it that man is afraid of speaking and practising truth, not untruth?
('87', 238, 1, 14, 341357) May 11, 1945 There is an English saying, which is true, that “cowards die many times before their death”.
('87', 238, 1, 15, 341463) As I have often said, death really means deliverance from pain and suffering.
('87', 238, 1, 16, 341541) Fear serves only to accentuate suffering and makes one’s condition pitiable.

('87', 239, 1, 2, 341660) May 12, 1945 By whatever name God be called, if there be godly attributes, we must surely bow to Him.
('87', 239, 1, 3, 341762) May 13, 1945 Then, what should God be like?
('87', 239, 1, 4, 341806) Passionless and Formless, He should be a repository of all attributes and yet be wholly without attributes.

('87', 239, 1, 6, 341958) This is purely a question of grammar.
('87', 239, 1, 7, 341996) The God of our conception, being formless, is neither male nor female.

('87', 240, 0, 1, 343148) VOL. 87: 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 241
('87', 240, 1, 2, 343190) The train is not moved by the steam engine; the aeroplane is not flown by the motor; nor does man live by the mere mechanical functioning of his heart.
('87', 240, 1, 3, 343342) May 24, 1945 “Sweet are the fruits of equanimity”—the truth of this is experienced every moment.
('87', 240, 1, 4, 343439) May 25, 1945 There is a vast difference between obstinacy and steadfastness.
('87', 240, 1, 5, 343516) To seek to foist one’s view on others is obstinacy; whereas steadfastness is that whereby we voluntarily impose something on ourselves and which results in bringing others round to the acceptance of our view of their own free will.

('87', 245, 1, 2, 351677) 413. MESSAGE TO STUDENTS 1
('87', 245, 2, 3, 351704) AGRA, July 17, 1945 [GANDHIJI:] Study and work for the country’s freedom.
('87', 245, 2, 4, 351778) This is my message to the students of India.
('87', 245, 3, 5, 351823) Gandhiji said that he realized the despondency of the student community on the failure of the Simla Conference 2 and the danger of ill feeling that might creep in between Hindu and Muslim students.
('87', 245, 3, 6, 352021) Hopes must not be lost.
('87', 245, 4, 7, 352045) Gandhiji stressed the need of unity among students and said it was deplorable that a number of parties existed and things had reached such a stage that the police were sometimes required to intervene.
('87', 245, 4, 8, 352246) He wished that students of every creed, colour and caste worked as a united body for the common cause.
('87', 245, 4, 9, 352349) He advised the people [to refrain] from indulging in mutual recriminations.
('87', 245, 5, 10, 352425) Asked if the Simla Conference failed on the issue of one seat given to a non Leaguer, Mahatma Gandhi refuted the contention.
('87', 245, 5, 11, 352550) He said that he would publicize his views regarding this problem at the earliest opportunity.
('87', 245, 5, 12, 352644) The Hindustan Times, 19 7 1945
('87', 245, 6, 13, 352675) 1 On his way to Wardha after the Simla Conference, Gandhiji addressed the crowd assembled at the Agra Cantt.
('87', 245, 6, 14, 352784) station where the special carrying him arrived at 3.40 p.
('87', 245, 6, 15, 352842) About a dozen local Communists, who had collected on the platform, were initially disallowed by the authorities but they were allowed on the assurance from them to remain peaceful.
('87', 245, 6, 16, 353023) 2 The Simla Conference was convened by the Viceroy, Lord Wavell, and was attended by leaders of the various parties, prominent among whom were Abul Kalam Azad, Bhulabhai Desai, M. A. Jinnah, Dr. Khan Saheb, Liaquat Ali Khan, Sir Henry Richardson, Rao Bahadur Shiv Raj and Master Tara Singh.
('87', 245, 6, 17, 353314) Gandhiji did not attend the Conference but he remained in Simla so as to be available for consultation.
('87', 245, 6, 18, 353418) The Conference, started on June 25, was adjourned on June 29 to enable the parties to send the lists of the names for the proposed Executive Council.
('87', 245, 6, 19, 353568) However, when it met again on July 14 Lord Wavell announced its failure.

('87', 248, 2, 7, 358362) 415. STATEMENT TO THE PRESS
('87', 248, 3, 8, 358390) SEVAGRAM, July 18, 1945 The public will not like to know, as I have not liked, the fact that I had to travel from Kalka to Wardha like a thief.
('87', 248, 3, 9, 358534) I could do so only by the courtesy of the authorities.
('87', 248, 3, 10, 358589) Why should I have to escape the embarrassing affection of the public?
('87', 248, 3, 11, 358659) When I travelled by the Frontier Mail from Bombay to Kalka 2, at every stopping station it was a wild demonstration.
('87', 248, 3, 12, 358776) Accidents, even fatal, were escaped by miracle.
('87', 248, 3, 13, 358824) Those who were with me in the compartment had a rough time and two wakeful nights.
('87', 248, 3, 14, 358907) Singly I might not have been able to cope with the din, noise and hustle of the crowd.
('87', 248, 3, 15, 358994) Of course this was not the first time that I had to face such wild demonstrations, nor am I unaware that other leaders have to go through such ordeals, but the fact is that each year makes me less fit for them.
('87', 248, 3, 16, 359205) My ears cannot stand the noise.
('87', 248, 3, 17, 359237) I can do no work among demonstrators and cannot make Harijan collections in such circumstances.
('87', 248, 3, 18, 359333) What is most painful is the fact that this wildness is no prelude to swaraj, it is no sign of non violence.
('87', 248, 3, 19, 359441) Crowds there should be to greet the leaders, but they should be peaceful, dignified and completely disciplined.
('87', 248, 3, 20, 359553) I have seen ordinary soldiers in thousands observing perfect silence whether on the march or at rest.
('87', 248, 3, 21, 359655) Our crowds, if they are non violent soldiers of swaraj, should be more disciplined than ordinary soldiers.
('87', 248, 3, 22, 359762) Will leaders of volunteers learn a lesson from my train journey from Kalka to Wardha and ensure perfectly peaceful demonstrations at stations and elsewhere in all circumstances and not only or especially for me?
('87', 248, 3, 23, 359974) The Hindu, 20 7 1945
('87', 248, 4, 24, 359995) 1 For the Congress President’s letter to the Viceroy regarding this, vide Appendix “Abul Kalam Azad’s letter to Lord Wavell”, 15 7 1945. 2 On June 22 and 23

('87', 257, 8, 17, 372469) What is and what is not my responsibility and to what extent is a matter of argument.

('87', 266, 6, 10, 384786) 453. LETTER TO SHYAMLAL
('87', 266, 7, 11, 384810) July 23, 1945
('87', 266, 8, 12, 384824) BHAI SHYAMLAL 2, There are two ways of serving the Harijans.
('87', 266, 8, 13, 384885) First, by raising them through education, etc., and secondly by rooting out untouch ability from among the caste Hindus.
('87', 266, 8, 14, 385006) The first course always bears fruit and it is desirable to pursue it however little one can.
('87', 266, 8, 15, 385099) Simple ‘Eradication of Untouchability’ does not serve our purpose.
('87', 266, 8, 16, 385166) There fore, ‘Harijan Sevak Sangh’ is a more appropriate expression.
('87', 266, 8, 17, 385234) It is true that so far very little work has been done among the savarnas.
('87', 266, 8, 18, 385308) The reasons are obvious.
('87', 266, 8, 19, 385333) We lack self sacrifice.
('87', 266, 8, 20, 385357) Everyone, to some extent, can do the work of spreading education.
('87', 266, 8, 21, 385423) But everyone cannot work among the savarnas for the removal of Untouchability.
('87', 266, 8, 22, 385502) Untouchability cannot be removed by delivering speeches.
('87', 266, 8, 23, 385559) It will be removed only by the power of our self sacrifice.
('87', 266, 8, 24, 385619) In such self sacrifice, fasting has an important place.
('87', 266, 8, 25, 385675) The fasts should be backed by discretion.
('87', 266, 8, 26, 385717) Something could be done if competent Shastris is sue public statements.
('87', 266, 8, 27, 385789) What Barveji 3 says is not right.
('87', 266, 8, 28, 385823) There can be no separate village for Harijans because they are an integral part of society and yet outside it.
('87', 266, 8, 29, 385934) They need wells, schools, etc., and if they are properly built and

('87', 267, 1, 4, 386427) It is a need of Hinduism.

('87', 282, 1, 2, 407245) 483. INTERVIEW TO “THE HINDU”
('87', 282, 2, 3, 407275) WARDHAGANJ, July 28, 1945
('87', 282, 3, 4, 407301) QUESTION: According to Dr. Pattabhi, the Desai Liaqat Formula contemplated formation of a new government first, to be followed by the release of the members of the Congress Working Committee.
('87', 282, 3, 5, 407493) This aspect of the Formula had been interpreted by some people as “bypassing the Congress” and by some others as “stabbing the Congress in the back”.
('87', 282, 4, 6, 407643) You have stated in your statement issued from Panchgani that you blessed the Formula as you thought it provided a basis for communal settlement.
('87', 282, 4, 7, 407788) It is generally believed that you were consulted at every stage of the agreement.
('87', 282, 4, 8, 407870) Is theinterpretation put on the agreement that it bypassed the Congress correct?
('87', 282, 5, 9, 407951) ANSWER: I consider the question has been addressed to a wrong person.
('87', 282, 5, 10, 408021) Parties to the Formula are the best persons to say what it meant.
('87', 282, 5, 11, 408087) Then what you put into Dr. Pattabhi’s mouth, he may repudiate.
('87', 282, 5, 12, 408150) I, therefore, suggest to all reporters at all times, but most specially at this time, to be precise and accurate in what they say.
('87', 282, 5, 13, 408281) There never was the slightest intention on the part of Advocate Bhulabhai Desai, on whose behalf alone I can speak, “of stabbing the Congress in the back” or making an attempt to “bypass” the Con gress.
('87', 282, 5, 14, 408484) He, himself made politically by the Congress, could never be guilty of any such intention, and, for me, I should be committing suicide if I could be a party to any such attempt.
('87', 282, 5, 15, 408662) I can say this much for Advocate Bhulabhai Desai that the only intention he had was that of honourably resolving the deadlock and thereby serving the Congress.
('87', 282, 5, 16, 408822) It would be wrong to say that I was consulted “at every stage” but it would be strictly correct to say that Advocate Bhulabhai Desai saw me more than once about the ‘Pact’.
('87', 282, 6, 17, 408995) Asked whether the release of the members of the Working Committee formed part of the agreement, whether it was agreed between the parties that the Muslim League alone should nominate the Muslim members of the new government and whether in view of so many statements and counter statements on the subject it would not be desirable to release the Formula for publication, Gandhiji said: I think, in the foregoing, I have said as much as I could, consis tently with the fact that the ‘Pact’ has not seen the light of day.
('87', 282, 6, 18, 409514) I wish that the parties had agreed to release it for publication.
('87', 282, 7, 19, 409580) The Hindu, 30 7 1945
('87', 283, 0, 1, 409601) 284 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 283, 1, 2, 409643) 484. LETTER TO SUDHIR GHOSH
('87', 283, 2, 3, 409671) July 28, 1945
('87', 283, 3, 4, 409685) MY DEAR SUDHIR, I have your good letter.
('87', 283, 3, 5, 409726) A man is sincere in the sense that he is not knowingly dishonest.
('87', 283, 3, 6, 409792) But if he makes up his mind hastily and will not deign to take the trouble to study accurately facts of each case, he is in fact untruthful without knowing that he is so.
('87', 283, 3, 7, 409963) Such is the case with perhaps millions of Hindus.
('87', 283, 3, 8, 410013) They sincerely believe that untouchability is a part of the divine plan.
('87', 283, 3, 9, 410086) But they hug a provable untruth.
('87', 283, 3, 10, 410119) Of course I will see Mr. Casey1 first, if I succeed in coming to Bengal which I want to do as early as the rains permit.
('87', 283, 3, 11, 410240) I have the pamphlets.
('87', 283, 3, 12, 410262) My blessings to you both 2.

('87', 295, 0, 1, 425788) 296 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 295, 1, 2, 425830) 511. WHY KHADI FOR YARN AND NOT FOR MONEY?
('87', 295, 2, 3, 425873) July 1945 Sjt.
('87', 295, 2, 4, 425888) Bharatan Kumarappa writes to me from his tours: People are asking what has Gandhiji done.
('87', 295, 2, 5, 425978) He will kill khadi by insisting on yarn being given in exchange for it.
('87', 295, 2, 6, 426050) What are we, who because of his teachings have vowed to put on only khadi, to do?
('87', 295, 2, 7, 426132) We do not know how to spin neither do we want to learn it.
('87', 295, 2, 8, 426191) Are we to go without khadi?
('87', 295, 2, 9, 426219) This rule regarding yarn only shows Gandhiji’s obduracy.
('87', 295, 2, 10, 426276) Bharatan Kumarappa’s letter is in English.
('87', 295, 2, 11, 426319) I have given its substance here.
('87', 295, 2, 12, 426352) People will not find any obduracy in my demand if only they understood that non violent swaraj depends on every drawing out of the yarn.
('87', 295, 2, 13, 426489) On the contrary they will then find absorbing interest in it.
('87', 295, 2, 14, 426551) Those who see only obduracy in it do not know how non violence works.
('87', 295, 2, 15, 426621) Since my return to India I have been crying myself hoarse that if we want to attain independence through non violence spinning should be an essential part of our activity.
('87', 295, 2, 16, 426793) The late Maulana Mohamed Ali used to say that the charkha was our rifle and the spindles of yarn our bullets; we shall attain swaraj only through.
('87', 295, 2, 17, 426940) these bullets.
('87', 295, 2, 18, 426955) This is as true today as when it was said.
('87', 295, 2, 19, 426998) My experience tells me that if khadi is to become universal, both in cities and in villages, it should be made available only in exchange of yarn.
('87', 295, 2, 20, 427145) Today one anna’s worth of yarn in the rupee is demanded.
('87', 295, 2, 21, 427202) But this is only the beginning.
('87', 295, 2, 22, 427234) When people have understood and learnt how to spin, then khadi will be given only in full exchange for yarn spun.
('87', 295, 2, 23, 427348) I hope that as days go by everyone will himself insist on buying khadi only in exchange of yarn.
('87', 295, 2, 24, 427445) If this does not happen and if they give yarn grudgingly swaraj through non violence is impossible.
('87', 295, 2, 25, 427545) Surely some effort has to be made for swaraj.
('87', 295, 2, 26, 427591) It cannot be had by mere begging.
('87', 295, 2, 27, 427625) A certain kind of freedom can of course be obtained on the strength of the rifle, but it will not be real swaraj and I for one am not interested in it.
('87', 295, 2, 28, 427777) The very idea of obtaining swaraj through the rifle makes my head reel and a mountain of difficulties appears before my eyes.
('87', 295, 2, 29, 427903) Thisarticle is not meant for those who would obtain swaraj through the rifle.
('87', 295, 2, 30, 427981) Why should they wear khadi at all?
('87', 295, 2, 31, 428016) From their point of view khadi can be proved to be quite a useless thing.
('87', 295, 2, 32, 428090) Readers of this article
('87', 296, 0, 1, 428114) VOL. 87: 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 297
('87', 296, 1, 2, 428156) should realize that if khadi is to be produced by villagers, not for their own use but for sale in cities, and if crores of villagers themselves are to use only mill cloth, then khadi will be of very little avail.
('87', 296, 1, 3, 428370) How can we rest content if khadi merely puts a few coppers into the pockets of the poor?
('87', 296, 1, 4, 428459) A doubt is raised that this new rule will kill the khadi which is now being produced by the poor and will make the wearing of khadi spun by themselves a matter of fashion only for a few select city dwellers.
('87', 296, 1, 5, 428667) This idea, however, displays ignorance.
('87', 296, 1, 6, 428707) The masses do not eat for fashion but in order that they may live.
('87', 296, 1, 7, 428774) Similarly they do not wear clothes for fashion, but for protection.
('87', 296, 1, 8, 428842) Therefore the charkha, like the oven, should find a place in every house and every able bodied person should spin.
('87', 296, 1, 9, 428957) Then all can wear khadi and obtain swaraj.
('87', 296, 1, 10, 429000) Able bodied persons should spin also for the crippled and the weak.
('87', 296, 1, 11, 429068) If games clubs demanding both energy and money can be run, as they are, why cannot swaraj clubs or charkha clubs be run where people can make slivers, spin and get khadi in exchange of yarn?
('87', 296, 1, 12, 429259) The truth is that where there is no will, unfavour able arguments present themselves and where there is a will, the will itself discovers favourable arguments.
('87', 296, 1, 13, 429419) If the will is strong nobody will give up the charkha even as nobody leaves games.
('87', 296, 1, 14, 429502) If the will can be found for games, can it not be found also for swaraj?
('87', 296, 1, 15, 429575) A powerful argument advanced against the system of exchang ing khadi for yarn is that if city people produce their own yarn the khadi produced by the poor will vanish and the little relief that has till now been given to them through khadi will stop, and the hope of seeing villagers clad in khadi produced by themselves will remain only a dream.
('87', 296, 1, 16, 429922) Supposing city people give up wearing khadi out of laziness or anger and villagers give up spinning and weaving for want of demand, what great loss is it to the country?
('87', 296, 1, 17, 430092) The poor people will take to other occupations in the place of khadi and will somehow make their living.
('87', 296, 1, 18, 430197) Such people will not be found in crores but only in lakhs as at present.
('87', 296, 1, 19, 430270) Those who are engaged in bidi making earn four times what is possible through spinning, or even more.
('87', 296, 1, 20, 430372) Many of the mill labourers have become rich.
('87', 296, 1, 21, 430417) This means that those who are starving today will starve still further till they die, and the few of them who can earn well will ride roughshod over the rest.
('87', 296, 1, 22, 430576) If more mills are increased and the number of cities is increased it will not make Indiaprosperous.
('87', 296, 1, 23, 430676) On the other hand it will make crores die of starvation and of the many diseases produced by starvation.
('87', 296, 1, 24, 430781) If city people are pleased with such a spectacle I have nothing to say.
('87', 296, 1, 25, 430853) Then it
('87', 297, 0, 1, 430861) 298 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 297, 1, 2, 430903) will be the reign of violence, not of non violence and truth, and I will admit that in that case khadi will have no place, it can have no place.
('87', 297, 1, 3, 431048) Then military training will be compulsory whether we like it or not.
('87', 297, 1, 4, 431117) But what I am talking about relates to the crores of the starving people.
('87', 297, 1, 5, 431191) If they are to live, and live well, the charkha will have to be central and spinning undertaken voluntarily also by those who do not need to spin.
('87', 297, 1, 6, 431338) The weapons of non violence must not be adopted by people because they have no other alternative.
('87', 297, 1, 7, 431436) Therefore to my mind the rule of yarn for khadi which has been introduced has to exist and increase in its application.
('87', 297, 1, 8, 431556) Exactly for the same reason, if all the khadi bhandars have to be closed down and khadi wearers give up khadi I will regard it as a triumph of truth, because then I shall understand that people had no belief in non violence and that if they wore khadi they did it out of ignorance and thereby merely deceived themselves into thinking that by wearing khadi they would somehow get swaraj.
('87', 297, 1, 9, 431943) Why should I thus allow people to deceive themselves when I know that such khadi will not bring swaraj and that it will be discarded after swaraj is obtained?
('87', 297, 1, 10, 432102) In that case the prophecy of the late Chintamani 1
('87', 297, 2, 11, 432153) will come true that on Gandhi’s death people will laugh at khadi and also at him and will burn his body with the charkhas they may have in their houses.
('87', 297, 2, 12, 432306) If hand spun yarn cannot represent non violence, why should I not retrieve my error while I am still alive and save the wood used in the charkhas?
('87', 297, 2, 13, 432453) But I do not regard that prophecy as true.
('87', 297, 2, 14, 432496) People have understood that the crores of India cannot obtain freedom through violence.
('87', 297, 2, 15, 432584) India occupies or will soon occupy a great place in the world.
('87', 297, 2, 16, 432647) That will be possible only through non violence.
('87', 297, 2, 17, 432696) If the crores of our people want to demonstrate the workability of non violence they can do it only by making the charkha central.
('87', 297, 2, 18, 432827) As the desire for freedom is strong amongst city folks it is their duty to understand this and to take to spinning and khadi wearing in order to obtain non violent swaraj.
('87', 297, 3, 19, 432999) Gram Udyog Patrika, Vol. I, pp.
('87', 297, 4, 20, 433031) 1 C. Y. Chintamani; President of the National Liberal Federation, 1920 and 1931; Editor of The Leader, 1909 20 and Chief Editor, 1926 41; Minister of Education in U. P., 1921 23

('87', 299, 0, 1, 434189) 300 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 299, 1, 2, 434231) 514. LETTER TO PURUSHOTTAM K. JERAJANI
('87', 299, 2, 3, 434270) SEVAGRAM, August 1, 1945
('87', 299, 3, 4, 434295) BHAI KAKUBHAI, I have your letter.
('87', 299, 3, 5, 434330) Kanu has given me the details in writing, but I shall not go into them.
('87', 299, 3, 6, 434402) All this misunderstanding arose because I could not explain myself fully.
('87', 299, 3, 7, 434476) “God has tied me with a cotton thread.
('87', 299, 3, 8, 434515) Whichever way he pulls me I am His.
('87', 299, 3, 9, 434551) I am pierced by the dagger of love.” This is from a famous bhajan of Mirabai.
('87', 299, 3, 10, 434629) Swaraj hangs by that thread; it does not snap because the weight is that of love.
('87', 299, 3, 11, 434711) The languages of India are full of allegories featuring yarn.
('87', 299, 3, 12, 434773) Narandas has conceived of a yarn bank.
('87', 299, 3, 13, 434812) If such a bank is organized well, it will ultimately beat the money banks.
('87', 299, 3, 14, 434887) Narandas is a supreme devotee of khadi.
('87', 299, 3, 15, 434927) None among us can beat him in his tapascharya.
('87', 299, 3, 16, 434974) He has no other work.
('87', 299, 3, 17, 434996) I am a witness to the work he has done for the charkha.
('87', 299, 3, 18, 435052) I am a lover of his work.
('87', 299, 3, 19, 435078) He has added immensely to the importance of Rentia Baras 1. It is not a work of Kathiawaris alone and this time Kathiawaris alone are not to do it.
('87', 299, 3, 20, 435226) In this scheme the Charkha Sangh was to play a major role and its benefit would have been also quite large.
('87', 299, 3, 21, 435334) Kanu after finishing his work in Bombay was to proceed further.
('87', 299, 3, 22, 435398) Collection of funds was Of secondary importance.
('87', 299, 3, 23, 435447) Yarn was the main thing.
('87', 299, 3, 24, 435472) The Charkha Sangh had to collect only the yarn delivered at its door and send the acknowledgement to Narandas’s bank.

('87', 305, 5, 13, 445631) I have naturally no record of those talks nor did I authorize publication of the talks.
('87', 305, 5, 14, 445719) I have however contemporaneous evidence of what I had in mind on 7th of August, 1942. My draft instructions 5 were circulated among Members of the Working Committee on 8th August.
('87', 305, 5, 15, 445899) They were to be considered on 9th August, but before they could be considered, Members of the Working Committee and I were arrested.
('87', 305, 5, 16, 446032) Hence no authorized instructions were or could be issued.
('87', 305, 5, 17, 446090) I had no opportunity to function in terms of the A. I. G. C.

('87', 311, 6, 8, 453639) 535. LETTER TO MADHAVDAS G. KAPADIA
('87', 311, 7, 9, 453675) August 4, 1945
('87', 311, 8, 10, 453690) MADHAVDAS, Dr. Krishnavarma has sent all the reports about you.
('87', 311, 8, 11, 453754) Kunvarji 1
('87', 311, 9, 12, 453765) has also written a postcard.
('87', 311, 9, 13, 453794) Dr. Krishnavarma has no interest in keeping you.
('87', 311, 9, 14, 453843) He has kept you only for my sake.
('87', 311, 9, 15, 453877) He kept Sailen also in the same way.
('87', 311, 9, 16, 453914) Your good lies in remaining underDr. Krishnavarma’s treatment and following his instructions.
('87', 311, 9, 17, 454008) I think I know Dr. Krishnavarma’s virtues and failings.
('87', 311, 9, 18, 454064) For his failings he will be answerable to God.
('87', 311, 9, 19, 454111) I see and cling to his virtues.
('87', 311, 9, 20, 454143) Many allegations are made against him.
('87', 311, 9, 21, 454182) Who is immune to them?
('87', 311, 9, 22, 454205) I do not care for such allegations.
('87', 311, 9, 23, 454241) I have seen with my own eyes how he looked after Ba.
('87', 311, 9, 24, 454294) I think he had seen Ba’s virtues and became a great admirer of hers.
('87', 311, 9, 25, 454363) The knowledge that you are Ba’s brother prompts him to keep you and look after you.
('87', 311, 9, 26, 454447) You need not worry about how much you will have to pay him.
('87', 311, 9, 27, 454507) The doctor has told me that he does not want a single pie, but I have decided that, if you agree, I shall pay him what I think proper from out of your own possessions.
('87', 311, 9, 28, 454675) I have discussed this with Manilal too.
('87', 311, 9, 29, 454715) But if you are not willing to pay a single pie, well, a lot of money has already been spent over you and this will be some more.
('87', 311, 9, 30, 454844) It will be to the good if you get well and can live a normal life.
('87', 311, 9, 31, 454911) However, Ba’s last words to me about you were: “You have done what you could for Madhavdas, I did what I could as his sister, and made you do what you could for him.
('87', 311, 9, 32, 455077) Now you need not do anything for
('87', 311, 10, 33, 455110) 1 Kunvarji Parekh, son in law of Harilal Gandhi
('87', 312, 0, 1, 455158) VOL. 87: 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 313
('87', 312, 1, 2, 455200) him.” This is what she said about you and Harilal.
('87', 312, 1, 3, 455251) I know that these words proceeded from her anger, but also from her love.
('87', 312, 1, 4, 455325) I have not, therefore, obeyed those words literally.
('87', 312, 1, 5, 455378) Now do what you wish, with God, whom you believe you worship every day, as witness.
('87', 312, 1, 6, 455462) Of one thing you may be sure, that I will not be able to keep you in the Ashram, nor can I cure you.
('87', 312, 1, 7, 455563) And remember also that no relation will be able to accommodate you.
('87', 312, 1, 8, 455631) Society is so constituted that even though a person may wish to do something he is not able to do it, cannot do it.
('87', 312, 1, 9, 455747) Ultimately, everyone has to turn to God, and only what He does or permits is possible.
('87', 312, 1, 10, 455834) If you can think, then after reading this letter stay where you are.
('87', 312, 1, 11, 455903) If you cannot think, then also, do not do anything in a hurry but stay there.
('87', 312, 1, 12, 455981) May God bless you.
('87', 312, 2, 13, 456000) Blessings from BAPU

('87', 312, 5, 16, 456092) August 4, 1945
('87', 312, 6, 17, 456107) BHAI KRISHNAVARMA, Please read the enclosed letter and then pass it on to Mama.
('87', 312, 6, 18, 456187) I read your whole letter yesterday, till then I was not able fully to go through it.
('87', 312, 6, 19, 456272) I agree with what you say.
('87', 312, 6, 20, 456299) I have given Mama some idea of you in my letter to him.

('87', 312, 6, 23, 456514) I had noticed that also when you were here.
('87', 312, 6, 24, 456558) I presume you are doing the same there.
('87', 312, 6, 25, 456598) Kanti Mashruwala is an admirer of yours.
('87', 312, 6, 26, 456639) Manilal had been there.
('87', 312, 6, 27, 456663) He is not an admirer of you but he is wise.
('87', 312, 6, 28, 456707) He has seen something of the world.
('87', 312, 6, 29, 456743) He recognizes your qualities.
('87', 312, 6, 30, 456773) He believes that you are no doubt good at heart but he also believes that you do not observe the rules of cleanliness nor make others do so.
('87', 312, 6, 31, 456914) I only know your goodness and therefore wish that your shortcomings may disappear.
('87', 312, 6, 32, 456997) I know that I have served my own interest in sending Mama to you and I still want to keep him there.
('87', 312, 6, 33, 457098) He will be in a very bad plight if he goes away from there.
('87', 312, 6, 34, 457158) I cannot keep him in the Ashram, as it will be against the spirit of the Ashram.
('87', 312, 6, 35, 457239) I do not think he can stay anywhere else.
('87', 312, 6, 36, 457281) Whatever has to be done, you alone can do.
('87', 312, 6, 37, 457324) As you have started a hospital it certainly is your duty.
('87', 312, 6, 38, 457382) Follow nature cure
('87', 313, 0, 1, 457401) 314 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 313, 1, 2, 457443) methods at the hospital.

('87', 313, 1, 4, 457538) There are too many mosquitoes there.
('87', 313, 1, 5, 457575) Just because you are taking work from the poor women you should not put up with their indifferent performance.
('87', 313, 1, 6, 457686) As a doctor and a householder it is your duty to teach them cleanliness.

('87', 314, 4, 11, 460097) 538. STATEMENT TO THE PRESS
('87', 314, 5, 12, 460125) WARDHA, August 4, 1945 Several Congressmen have asked me questions relating to the Congress programme.
('87', 314, 5, 13, 460228) Cablegrams too have been received from London and other places.
('87', 314, 5, 14, 460292) I am sorry I have not been able to acknowledge them.
('87', 314, 5, 15, 460345) The reason, however, is and should be obvious.
('87', 314, 5, 16, 460392) In the absence of the Maulana Saheb and other members of the Working Committee, it is true I took upon myself the responsibility to give such advice as I was capable of giving in regard to Congress matters.
('87', 314, 5, 17, 460599) Now that the Working Committee is out, I can only give advice through the Maulana Saheb and the Working Committee.
('87', 314, 5, 18, 460714) My advice, independently given, may be in conflict with their opinion and it may embarrass them and even put them or me in a wrong position and, what is more, may confuse the public mind.
('87', 314, 5, 19, 460902) Therefore, I should warn all here and outside India against making any reference to me on such questions as are properly for the President and the Working Com mittee to advise upon.
('87', 314, 6, 20, 461084) The Hindu, 6 8 1945
('87', 315, 0, 1, 461104) 316 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 315, 1, 2, 461146) 539. INTERVIEW TO “THE HINDU”
('87', 315, 2, 3, 461176) August 4, 1945 I said then and I repeat now that my offer to Mr. Jinnah was not in the nature of a bargain.
('87', 315, 2, 4, 461284) 1 It was my settled conviction though originally derived from Rajaji 2. I am not in the habit of deriving anything from anybody, however great he is, unless I can appropriate and assimilate it for myself.
('87', 315, 2, 5, 461489) Therefore even if Rajaji went back on that Formula, I shall stick to it so long as I retain my sanity.
('87', 315, 2, 6, 461592) I hold it to be substantial and also directly derivable from the Congress Resolutions and immediately from the Resolution of August 8, 1942. Only I have given it concrete shape.
('87', 315, 3, 7, 461770) The Hindu, 6 8 1945

('87', 317, 1, 2, 463496) 543. LETTER TO KANTILAL GANDHI
('87', 317, 2, 3, 463527) August 5, 1945
('87', 317, 3, 4, 463542) KANTI 1, Both of you should learn non attachment from the service of Harilal.
('87', 317, 3, 5, 463620) Through non attachment devotion to someone can be transformed into devotion to God.
('87', 317, 3, 6, 463704) If such devotion is not linked with devotion to God, it becomes infatuation and assumes a dangerous form.
('87', 317, 3, 7, 463810) You two have spared no effort in the service of Harilal.
('87', 317, 3, 8, 463867) I had felt all along that Harilal would ultimately act as he had always done.
('87', 317, 3, 9, 463945) But let not this worry you in the least.
('87', 317, 3, 10, 463986) You should be thankful if even the last rites fell to your lot to perform.
('87', 317, 3, 11, 464061) You have shown devotion in many ways.
('87', 317, 3, 12, 464099) All that devotion will have achieved fulfilment if now you turn it into devotion to God.
('87', 317, 3, 13, 464188) And true devotion to God as I see itnow is devotion to Sutranarayana 2. The word Daridranarayana 3 was first used by Vivekananda (if my memory serves me right, for I am not quite sure whether it was he or some other holy man who used it first).
('87', 317, 3, 14, 464433) The word Satyanarayana 4 is well known.
('87', 317, 3, 15, 464473) But as God of action it is Sutranarayana who reveals Himself to me.
('87', 317, 3, 16, 464541) You have started worship of that God.
('87', 317, 3, 17, 464579) Understand His nature properly.
('87', 317, 3, 18, 464611) Rise above the intrigues there or anywhere else.
('87', 317, 3, 19, 464660) If you do not show the slightest softness to Harilal, he will leave Mysore.
('87', 317, 3, 20, 464736) Try to find out, if you can, how he managed to obtain Rs. 200 from the Maharaja of Mysore.
('87', 317, 3, 21, 464827) You may tell me, when we meet, the other things which you have on your mind.
('87', 317, 3, 22, 464904) But do not worry if you cannot.
('87', 317, 3, 23, 464936) If you wish to write about them, have no hesitation in doing so.
('87', 317, 3, 24, 465001) See that Saraswati 5 and you devote yourselves to your studies and complete them.
('87', 317, 4, 25, 465083) Blessings to both of you from BAPU
('87', 317, 5, 26, 465118) From a photostat of the Gujarati: C.W. 7376. Courtesy: Kantilal Gandhi
('87', 317, 6, 27, 465189) 1 Son of Harilal Gandhi 2 God in the form of yarn 3 God in the form of the poor 4 God in the form of Truth 5 Addressee’s wife
('87', 318, 0, 1, 465315) VOL. 87: 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 319
('87', 318, 1, 2, 465357) 544. LETTER TO RAMDAS GANDHI
('87', 318, 2, 3, 465386) August 5, 1945
('87', 318, 3, 4, 465401) RAMDAS, You have used reasoning in your letter which, however, does not appeal to me.
('87', 318, 3, 5, 465487) You have a right to go to Dinshaw’s because he has made you his own.
('87', 318, 3, 6, 465556) Dinshaw is imbued with the spirit of altruism, even towards the poorest.
('87', 318, 3, 7, 465629) His is not an organization for the poor.
('87', 318, 3, 8, 465670) Similarly it is not for the rich.
('87', 318, 3, 9, 465704) However, both can go there as also those belonging to the middle class; that is possible because of Dinshaw’s good nature.
('87', 318, 3, 10, 465827) Moreover, you had no right to use reasoning the way you have, for you had given me to understand that you were about to take long leave, or had taken it, and would be devoting a year to improving your health.
('87', 318, 3, 11, 466036) Of course you will have yourself treated there and think of going to Dinshaw only after you have completely ruined your health.
('87', 318, 3, 12, 466164) As you will yourself admit you could not perceive Dinshaw’s love for you.
('87', 318, 3, 13, 466238) I therefore even now advise you to take oneyear’s leave and go to Dinshaw’s.
('87', 318, 3, 14, 466315) As I have already told you, I shall manage to find your one year’s expenses from somewhere.
('87', 318, 3, 15, 466407) I shall not pay from the Ashram funds but seek money for you from somewhere.
('87', 318, 3, 16, 466484) I have forgotten what arrangement was made about the expenditure.
('87', 318, 3, 17, 466550) However, explain that to me again and I will act accordingly.
('87', 318, 3, 18, 466612) You have something that attracts older persons to you.
('87', 318, 3, 19, 466667) I myself do not know what it is but I have firsthand knowledge of it.
('87', 318, 3, 20, 466737) Dinshaw knows many of my people but he is not drawn to them.
('87', 318, 3, 21, 466798) But he is attracted to you.
('87', 318, 3, 22, 466826) Most probably you yourself do not know why that is so.
('87', 318, 3, 23, 466881) This is one of the instances.
('87', 318, 3, 24, 466911) I have many others in my mind.
('87', 318, 3, 25, 466942) It would therefore be better if you did not argue over the matter and went to Dinshaw’s.
('87', 318, 3, 26, 467031) If you both want to go you may.
('87', 318, 3, 27, 467063) It will be enough for you to wind up the establishment from there for one year.
('87', 318, 3, 28, 467143) There are numerous teaching institutions in Poona.
('87', 318, 3, 29, 467194) Kanam and Usha won’t have any difficulty in learning Marathi if they have to.

('87', 327, 12, 18, 481043) 559. THE MISSING LINK
('87', 327, 13, 19, 481065) [Before August 8, 1945] 2
('87', 327, 14, 20, 481091) This is what the Editor of the Gram Udyog Patrika tells me:
('87', 327, 15, 21, 481151) I am afraid your last article 3 in regard to why people should give yarn for khadi is not convincing.
('87', 327, 15, 22, 481253) Your whole argument rests on the view, which is repeated several times in the course of your article, that non violent swaraj is impossible unless everybody spins.
('87', 327, 15, 23, 481417) This crucial point, however, is never explained, but taken for granted and asserted repeatedly.
('87', 327, 15, 24, 481513) Unless you can show
('87', 327, 16, 25, 481533) 1 From the reference to the letter to Atulanand Chakravarty dated August 7, 1945; vide “Letter to Atulanand Chakravarty”, 7 8 1945. 2 The article appeared in The Hindu, 11 8 1945, under the date line “Bombay, August 8”.
('87', 327, 16, 26, 481753) 3Vide “Why Khadi for yarn and not for money?”, july 1945.
('87', 328, 0, 1, 481811) VOL. 87: 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 329
('87', 328, 1, 2, 481853) what connection there is between non violent swaraj and the people of all kinds—even those who have more profitable occupation—taking to the charkha for their cloth requirements, your argument cannot convince those who honestly feel that your asking them to spin, if they want to use khadi, even when their time can be spent more profitably, is to expect a little too much from them.
('87', 328, 1, 3, 482237) So can you perhaps provide this missing link in your argument for the next issue, and show how through spinning we can obtain non violent swaraj?
('87', 328, 1, 4, 482383) The better course this time is to answer in English.
('87', 328, 1, 5, 482436) Few, if any, readers who do not know English would ask for the “missing link”, for the very simple reason that, they know my argument showing the connection between hand spinning and swaraj obtained through non violence.
('87', 328, 1, 6, 482657) Swaraj can only be obtained by work, either violent or non violent.
('87', 328, 1, 7, 482725) Violent work we know.
('87', 328, 1, 8, 482747) It necessarily includes training in the use of the most modern weapons of destruction and all it means.
('87', 328, 1, 9, 482851) By common consent this has been ruled out.
('87', 328, 1, 10, 482894) Mere constitutional means, though non violent, went out of date long ago.
('87', 328, 1, 11, 482968) It is a superstition to think that liberty can be gained by such means in the teeth of armed opposition.
('87', 328, 1, 12, 483073) Non violent work is then the only means for winning freedom.
('87', 328, 1, 13, 483134) What is the training or work that Indians should undertake for adapting themselves for non violent efforts?
('87', 328, 1, 14, 483242) It has been shown that Indian freedom was lost when India’s chief trade in cotton fabric, which was prepared in her cottages, was destroyed and together with it many other occupations which Indians carried on to sustain that trade.
('87', 328, 1, 15, 483474) It is obvious that that trade and the allied occupations should be revived or some others consistent with non violence should be taken up.
('87', 328, 1, 16, 483613) Revival was the only thing thought of.
('87', 328, 1, 17, 483652) It was being attempted by way of copying the English or, say, the modern method of replacing human labour by means of power driven machinery.
('87', 328, 1, 18, 483794) Instinctively I rejected it [as] being a way of violence and sought to replace it by human labour [as] being a way of non violence.
('87', 328, 1, 19, 483926) The struggle between the two is going on.
('87', 328, 1, 20, 483968) In my opinion, the war that is ending has demonstrated the bankruptcy of violence.
('87', 328, 1, 21, 484051) Solvency of non violence remains to be proved.
('87', 328, 1, 22, 484098) Revival of the central trade of India by means of power driven machinery is possible only by a superior exhibition of the resourcefulness of the West.
('87', 328, 1, 23, 484249) And, if it becomes possible, it will find the masses of India no better off than now.
('87', 328, 1, 24, 484335) I advance no argument in proof of this proposition.
('87', 328, 1, 25, 484387) For, it can be studied through a perusal of my writings already published in
('87', 329, 0, 1, 484464) 330 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 329, 1, 2, 484506) book form 1. Then the only form of non violent work to be done by the largest number of men, women and children of the land, in order to regain the lost trade with its attendant activities, is the spinning wheel.
('87', 329, 1, 3, 484719) Thus conceived, it easily becomes the symbol par excellence of non violence.
('87', 329, 1, 4, 484796) To be an instrument of swaraj, naturally it must not flourish under Government or any other patronage.
('87', 329, 1, 5, 484899) It must flourish, if need be, even in spite of the resistance from Government or the capitalist who is interested in his spinning and weaving mills.
('87', 329, 1, 6, 485048) The spinning wheel represents the millions in the villages as against the classes represented by the mill owners and the like.
('87', 329, 1, 7, 485175) “Assuming,” the Editor asks, “that the wheel is designed to bring in swaraj non violently, why should a person who is more usefully occupied or even disinclined spin?” The reason is more psychological than utilitarian.
('87', 329, 1, 8, 485394) The villagers have become used to imitating the city dwellers so much so that the movement is towards migration to the city slums instead of remaining in and improving their own lot in the villages.
('87', 329, 1, 9, 485593) If every person sets apart, for the sake of winning swaraj non violently, a certain time for hand spinning, an atmosphere for spinning will be created and if khadi became an article for personal use instead of being an article of commerce, which it now largely is, the question of competition with mill cloth or any other cloth will disappear and the poorest as well as the richest will be able to wear and use khadi without the slightest difficulty.
('87', 329, 1, 10, 486044) No wonder Pandit Jawaharlal Nehru has called it “the livery of our freedom”.
('87', 329, 2, 11, 486121) Gram Udyog Patrika, Vol. I
('87', 329, 3, 12, 486148) 1Economics of Khadi, a collection of Gandhiji’s articles, published in 1942 2Vide “Letter to Jawaharlal Nehru”, 30 7 1937 and Appendix “Livery of Freedom”, 31 7 1937.

('87', 335, 6, 12, 493565) 570. STATEMENT ON APPEAL FOR FUNDS 1
('87', 335, 7, 13, 493602) August 8, 1945 I have gone through the appeal 2 of the trustees.
('87', 335, 7, 14, 493667) I like it.
('87', 335, 7, 15, 493678) I hope that the entire amount they have asked for in it will be available through contributions.
('87', 335, 7, 16, 493775) I feel that much has been done for the propagation of Hindustani in the southern provinces and hope that even more will be done in the future.
('87', 335, 7, 17, 493918) People should contribute on the understanding that the money thus raised will be used for furthering the cause of the national language as I have defined it.
('87', 335, 7, 18, 494076) The national language as explained in the appeal is a language written in the Urdu or Hindi style and in the Nagari or Urdu script.
('87', 335, 7, 19, 494208) This means that the Hindi written solely in the Devanagari script cannot be called national language, nor can the language written solely in the Persian script.
('87', 335, 7, 20, 494369) The true Hindustani will be evolved only when we, who know the national language, are able to write it in both the scripts and speak in both the dictions.
('87', 335, 7, 21, 494524) There can be no doubt that even today millions of Hindus and Muslims in the North speak such a language, such Hindustani.
('87', 335, 7, 22, 494646) However, we cannot say that educated people of the North speak such Hindustani.
('87', 335, 7, 23, 494726) If it has to be our misfortune that such a state of affairs should continue, then it will continue, but it should be our
('87', 335, 8, 24, 494847) 1 This was communicated to M. Satyanarayana, General Secretary, Dakshin Bharat Hindi Prachar Sabha.

('87', 336, 0, 1, 495018) VOL. 87: 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 337
('87', 336, 1, 2, 495060) hope that it will come to an end soon.
('87', 336, 1, 3, 495099) This can be the only meaning of propagating Hindustani.
('87', 336, 1, 4, 495155) Therefore the work of propagating Hindustani which is going on in South India will emphasize both the styles.
('87', 336, 1, 5, 495265) And that is the meaning of the resolution which the Congress passed in 1925 1. The resolution was:
('87', 336, 2, 6, 495364) This Congress resolves that the proceedings of the Congress, A.I.C.C. and the Congress Working Committee shall ordinarily be conducted in Hindustani.

('87', 339, 1, 2, 499211) 575. LETTER TO VALLABHBHAI PATEL
('87', 339, 2, 3, 499244) SEVAGRAM, August 9, 1945
('87', 339, 3, 4, 499269) BHAI VALLABHBHAI, It is a pity that you cannot sleep while travelling.
('87', 339, 3, 5, 499340) We shall be reaching Poona in time, and shall see what happens there.
('87', 339, 3, 6, 499410) I leave on the 19th and arrive there 1 on the 20th.
('87', 339, 3, 7, 499462) I shall spend the day there and then we shall leave for Poona on the 21st by the first train, assuming that, as before, they will offer us a third class compartment.

('87', 342, 1, 2, 502393) 580. LETTER TO INDUMATI GUNAJI
('87', 342, 2, 3, 502424) August 10, 1945
('87', 342, 3, 4, 502440) INDU, This letter is for both of you.
('87', 342, 3, 5, 502478) I propose to solemnize your wedding on the 19th.
('87', 342, 3, 6, 502527) The ceremony is likely to be performed by Prabhakar.
('87', 342, 3, 7, 502580) He is from a Harijan family.
('87', 342, 3, 8, 502609) His parents had become Christians.
('87', 342, 3, 9, 502644) The rite is being drafted by Kakasaheb.
('87', 342, 4, 10, 502684) I assume that you approve of all this.
('87', 342, 4, 11, 502723) I think you ought to write to your elders and seek their permission.
('87', 342, 4, 12, 502792) I assume also that this marriage will not be for indulgence but for service.
('87', 342, 4, 13, 502869) I assume further that until real independence is achieved you will not consummate your marriage.
('87', 342, 4, 14, 502966) And of course I take it for granted that you will not take to contraceptive methods.
('87', 342, 4, 15, 503051) I need not say that if you find all this hard you should not feel obliged to have the marriage solemnized here.
('87', 342, 4, 16, 503163) If you approve of a marriage of this type, do regular spinning, study the 12th Chapter of the Gita with interest and understanding, and think only of public good while working in the Ashram.
('87', 342, 4, 17, 503354) Remember that in drafting this rite I have not taken the law into consideration.

('87', 344, 5, 12, 505273) 584. STATEMENT TO THE PRESS
('87', 344, 6, 13, 505301) SEVAGRAM, August 11, 1945 Those like me, who were interested in saving Mahendra Chowdhary from the gallows, are, I know, shocked that he was hanged at the Central Jail in Bhagalpur on August 7. Those who remain behind will have to know that many more such tragedies will take place.
('87', 344, 6, 14, 505584) Only, we must learn the lesson of each.
('87', 344, 6, 15, 505624) Let us, then, now dispassionately learn the lesson of this accomplished death sentence.
('87', 344, 6, 16, 505712) First, the Government.
('87', 344, 6, 17, 505735) They do not call it a political dacoity.
('87', 344, 6, 18, 505776) Every dacoity is not a political act.
('87', 344, 6, 19, 505814) Many professionals used the political ferment for their own ends.
('87', 344, 6, 20, 505880) Government, whether truly national or foreign, would not let such crimes go unpunished.
('87', 344, 6, 21, 505968) The authorities, in this case, held Mahendra Chowdhary to be implicated in such a dacoity and, therefore, they allowed the sentence to take the extreme course.
('87', 344, 6, 22, 506128) Now, for the popular side.
('87', 344, 6, 23, 506155) They say that Mahendra Chowdhary was a young man of twenty five.
('87', 344, 6, 24, 506220) He had no idea of taking part in a dacoity whether professional or political, so called.
('87', 344, 6, 25, 506309) He was in hiding.
('87', 344, 6, 26, 506327) He was tried after the event and sentenced on doubtful evidence.Acceptance of the evidence and the verdict depended on the whim of the judge or judges and at the time judges were, as often as not, biased.
('87', 344, 7, 27, 506532) 1 The contents of the letter indicate that this was written after the letter to the addressee dated August 10, 1945; vide “Letter to Indumati Gunaji”, 10 8 1945.
('87', 345, 0, 1, 506694) 346 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 345, 1, 2, 506736) If the popular belief is founded on fact, the death was a murder, worse, reprehensible because judicial.
('87', 345, 1, 3, 506841) Who can find the truth, except a body of utterly impartial lawyers?
('87', 345, 1, 4, 506909) They have to do so from the recorded evidence and the judgements of the original and appellate courts.
('87', 345, 1, 5, 507012) Let us neither be carried away by sentiment nor lazily forget the incident, now that Mahendra Chowdhary is no more.
('87', 345, 1, 6, 507128) If Government at all care for public opinion and would not rest on the overwhelming force they have at their disposal, they will be equally interested, and will associate themselves with the public.
('87', 345, 2, 7, 507327) The Hindu, 13 8 1945

('87', 350, 1, 2, 514228) 594. LETTER TO HAREKRUSHNA MAHTAB
('87', 350, 2, 3, 514262) August 12, 1945
('87', 350, 3, 4, 514278) BHAI MAHTAB 1, How are you?
('87', 350, 3, 5, 514306) You did not even mention in your letter where you were writing from.
('87', 350, 3, 6, 514375) It is not that the khadi produced in Orissa cannot go out of the province.

('87', 355, 4, 5, 519522) 607. LETTER TO Y. M. PARNERKAR
('87', 355, 5, 6, 519553) August 13, 1945
('87', 355, 6, 7, 519569) PARNERKAR, If the manure was lying there because of paucity of labour you should have taken help from the Ashram inmates.
('87', 355, 6, 8, 519691) You will remember you have asked for such help before.
('87', 355, 6, 9, 519746) There was no point in shifting itfrom one place to another.
('87', 355, 6, 10, 519806) It can be used for vegetables; but the question is whether it is more useful for the fruit trees or for the vegetables.
('87', 355, 6, 11, 519926) I felt that your reply was not straight.
('87', 355, 6, 12, 519967) If we have been negligent it is our duty to own it.
('87', 355, 6, 13, 520019) (2) I will myself see about the trees.
('87', 355, 6, 14, 520058) (3) I shall be pleased if Shri Patil and his sister in law live in the Ashram and work in the Goshala.
('87', 355, 6, 15, 520161) But have a talk with Munnalalji and write to Patil what he says.
('87', 355, 6, 16, 520226) (4) I will certainly like it if Ramnarayan can stay in the Goshala.
('87', 355, 6, 17, 520294) Ask him whether he wishes to stay or not.
('87', 355, 6, 18, 520336) I was under the impression that at the moment it is not possible to accommodate him under any circumstances.
('87', 355, 6, 19, 520445) (5) Does the Hindustani Talimi Sangh want developed land?
('87', 355, 6, 20, 520503) I thought it was otherwise.
('87', 355, 6, 21, 520531) We must give the land.
('87', 355, 6, 22, 520554) Put down everything in Writing and let me know.
('87', 355, 6, 23, 520602) Let them have it on a nominal rent, for a specific period.
('87', 355, 6, 24, 520661) Give them the right to return the land.
('87', 355, 6, 25, 520701) I think I have replied to all your questions.

('87', 356, 1, 2, 520904) 608. NOTE TO INDUMATI GUNAJI [After August 13, 1945] 1
('87', 356, 2, 3, 520959) Now you can talk.
('87', 356, 2, 4, 520977) I shall talk if I have to reply.
('87', 356, 2, 5, 521010) The question is not about.
('87', 356, 2, 6, 521037) 2 at Wardha.
('87', 356, 2, 7, 521050) The question is what is proper for you.
('87', 356, 2, 8, 521090) I have not laid down any condition.
('87', 356, 2, 9, 521126) If you Say it is something new, then you may leave it.
('87', 356, 2, 10, 521181) You are not a little girl, nor are you an ordinary woman.
('87', 356, 2, 11, 521239) You are a worker of some standing.
('87', 356, 2, 12, 521274) Tendulkar is an experienced man.
('87', 356, 2, 13, 521307) I might join you two in wedlock only to see you lost in family life.
('87', 356, 2, 14, 521376) Read my letter 3 again; you will not find in it any condition, only a keendesire on my part.
('87', 356, 2, 15, 521469) If you have already decided to lead family life, what is the use of going through an Ashram wedding?
('87', 356, 2, 16, 521570) You do not know the amount of pains I am taking and how much I am thinking about it.
('87', 356, 2, 17, 521655) In my opinion this is no small matter.
('87', 356, 2, 18, 521694) Know that I had expressed the same desire in the case of every other wedding.
('87', 356, 2, 19, 521772) But they were all young girls with the exception of Saundaram.
('87', 356, 2, 20, 521835) You on the other hand ought to raise more important questions.
('87', 356, 2, 21, 521898) How will it look if you desired progeny before the coming of independence?
('87', 356, 2, 22, 521973) I shall not forbid you from inviting those people if you wish.
('87', 356, 2, 23, 522036) Will they have to be served a meal here?
('87', 356, 2, 24, 522077) Tell me after thinking over it.
('87', 356, 2, 25, 522109) Show me my letter.
('87', 356, 2, 26, 522128) Does my language imply a condition?
('87', 356, 4, 27, 522164) This is a different matter.
('87', 356, 4, 28, 522192) When you say that I laid down a condition which was not there earlier, I maintain that I have stipulated no such condition.
('87', 356, 4, 29, 522316) This is why I made the inquiry.
('87', 356, 4, 30, 522348) I can do something only on the assumption that neither of you will be a hypocrite.
('87', 356, 4, 31, 522431) In the event of hypocrisy I shall not be losing anything; only you two will stand to lose.
('87', 356, 4, 32, 522522) This has been my experience to date.
('87', 356, 4, 33, 522559) Those who betrayed me have ultimately fallen.
('87', 356, 5, 34, 522605) From a photostat of the Hindi: C.W. 10950. Courtesy: Indumati G. Tendulkar
('87', 356, 6, 35, 522680) 1 From the contents it is evident that this note was written after the letter to the addressee dated August 13, 1945. Vide “Letter to Indumati Gunaji”, 13 8 1945. 2 One word is illegible here.
('87', 356, 6, 36, 522873) 3 Dated August 10; vide “Letter to Indumati Gunaji”, 10 8 1945.

('87', 357, 5, 10, 523237) 610. DISCUSSION WITH B. S. MURTHY 1
('87', 357, 6, 11, 523273) [Before August 14, 1945] 2
('87', 357, 7, 12, 523300) I can give you advice only as from one individual to another.
('87', 357, 7, 13, 523362) I am not giving any advice to the Harijan Sevak Sangh which is an institution.
('87', 357, 7, 14, 523441) After all the Harijan Sevak Sangh is only as good as the best men in it and I know how few they are.
('87', 357, 7, 15, 523542) The Sangh has done substantial work, though not in the estimation of the Harijans or in the estimation of the orthodox Hindus.
('87', 357, 7, 16, 523669) The Harijans may want to smash the caste Hindus and the caste Hindus may want to cling to the old way.
('87', 357, 7, 17, 523772) The Sangh has to face both these.
('87', 357, 7, 18, 523806) You have asked me how the Sangh can be revitalized.
('87', 357, 7, 19, 523858) I know the royal way is a fast by me.
('87', 357, 7, 20, 523896) I might fast again and that more readily for Harijans than for anything else.
('87', 357, 7, 21, 523974) But I must wait till God asks me to do it.
('87', 357, 7, 22, 524017) There is no such thing as a forced fast.
('87', 357, 7, 23, 524058) It has to come and I cannot say now when it will come.
('87', 357, 7, 24, 524113) I must also tell you that there are others who want to fast for the Harijans.
('87', 357, 7, 25, 524191) But I have told them that they are not to fast while I am alive.
('87', 357, 7, 26, 524256) I have also the idea of a chain of fasts.
('87', 357, 7, 27, 524298) In such a chain I will fast first and then when my body has perished, the next fast will begin and it will go on till untouchability is no more.
('87', 357, 7, 28, 524443) Such a fast is conceived, but it cannot be taken up at once as I said it has to come.
('87', 357, 7, 29, 524529) But before even such a thing happens a lot of spade work has to be done.
('87', 357, 7, 30, 524602) That is why Harijan Sevak Sangh workers are
('87', 357, 8, 31, 524646) 1Who had sought Gandhiji’s advice on the various problems of Harijans 2From the reference to the Harijan Sevak Sangh workers’ meeting which was held on August 14, 1945. Vide also “Letter to Sudhir Ghosh”, 28 8 1945.
('87', 358, 0, 1, 524862) VOL. 87 : 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 359
('87', 358, 1, 2, 524905) meeting here soon.
('87', 358, 1, 3, 524924) They are meeting for the very purpose of revitalizing the Sangh’s work.
('87', 358, 1, 4, 524996) The present feeling among the Harijan Sevak Sangh workers is that practically nothing has been done among caste Hindus.
('87', 358, 1, 5, 525116) Education of Harijans is one thing; education of Savarnas is another and as I know more difficult.
('87', 358, 1, 6, 525215) You can educate Harijans by giving them scholarships, hostels, etc., but no such way is possible among the caste Hindus.
('87', 358, 1, 7, 525336) The task, therefore, is to educate the savarnas.
('87', 358, 1, 8, 525385) But this can be done only by those who are fired by a living faith in the Hinduism which I understand.
('87', 358, 1, 9, 525488) Only those who fully know the meaningof Hinduism as I know it can perform the miracle.
('87', 358, 1, 10, 525575) Let us not forget that untouchability is a most difficult thing to remove and that our task is a heavy one.
('87', 358, 1, 11, 525683) But I have no doubt that God will remove untou chability or remove Hinduism.
('87', 358, 1, 12, 525760) Now in regard to your question on the political future of Harijans, I certainly see that those Harijans who have become poli tically conscious should straightaway have a full opportunity to figure in politics.
('87', 358, 1, 13, 525970) You have asked me what I mean by saying that I want such Harijans to be more than a match for all other political competitors.
('87', 358, 1, 14, 526097) Many people weigh the Harijans in some special Harijan balance.
('87', 358, 1, 15, 526161) But I want to weigh the Harijans in the same balance in which I weigh the best.
('87', 358, 1, 16, 526241) You have to outweigh others because you have to cover so much lost distance.
('87', 358, 1, 17, 526318) That is why I expect from the Harijans greater effort than from others.
('87', 358, 1, 18, 526390) You have asked me whether Dr. Ambedkar has in my opinion thus proved himself to be more than a match.
('87', 358, 1, 19, 526492) My answer is ‘Yes’ and ‘No’.
('87', 358, 1, 20, 526521) Dr. Ambedkar is a fierce and fearless man.
('87', 358, 1, 21, 526564) He does not scruple to beat the Hindu dog with any stick he can get.
('87', 358, 1, 22, 526633) He wants to destroy Hinduism.
('87', 358, 1, 23, 526663) It is open to him to do it.
('87', 358, 1, 24, 526691) If the Harijans want to do it they can do it.
('87', 358, 1, 25, 526737) Then the Harijans must become the destroyers of Hinduism.
('87', 358, 1, 26, 526795) I want Harijans to become as able and earnest as Dr. Ambedkar but in a different way.
('87', 358, 1, 27, 526881) I want you to do even better.
('87', 358, 1, 28, 526911) I want you to produce sterling men who will reshape the whole of our society.
('87', 358, 1, 29, 526989) It is not enough to be educated.
('87', 358, 1, 30, 527022) It is necessary to be cultured and fearless.
('87', 358, 1, 31, 527067) Such men who will reshape society will have to work among the people and not cut themselves away from the people.
('87', 358, 1, 32, 527181) They will have to be stern, incorruptible and self reliant.
('87', 358, 1, 33, 527241) There is nothing to prevent such people from taking any assistance from clean quarters.
('87', 358, 1, 34, 527329) But my point is the more you lean on such assistance, the more difficult becomes the task of uplifting the Harijans.
('87', 358, 1, 35, 527446) The Hindu, 21 8 1945 and 31 8 1945

('87', 364, 7, 16, 532291) WARDHA, August 14, 1945
('87', 364, 8, 17, 532315) Gandhiji said that only caste Hindus and no Harijan should be taken on the Executive of the Sangh, as it was the caste Hindus who had to atone for their sin of prolonging untouchability.
('87', 364, 8, 18, 532502) Harijans could be members of the supervision committee that might be set up for carrying on the work properly.
('87', 364, 9, 19, 532613) Replying to a question, Gandhiji said that he would appreciate the principle of satyagraha for enforcing the civic rights of Harijans in public places like tanks, wells, temples, etc.
('87', 364, 9, 20, 532797) He, however, emphasized that the Harijan Sevak Sangh as an organization should not be involved in such a satyagraha.
('87', 364, 9, 21, 532914) Individual Harijan workers might try that remedy with the help of others.
('87', 364, 10, 22, 532988) Gandhiji explained to the members how Harijan work was to be carried on.
('87', 364, 10, 23, 533061) Persistent propaganda for changing the hearts of the orthodox and caste Hindus, hesaid, would greatly help to solve the problem of untouchability which was a stigma on Hinduism.
('87', 364, 11, 24, 533239) To create confidence among Harijans, Mahatma Gandhi went on, Harijan workers had to live amidst Harijans, mix with them, study their local and other
('87', 364, 12, 25, 533388) 1 Of the Central Board of Harijan Sevak Sangh; vide the following item.

('87', 365, 1, 2, 533574) problems and try to solve them to their satisfaction.

('87', 366, 8, 23, 536589) I grant that in the very first year we cannot become self reliant.
('87', 366, 8, 24, 536656) However, when we complete the entire process the expenditure and the income should balance.
('87', 366, 8, 25, 536748) I would not call agriculture a handicraft.
('87', 366, 8, 26, 536791) But it is an occupation of crores of people.
('87', 366, 8, 27, 536836) It does not encourage skill but it does give a lot of physical exercise.
('87', 366, 8, 28, 536909) It has been accorded its rightful place after seven years.
('87', 366, 8, 29, 536968) It is a sad thing that we have been divided into two groups but that is inevitable.
('87', 366, 8, 30, 537052) We regard constructive work as a symbol of ahimsa while others look upon it as a means of furthering their work.
('87', 366, 8, 31, 537165) And that only to the extent that if they can do without itthey will do so.

('87', 370, 0, 1, 542057) VOL. 87 : 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 371
('87', 370, 1, 2, 542100) Kan aiyo.
('87', 370, 1, 3, 542110) They all agree with me.
('87', 370, 1, 4, 542134) Jajuji has even written down his view.
('87', 370, 1, 5, 542173) I send it with this.
('87', 370, 1, 6, 542194) He has described his own experience.
('87', 370, 1, 7, 542231) I am confident that a person like you is bound to have the same experience.
('87', 370, 1, 8, 542307) “Swaraj will be gained through yarn,” I said, relying on intuition.
('87', 370, 1, 9, 542375) But I realize now that intuition is one thing and its confirmation by experience another.
('87', 370, 1, 10, 542465) And what I have been putting forward now is something different still.
('87', 370, 1, 11, 542536) Others are having more convincing experience of the same.
('87', 370, 1, 12, 542594) It is not going to impress me at all even if in Kathiawar khadi worth Rs. 4 lakhs instead of Rs. 2 lakhs is produced and sold.
('87', 370, 1, 13, 542721) For it could be proved that such production and sale of khadi would only promote the welfare of the poor, and an all India institution like the Charkha Sangh need not be established merely for that purpose.
('87', 370, 1, 14, 542928) A co operative of the poor for producing khadi could be established and more khadi at still lower cost could be produced.
('87', 370, 1, 15, 543050) But even then that khadi would be of value only as khadi for the poor.
('87', 370, 1, 16, 543121) It would, one may say, make no contribution to the cause of swaraj.
('87', 370, 1, 17, 543189) I, therefore, desire that you should have perfect self confidence and adopt this new method—policy—for khadi and discover from experience that it is khadi for swaraj.
('87', 370, 1, 18, 543356) It is quite possible that Kathiawar may not accept such khadi.
('87', 370, 1, 19, 543419) If so, don’t mind if no khadi work is done there, for you must be aware that no such work is done in many Indian States.
('87', 370, 1, 20, 543540) In the same way if no work is done in Kathiawar, either, the cause of khadi for swaraj would not suffer.
('87', 370, 1, 21, 543645) I go even further and say that in carrying on khadi activity for swaraj, if it ceases to be khadi for the poor, the latter are not going to lose anything for they will be able to earn their bread in some other way.
('87', 370, 1, 22, 543860) But if khadi supports the poor even while remaining khadi for the swaraj, it would be a credit both to the poor and the cause of swaraj.
('87', 370, 1, 23, 543997) The poor thereby would have contributed to the winning of swaraj.
('87', 370, 1, 24, 544063) If I have left any point unexplained, Kanaiyo will explain it when he arrives there.
('87', 370, 1, 25, 544148) I hope your health is perfect.
('87', 370, 1, 26, 544179) If you can leave that place, it might be better for you to come and see me once.
('87', 370, 2, 27, 544260) Blessings from BAPU
('87', 370, 3, 28, 544280) From a microfilm of the Gujarati: M.M.U./II.

('87', 371, 0, 1, 544367) 372 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 371, 1, 2, 544409) 632. LETTER TO LAKSHMI NARAYAN AGRAWAL
('87', 371, 2, 3, 544448) August 16, 1945
('87', 371, 3, 4, 544464) BHAI LAKSHMI BABU, We cannot accept even one of the three conditions.
('87', 371, 3, 5, 544534) 1 Even though we believe that it is an inflammatory speech, constructive activity has no relation at all with movements such as that of 1942. Even if we denounce the violent activities of Shri Jayaprakash Narayan, we cannot accept any of these three conditions, that is to say, we cannot compel the workers to respect them.
('87', 371, 3, 6, 544858) If the independence of India is common cause between us and the Government then what is the meaning of all these differences?
('87', 371, 3, 7, 544984) The truth is that the Bihar Government has made a mistake in making the arrests but instead of acknowledging the mistake it wants to put the responsibility on us.
('87', 371, 3, 8, 545147) We will not accept the responsibility even if they should wipe us out.
('87', 371, 3, 9, 545218) Let them stop our peaceful activities.
('87', 371, 3, 10, 545257) We shall still go forward.

('87', 373, 6, 21, 549995) 636. YARN DONATION
('87', 373, 7, 22, 550014) We all know that Shri Narandas Gandhi is a dedicated votary of khadi.
('87', 373, 7, 23, 550084) He has such great faith in khadi that he sees Daridranarayana in it.
('87', 373, 7, 24, 550153) He therefore spins for many hours a day.
('87', 373, 7, 25, 550194) He has also given a prominent place to spinning in the national school conducted by him at Rajkot.
('87', 373, 7, 26, 550293) For the last many years he has been collecting both yarn and money for the “Charkha Dwadashi’’ 1. This time he has carried
('87', 373, 8, 27, 550416) 1Gandhiji’s birthday according to the Vikram calendar
('87', 374, 0, 1, 550470) VOL. 87 : 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 375
('87', 374, 1, 2, 550513) the sutra yajna a long way and he has expressed his wish to the country that not only spinning but donating of yarn should catch on.
('87', 374, 1, 3, 550646) Everyone can participate in it.
('87', 374, 1, 4, 550678) It should be borne in mind that he does not insist that the yarn should be donated to him only.
('87', 374, 1, 5, 550774) It can be given to All India Spinners’ Association as well.
('87', 374, 1, 6, 550834) What he wants is that people should now give yarn donations freely and that he should be supplied with figures as to the quantity of yarn spun all over India and the quantity of yarn donated.
('87', 374, 1, 7, 551026) To provide information to the public it is enough if these figures are sent to the All India Spinners’ Asso ciation office.
('87', 374, 1, 8, 551150) However, the activity will gain impetus if figures are sent to the person who has conceived the idea, has struggled for it and has fostered the activity.
('87', 374, 1, 9, 551304) If the figures are sent to him, he will have a clear picture of the work done and his planning and knowledge will prove very useful to all for further progress of work.
('87', 374, 1, 10, 551473) Every year he seeks my consent for whatever work he does.
('87', 374, 1, 11, 551531) This year I thought it proper to accept only yarn donations and suggested it to him accordingly.
('87', 374, 1, 12, 551628) I have visualized yarn currency and have called Chi.
('87', 374, 1, 13, 551681) Narandas its banker.
('87', 374, 1, 14, 551702) I believe that he has the right ability and purity for that kind of work.
('87', 374, 1, 15, 551776) It is possible that at present the yarn will not fulfil all the requirements of the currency.
('87', 374, 1, 16, 551870) But our aim today is to increase the number of spinners from the standpoint of non violent swaraj.
('87', 374, 1, 17, 551969) An experiment to make yarn a currency was made locally at Nalwadi.
('87', 374, 1, 18, 552036) Another experiment is going on in Bezwada.
('87', 374, 1, 19, 552079) However the ideas behind the two experiments were different.
('87', 374, 1, 20, 552140) The experiment can be extended to cover the whole of India.
('87', 374, 1, 21, 552200) Only one year will be required for such currency to come into force.
('87', 374, 1, 22, 552269) Every home will then become a mint.
('87', 374, 1, 23, 552305) But it is only an idea today.
('87', 374, 1, 24, 552335) For the time being all the spinners will produce currency in the form of yarn and will give that away in donation.
('87', 374, 1, 25, 552450) Every branch of the All India Spinners’ Associa tion will collect such donations.
('87', 374, 1, 26, 552532) The yarn will belong to the All India Spinners’ Association.
('87', 374, 1, 27, 552593) Only the account will be sent to Chi.
('87', 374, 1, 28, 552631) Narandas.
('87', 374, 1, 29, 552641) The ownership will be that of the All India Spinners’ Association.
('87', 374, 1, 30, 552708) Narandas will be the custodian of the yarn sent to him directly or collected by himself.
('87', 374, 1, 31, 552797) It will be utilized and distributed with my permi ssion.
('87', 374, 1, 32, 552854) The money and the yarn collected by Chi.
('87', 374, 1, 33, 552895) Narandas every year is distributed with my permission.
('87', 374, 1, 34, 552950) It will be the same this year also.
('87', 374, 1, 35, 552986) This year the idea of cash collection has been given up.
('87', 374, 1, 36, 553043) However, cash will be received from those who want to give it but the
('87', 375, 0, 1, 553113) 376 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 375, 1, 2, 553155) All India Spinner’s Association will not make any arrangement for its collection.
('87', 375, 1, 3, 553237) The same rule applies to Chi.
('87', 375, 1, 4, 553267) Narandas.
('87', 375, 1, 5, 553277) The aim will be to collect only yarn donations.
('87', 375, 1, 6, 553325) Whatever yarn the All India Spinners’ Association collects will be its capital.
('87', 375, 1, 7, 553405) From now on it will not collect cash for carrying on its activities but will manage with yarn only.
('87', 375, 1, 8, 553505) The yarn thus collected will not be sold.
('87', 375, 1, 9, 553547) But the khadi made from it will be sold.
('87', 375, 1, 10, 553588) Yarn will be taken but not given.
('87', 375, 1, 11, 553622) Only the things made from it will be given and sold.
('87', 375, 1, 12, 553675) The rule already exists of taking a certain amount of yarn when selling khadi but at some places the practice has been started of giving khadi in exchange for the full quantity of yarn.
('87', 375, 1, 13, 553861) In spite of that the effort will be to have only yarn donations on the occasion ofCharkha Jayanti.
('87', 375, 1, 14, 553960) However, I want that besides khadi other articles of village industries should be made available in exchange for yarn.
('87', 375, 1, 15, 554079) But that can be realized only when we take the final step.
('87', 375, 1, 16, 554138) At the moment I have presented the idea of yarn currency only in its initial form.
('87', 375, 1, 17, 554221) It is easy for accounting and the capital of yarn increases not by interest but by the labour of the spinner.
('87', 375, 1, 18, 554331) If the people understand this scheme then yarn will become an instrument for the production of goods worth crores of rupees.
('87', 375, 1, 19, 554456) Physical labour will become the capital and will easily be able to compete with capitalists.
