('87', 376, 3, 5, 554727) I shall look into the Nayee Talim matter.
('87', 376, 3, 6, 554769) Ashadevi is not here at present.
('87', 376, 3, 7, 554802) I have not a full copy of the Ramayana as abridged by me but I send you a marked copy of the Ramayana from which you will be able to know the principles on which I had worked.
('87', 376, 3, 8, 554978) As far as possible I have tried to retain the historical or narrative portion unbroken.
('87', 376, 3, 9, 555066) Some of the interpolations are useful by themselves, but still I have dropped them altogether.
('87', 376, 3, 10, 555161) I have also dropped any matter which had been over lengthened as also such portions as appeared to me unnecessary for the narrative.
('87', 376, 3, 11, 555294) I have also generally removed portions where woman is referred to in derogatory terms.
('87', 376, 3, 12, 555381) But I have kept some portions of it just to indicate the mind of Tulsidas.
('87', 376, 3, 13, 555456) So far as I can remember at the moment, these are the principles I worked upon.
('87', 376, 3, 14, 555536) But you are intelligent enough to discover any other principle not mentioned here from the marks in the book.
('87', 376, 3, 15, 555646) Failure has compelled me to do what I was not prepared to do by persuasion.
('87', 376, 3, 16, 555722) I mean that I have commenced from yesterday therecitation of Gitai 2 in place of the Sanskrit Gita.
('87', 376, 3, 17, 555822) I realized that nobody learnt Sanskrit.
('87', 376, 3, 18, 555862) The same old members are there, but even they do not or are unable to study Sanskrit even to the extent of understanding the Gita.
('87', 376, 3, 19, 555993) Moreover, they were unable to recite it in chorus, and what pained me more was the fact that though the recitation of the whole of the Gita was confined to the morning prayer, still some members walked out as soon as the recitation began.
('87', 376, 3, 20, 556232) On making an enquiry into the cause of this, I found that it was very trivial.
('87', 376, 3, 21, 556311) I did not know it before.
('87', 376, 3, 22, 556337) I found it out only the day before yesterday, and I immediately came to the conclusion that perhaps interest in the Gita might be created more quickly if it was recited in Hindi, Marathi or Gujarati since the people would understand its

('87', 381, 4, 9, 563453) 646. HOW TO DO IT?
('87', 381, 5, 10, 563472) The A. I. V. I. A. has not shown the results it might have.
('87', 381, 5, 11, 563532) I have often asked myself that question.
('87', 381, 5, 12, 563573) I try now and here to think aloud and confer with the workers to see what can be done.
('87', 381, 5, 13, 563660) We lazily copy the Congress and set up committees and think that we shall thereby popularize and advance the craft of the villages.
('87', 381, 5, 14, 563792) We forget that the Congress, being a democratic body, must work democratically and through committees set up by the people from [among] themselves.
('87', 381, 5, 15, 563940) On the other hand, the A.I.V.I.A. and like bodies are self formed to work out particular purposes often requiring high technical skill.
('87', 381, 5, 16, 564076) They collect money from those who appreciate the particular purpose and become trustees for the money to be used therefor.
('87', 381, 5, 17, 564199) We collect and study the literature on the subject.
('87', 381, 5, 18, 564251) We look about for and employ experts and if there are none become experts ourselves.
('87', 381, 5, 19, 564336) The work will make progress in exact proportion to our knowledge, earnestness and industry.
('87', 381, 5, 20, 564428) The work itself may be unpopular or unknown.
('87', 381, 5, 21, 564473) We have then to make it popular or known.
('87', 381, 5, 22, 564515) Such associations all over the world must work whether in countries democratically or autocratically governed.
('87', 381, 5, 23, 564626) In either case they must work under patronage or in the teeth of opposition.
('87', 381, 5, 24, 564703) The system of work will be identical under either autocracy or democracy.
('87', 381, 5, 25, 564777) With us the A. I. S. A., the A. I. V. I. A., the Hindustani Talimi Sangh, etc., though autonomous, are creations of the Congress and, therefore requiring enthusiastic support of all Congressmen and, to the extent that Congressmen represent all India, of Indians throughout the land.
('87', 381, 5, 26, 565060) But before this can happen we must dot India with experts of the type wanted.
('87', 381, 5, 27, 565138) Therefore, the first thing is to have a central body of honest experts.
('87', 381, 5, 28, 565210) There is no other royal road to success.
('87', 381, 5, 29, 565251) Committees or even agents can show no results unless they are experts who know their
('87', 382, 0, 1, 565336) VOL. 87 : 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 383
('87', 382, 1, 2, 565379) Can an M.A., however brilliant he may be, introduce, say, the charkha among the villagers, or gur making from palm trees or manure making from village refuse including human excreta and cattle dung?
('87', 382, 1, 3, 565578) We must have experts in these and such other branches.
('87', 382, 1, 4, 565633) If we had our own government, however inefficient, we would have technical institutes where every one of the useful activities now going on or which were going on even yesterday in the 7,00,000 villages could be studied.
('87', 382, 1, 5, 565854) Unfortunately, we have not.
('87', 382, 1, 6, 565882) Hence our associations have also to be such institutes in addition to becoming propagandists.
('87', 382, 1, 7, 565976) But before we can become the latter, we have to become the former.
('87', 382, 1, 8, 566043) If I have drawn a correct picture, let us mend even though the mending may be difficult and even hurtful to our pride.
('87', 382, 1, 9, 566162) ON THE TRAIN TO BOMBAY, August 20, 1945
('87', 382, 2, 10, 566202) From a copy: Pyarelal Papers.
('87', 382, 2, 11, 566232) Courtesy: Pyarelal.
('87', 382, 2, 12, 566252) Also Gram Udyog Patrika, Vol. I, pp.
('87', 382, 3, 13, 566289) 647. FOREWORD TO “THE ECONOMY OF PERMANENCE”
('87', 382, 4, 14, 566334) Like his brochure on the Practice and Precepts of Jesus, Dr. Kumarappa’s on The Economy of Permanence is a jail production.
('87', 382, 4, 15, 566458) It is not as easy to understand as the first.
('87', 382, 4, 16, 566504) It needs careful reading twice or thrice if it is to be fully appreciated.
('87', 382, 4, 17, 566579) When I took up the manuscript I was curious to know what it could contain.
('87', 382, 4, 18, 566654) The opening chapter satisfied my curiosity and led me on to the end without fatigue and yet with profit.
('87', 382, 4, 19, 566759) This doctor of our village industries shows that only through them we shall arrive at the economy of permanence in the place of that of the fleeting nature we see around us at present.
('87', 382, 4, 20, 566944) He tackles the question—shall the body triumph over and stifle the soul or shall the latter triumph over and express itself through a perishable body which, with its few wants healthily satisfied, will be free to subserve the end of the imperishable soul?
('87', 382, 4, 21, 567200) This is “Plain living and high thinking”.
('87', 382, 5, 22, 567242) M. K. GANDHI ON THE TRAIN TO BOMBAY, August 20, 1945
('87', 382, 6, 23, 567295) The Economy of Permanence

('87', 390, 5, 19, 577107) I hope you are well.

('87', 393, 1, 2, 579795) 668. LETTER TO RAMNARAYAN CHOWDHARY
('87', 393, 2, 3, 579831) August 22, 1945
('87', 393, 3, 4, 579847) RAMNARAYAN, I have gone through the English part of what you have sent.
('87', 393, 3, 5, 579919) Why did you have to write in English?
('87', 393, 3, 6, 579957) Hindustani would have been sufficient.
('87', 393, 3, 7, 579996) The English needs improvement.
('87', 393, 3, 8, 580027) You must leave that to others.
('87', 393, 3, 9, 580058) I shall try to read the Hindustani also.
('87', 393, 3, 10, 580099) I shall read the scheme of Goseva Sangh also before getting it published.
('87', 393, 3, 11, 580173) Show it to Parnerkar and Satis Babu and, if possible, to a veterinarian.
('87', 393, 3, 12, 580246) I had a few pages read out to me by Sushilabehn.
('87', 393, 3, 13, 580295) She has pointed out some technical mistakes.
('87', 393, 3, 14, 580340) The treatment of the subject matter is good.
('87', 393, 3, 15, 580385) You have said in brief all that you could say.
('87', 393, 3, 16, 580432) If I want to return it shall I send it to Ahmedabad?
('87', 393, 3, 17, 580485) I understand that you have not kept a copy.
('87', 393, 3, 18, 580529) You suggest boycotting the buffalo.
('87', 393, 3, 19, 580565) This you will not have got from my writings.
('87', 393, 3, 20, 580610) My view is that our preference should be for the Cow.Doing this will save both.
('87', 393, 3, 21, 580690) At present there is shortage of milk, so We need both.
('87', 393, 3, 22, 580745) Preferring the cow saves both, preferring the buffalo destroys both.
('87', 393, 3, 23, 580814) I hope all of you are well.
('87', 393, 4, 24, 580842) Blessings from BAPU SHRI RAMNARAYANJI AHMEDABAD

('87', 394, 6, 9, 581526) POONA, August 23, 1945
('87', 394, 7, 10, 581549) MY DEAR MARIA 1, Your half angry and half loving letter.
('87', 394, 7, 11, 581606) Why are you so foolish as to take in what a third party says?
('87', 394, 7, 12, 581668) Kasturba 2 is a wholly non sectarian organization.
('87', 394, 7, 13, 581719) Who was the third party who gave you to understand that only Hindus could apply?
('87', 394, 7, 14, 581800) The thing has to come before me.
('87', 394, 7, 15, 581833) It has not yet.
('87', 394, 7, 16, 581849) If you have applied send me a copy of the application too.
('87', 394, 7, 17, 581908) You know that Aryanayakum is a Christian?
('87', 394, 7, 18, 581950) Raihana Tyabji is a trustee.
('87', 394, 7, 19, 581979) So much for the Trust.
('87', 394, 7, 20, 582002) When there is independence, why should you fear the majority?
('87', 394, 7, 21, 582064) If you have God with you and the majority have not, should you still fear?
('87', 394, 7, 22, 582139) And if both have God between them who should fear whom?
('87', 394, 7, 23, 582195) Is there then any question of majority and minority?
('87', 394, 7, 24, 582248) Let us pray.
('87', 394, 8, 25, 582261) BAPU MISS MARIA PETERSEN SEVA MANDIR PORTO NOVO (S. I.)

('87', 408, 6, 11, 596948) 702. LETTER TO KISHORELAL G. MASHRUWALA
('87', 408, 7, 12, 596988) August 27, 1945
('87', 408, 8, 13, 597004) KISHORELAL, I have your letter.
('87', 408, 8, 14, 597036) The weather is still moist.
('87', 408, 8, 15, 597064) The house is near the mill and it is possible to find something there.
('87', 408, 8, 16, 597135) But I do not have the courage to call you here till the weather completely clears.
('87', 408, 8, 17, 597218) We do not want to fall out of the frying pan into the fire.
('87', 408, 8, 18, 597278) Still I will call you when it completely stops raining here and that too in the hope that the change of air will do good to both of you.
('87', 408, 8, 19, 597415) I do not want to take work from you here.
('87', 408, 8, 20, 597457) Valji comes daily.
('87', 408, 8, 21, 597476) His competent son is also prepared to render some service but I have not entrusted him with any work.
('87', 408, 8, 22, 597578) There is no work which can be given to him.
('87', 408, 8, 23, 597622) I understand about Parnerkar.
('87', 408, 8, 24, 597652) You have done what you could.
('87', 408, 8, 25, 597682) It seems that your recom mendations cannot be implemented now.
('87', 408, 8, 26, 597745) Everyone has land and a house, how can they be removed?
('87', 408, 8, 27, 597801) Moreover, can those who are true workers stay at a distance?
('87', 408, 8, 28, 597862) Why should they be servants?
('87', 408, 8, 29, 597891) It is a matter of shame and sorrow that they are retained as servants.
('87', 408, 8, 30, 597962) Thenumber of those who are retained as servants will not be reduced by their staying in different places.
('87', 408, 8, 31, 598068) Only the attitude of everyone should be changed.
('87', 408, 8, 32, 598117) If that happens the question of staying separately or in different places should not arise.
('87', 408, 8, 33, 598209) Yes, one thing is certain.
('87', 408, 8, 34, 598236) It will
('87', 409, 0, 1, 598244) 410 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 409, 1, 2, 598286) be a long time before people’s nature changes.
('87', 409, 1, 3, 598333) In the mean time there will be a scramble for servants and that will do good to no one.
('87', 409, 1, 4, 598421) However, if I have understood your recommendations they may be applied in future but not to the organizations which are functioning today.
('87', 409, 1, 5, 598560) There was and is a purpose in merging all the organizations, although whatever has happened was only a drifting of the current.
('87', 409, 1, 6, 598688) Do let me know if there is a flaw in the argument.
('87', 409, 1, 7, 598739) If the present situation cannot be changed I want to understand the whole position.
('87', 409, 1, 8, 598823) I hope both of you are keeping good health.

('87', 415, 6, 13, 604507) 716. MESSAGE TO AMERICA 1
('87', 415, 7, 14, 604533) [On or before August 29, 1945] 2
('87', 415, 8, 15, 604566) In spite of my disinclination to answer the question like the one put to me by Mr. Emanuel Celler, I feel that I shall be wanting in courtesy, if I do not meet Mr. Celler’s wishes.
('87', 415, 8, 16, 604747) The best way for America to assist India’s struggle for independence is to study the question, so as not to be misled by the untruth that is being spread by British Agency at a great cost about India.
('87', 415, 8, 17, 604948) Americans have to get out of the way of her struggle.
('87', 415, 8, 18, 605002) For the rest, India has to fight her own battle of independence which she is trying to secure by a non violent technique.
('87', 415, 9, 19, 605124) The Bombay Chronicle, 30 8 1945
('87', 415, 10, 20, 605156) 1 This was conveyed to Emanuel Celler, member of the United States House of Representatives, through D. F. Karaka, special correspondent of The Bombay Chronicle in New York.
('87', 415, 10, 21, 605330) Emanuel Celler had asked how “we in the United States can aid in hastening the attainment of India’s independence”.
('87', 415, 10, 22, 605446) 2 The report appeared under the date line “Wednesday” which was August 29.

('87', 422, 8, 17, 611758) What will you do if I die?

('87', 424, 1, 2, 614199) APPENDICES
('87', 424, 2, 3, 614210) APPENDIX I
('87', 424, 3, 4, 614221) LETTER FROM JAIRAMDAS DAULATRAM TO ANAND T. HINGORANI 1
('87', 424, 4, 5, 614277) PANCHGANI, June 10, 1945
('87', 424, 5, 6, 614302) DEAR BROTHER,
('87', 424, 6, 7, 614316) You must have received my letter sent from here.
('87', 424, 6, 8, 614365) Your letter of the 3rd June addressed to Bapu was received by him today.
('87', 424, 6, 9, 614438) There is a great pressure of work on him, so he has asked me to reply to it.
('87', 424, 7, 10, 614515) Bapu said that he had also received your earlier letter, but owing to rush of work he could not send a reply.
('87', 424, 7, 11, 614625) After coming here I am better able to realize what a tremendous burden of work rests on him and how he can deal with it only bit by bit on account of his reduced capacity.
('87', 424, 7, 12, 614797) There is no quick disposal of work as before.
('87', 424, 7, 13, 614843) Besides, the present happenings in the country also take up much of his time.
('87', 424, 8, 14, 614921) About the “Daily Thoughts”, Bapu inquired whether they would be published in Hindi only or there would also be English rendering simultaneously.If there is to be an English translation, then he will like to see it himself and this task he will not be able to shoulder at present.
('87', 424, 8, 15, 615201) I do not exactly remember what we had decided about the English translation.
('87', 424, 8, 16, 615278) So please write to me by return of post.
('87', 424, 8, 17, 615319) If it is only the Hindi edition, then there will be no difficulty in Bapu’s writing a preface to it.
('87', 424, 8, 18, 615420) Perhaps it would be easier for him to find time for it.
('87', 424, 9, 19, 615476) As regards the questions you had sent to Bapu in respect of your book “To the Statesmen of the World”, Bapu says that he would have gladly answered them, but that at the present moment his mind is not disposed to undertake that burden either.
('87', 424, 9, 20, 615719) You will, therefore, have to do without his answer to your questions.
('87', 424, 10, 21, 615789) I had spoken to Bapu regarding the Navajivan and the “Gandhi Series”.
('87', 424, 10, 22, 615859) He advised me that since Naraharibhai was here, I should personally hear what he has to say.
('87', 424, 10, 23, 615952) I had, therefore, a brief talk with him last evening and will have further discussion with him again today.
('87', 424, 10, 24, 616060) Then we shall see where the matter stands.
('87', 424, 11, 25, 616103) Have you got enough supply of paper for bringing out your new book “To the Statesmen”?
('87', 424, 11, 26, 616190) I learn that the Government is increasing the paper quota.
('87', 424, 11, 27, 616249) How far is it

('87', 425, 5, 8, 616585) SPEECH BROADCAST BY THE VICEROY 1
('87', 425, 6, 9, 616619) June 14, 1945
('87', 425, 7, 10, 616633) I have been authorized by His Majesty’s Government to place before Indian political leaders proposals designed to ease the present political situation and to advance India towards her goal of full self government.
('87', 425, 7, 11, 616847) These proposals are at the present moment being explained to Parliament by the Secretary of State for India.
('87', 425, 7, 12, 616956) My intention in this broadcast is to explain to you the proposals, the ideas underlying them, and the method by which I hope to put them into effect.
('87', 425, 8, 13, 617106) This is not an attempt to obtain or impose a constitutional settlement.
('87', 425, 8, 14, 617178) His Majesty’s Government had hoped that the leaders of the Indian parties would agree amongst themselves on a settlement of the communal issue, which is the main stumbling block; but this hope has not been fulfilled.
('87', 425, 9, 15, 617395) In the mean time, India has great opportunities to be taken and great problems to be solved, which require a common effort by the leading men of all parties.
('87', 425, 9, 16, 617553) I, therefore, propose, with the full support of His Majesty’s Government, to invite Indian leaders, both of Central and Provincial politics, to take counsel with me with a view to the formation of a new Executive Council more representative of organized political opinion.
('87', 425, 9, 17, 617826) The proposed new Council would represent the main communities and would include equal proportions of caste Hindus and Muslims.
('87', 425, 9, 18, 617953) It would work, if formed, under the existing Constitution.
('87', 425, 9, 19, 618012) But it would be an entirely Indian Council, except for the Viceroy and the Commander in Chief, who would retain his position as War Member.
('87', 425, 9, 20, 618152) It is also proposed that the portfolio of External Affairs, which has hitherto been held by the Viceroy, should be placed in charge of an Indian Member of Council, so far as the interests of British India are concerned.
('87', 425, 10, 21, 618372) A further step proposed by His Majesty’s Government is the appointment of a
('87', 425, 11, 22, 618448) 1Vide “Telegram to Private Secretary to Viceroy”, 14 6 1945; “Telegram to Lord Wavell”, 15 6 1945; “Statement to the press”, 15 6 1945 and “Interview to associated Press of India”, 30 6 1945.
('87', 426, 0, 1, 618640) VOL. 87 : 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 427
('87', 426, 1, 2, 618683) British High Commissioner in India, as in the Dominions, to represent Great Britains’ commercial and other such interests in India.
('87', 426, 2, 3, 618815) Such a new Executive Council will, you realize, represent a definite advance on the road to self government.
('87', 426, 2, 4, 618924) It will be almost entirely Indian, and the Finance and Home Members will for the first time be Indians, while an Indian will also be charged with the management of India’s Foreign Affairs.
('87', 426, 2, 5, 619113) Moreover, Members will now be selected by the Governor General after consultations with political leaders; though their appointment will of course be subject to the approval of His Majesty the King Emperor.
('87', 426, 3, 6, 619320) The council will work within the framework of the present constitution and there can be no question of the Governor General agreeing not to exercise his constitutional power of control; but it will of course not be exercised unreasonably.
('87', 426, 4, 7, 619559) I should make it clear that the formation of this interim Government will in no way prejudice the final constitutional settlement.
('87', 426, 5, 8, 619690) The main task for this new Executive Council would be:
('87', 426, 6, 9, 619745) First, to prosecute the war against Japan with the utmost energy till Japan is utterly defeated.
('87', 426, 7, 10, 619842) Secondly, to carry on the Government of British India, with all the manifold tasks of post war development in front of it, until a new permanent constitution can be agreed upon and come into force.
('87', 426, 8, 11, 620040) Thirdly, to consider, when the Members of the Government think it possible, the means by which such agreement can be achieved.
('87', 426, 8, 12, 620167) The third task is most important.
('87', 426, 8, 13, 620201) I want to make it quite clear that neither I nor His Majesty’s Government have lost sight of the need for a long term solution, and that the present proposals are intended to make a long term solution easier.
('87', 426, 9, 14, 620410) I have considered the best means of forming such a Council; and have decided to invite the following to Viceregal Lodge to advise me:
('87', 426, 10, 15, 620544) Those now holding office as Premier in a Provincial Government; or, for provinces now under Section 93 Government, those who last held the office of the Premier.
('87', 426, 11, 16, 620706) The Leader of the Congress Party and the Deputy Leader of the Muslim League in the Central Assembly; the leader of the Congress Party and the Muslim League in the Council of State; also the leader of the Nationalist Party and the European Group in the Assembly.
('87', 426, 12, 17, 620968) Mr. Gandhi and Mr. Jinnah as the recognized leaders of the two main political parties.
('87', 426, 13, 18, 621055) Rao Bahadur N. Siva Raj to represent the Scheduled Classes.
('87', 426, 14, 19, 621115) Master Tara Singh to represent the Sikhs.
('87', 427, 0, 1, 621157) 428 THE COLLETED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 427, 1, 2, 621198) Invitations to these gentlemen are being handed to them today and it is proposed to assemble the conference on 25th June at Simla where we shall be cooler than at Delhi.
('87', 427, 2, 3, 621368) I trust that all those invited will attend the conference and give me their help.
('87', 427, 2, 4, 621450) On me and on them will lie a heavy responsibility in this fresh attempt to make progress towards a final settlement of India’s future.
('87', 427, 3, 5, 621585) If the meeting is successful, I hope that we shall be able to agree on the formation of the new Executive Council at the Centre.
('87', 427, 3, 6, 621714) I also hope that it will be possible for Ministries to re assume office and again undertake the tasks of Government in the provinces now administered under Section 93 of the Constitution Act and that these Ministries will be coalitions.
('87', 427, 4, 7, 621951) If the meeting should unfortunately fail, we must carry on as at present until the parties are ready to come together.
('87', 427, 4, 8, 622070) The existing Executive Council, which has done such valuable work for India will continue it if other arrangements cannot be agreed.
('87', 427, 5, 9, 622203) But I have every hope that the meeting will succeed, if the party leaders will approach the problem with the sincere intention of working with me and with each other.
('87', 427, 5, 10, 622370) I can assure them that there is behind this proposal a most genuine desire on the part of all responsible leaders in the United Kingdom and of the British people as a whole to help India towards her goal.
('87', 427, 5, 11, 622575) I believe that this is more than a step towards that goal, it is a considerable stride forward, and a stride on the right path.
('87', 427, 6, 12, 622703) I should make it clear that these proposals affect British India only and do not make any alteration in the relations of the Princes with the Crown Representative.
('87', 427, 7, 13, 622867) With the approval of His Majesty’s Government, and after consultation with my Council, orders have been given for the immediate release of the members of the Working Committee of Congress who are still in detention.
('87', 427, 7, 14, 623083) I propose to leave the final decision about the others still under detention as the result of the 1942 disturbances to the new Central Government, if formed, and to the Provincial governments.
('87', 427, 8, 15, 623276) The appropriate time for fresh elections for the Central and Provincial legislatures will be discussed at the conference.
('87', 427, 9, 16, 623398) Finally, I would ask you all to help in creating the atmosphere of goodwill and mutual confidence that is essential if we are to make progress.
('87', 427, 9, 17, 623542) The destiny of this great country and of the many millions who live in it depends on the wisdom and good understanding of the leaders, both of action and of thought, British and Indian, at this critical moment of India’s history.
('87', 427, 10, 18, 623772) India’s military reputation never stood higher in the world than it does at present; thanks to the exploits of her sons drawn from all parts of the country.
('87', 427, 10, 19, 623929) Her representatives at international conference have won high regard for their
('87', 428, 0, 1, 624008) VOL. 87 : 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 429
('87', 428, 1, 2, 624051) statesmanlike attitude.
('87', 428, 1, 3, 624075) Sympathy for India’s aspirations and progress towards prosperity was never greater or more widespread.
('87', 428, 1, 4, 624178) We have thus great assets if we can use them wisely.
('87', 428, 1, 5, 624231) But it will not be easy, it will not be quick; there is very much to do, there are many pitfalls and dangers.
('87', 428, 1, 6, 624341) There is on all sides something to forgive and forget.
('87', 428, 2, 7, 624396) I believe in the future of India, and as far as in me lies will further her greatness.
('87', 428, 2, 8, 624483) I ask you all for your co operation and goodwill.

('87', 428, 8, 26, 625660) Second, that this can only be achieved under a constitution or constitutions framed by Indians to which the main elements are consenting parties.

('87', 429, 3, 4, 626519) The Congress and the League agree that they will join in forming an interim government in the Centre.
('87', 429, 3, 5, 626621) The composition of such Government will be on the following lines:
('87', 429, 4, 6, 626688) (a) An equal number of persons nominated by the Congress and the League in the Central Executive (the persons nominated need not be members of the Central Legislature),
('87', 429, 5, 7, 626857) (b) representatives of minorities (in particular the Scheduled Castes and the Sikhs),
('87', 429, 6, 8, 626943) (c) the Commander in Chief.
('87', 429, 7, 9, 626971) The Government will be formed and will function within the framework of the existing Government of India Act.
('87', 429, 7, 10, 627081) It is, however, understood that, if the Cabinet cannot get a particular measure passed by the Legislative Assembly, they will not enforce the same by resort to any of the reserve powers of the Governor General or the Viceroy.
('87', 429, 7, 11, 627307) This will make them sufficiently independent of the Governor General.
('87', 429, 8, 12, 627377) It is agreed between the Congress and the League that, if such interim government is formed, their first step would be to release the Working Committee members of the Congress.
('87', 429, 9, 13, 627554) The steps by which efforts would be made to achieve this end are at present indicated to take the following course:
('87', 429, 10, 14, 627670) On the basis of the above understanding some way should he found to get the Governor General to make a proposal or a suggestion that he desires an interim Government to be formed in the Centre on the agreement between the Congress and the League and when the Governor General invites Mr. Jinnah and Mr. Desai either jointly or separately, the above proposal would be made declaring that they are prepared to join in forming the government.
('87', 429, 11, 15, 628110) The next step would be to get the withdrawal of Section 93 in the Provinces and to form as soon as possible Provincial Governments on the lines of a coalition.

('87', 431, 1, 2, 629666) APPENDIX VI
('87', 431, 2, 3, 629678) STATEMENT MADE IN PARLIAMENT BY SECRETARY OF STATE FOR INDIA 1
('87', 431, 3, 4, 629741) June 14, 1945
('87', 431, 4, 5, 629755) During the recent visit of Field Marshal Viscount Wavell to this country, His Majesty’s Government reviewed with him a number of problems and discussed particularly the present political situation in India.
('87', 431, 5, 6, 629962) Members will be aware that since the offer by His Majesty’s Government to India of March 1942, there has been no further progress towards the solution of the Indian constitutional problem.
('87', 431, 6, 7, 630151) As was then stated, the working out of India’s new constitutional system is a task which can only be carried through by the Indian people themselves.
('87', 431, 7, 8, 630301) While His Majesty’s Government are at all times most anxious to do their utmost to assist the Indians in the working out of a new constitutional settlement, it would be a contradiction in terms to speak of the imposition by this country of self governing institutions upon an unwilling India.
('87', 431, 7, 9, 630594) Such a thing is not possible, nor could we accept the responsibility for enforcing such institutions at the very time when we were, by its purpose, withdrawing from all control of British Indian affairs.
('87', 431, 8, 10, 630798) The main constitutional position remains therefore as it was.
('87', 431, 8, 11, 630860) The offer of March 1942 stands in its entirety without change or qualification.
('87', 431, 8, 12, 630940) His Majesty’s Government still hope that the political leaders in India may be able to come to an agreement as to the procedure whereby India’s permanent future form of government can be determined.
('87', 431, 9, 13, 631139) His Majesty’s Government are, however, most anxious to make any contribution that is practicable to the breaking of the political deadlock in India.
('87', 431, 9, 14, 631288) While that deadlock lasts not only political but social and economic progress is being hampered.
('87', 431, 10, 15, 631385) The Indian administration, over burdened with the great tasks laid upon it by the war against Japan and by the planning for the post war period, is further strained by the political tension that exists.
('87', 431, 11, 16, 631588) All that is so urgently required to be done for agricultural development and for the peasants and workers of India cannot be carried through unless whole hearted co operation of every community and section of the Indian people is forthcoming.
('87', 431, 12, 17, 631831) His Majesty’s Government have therefore considered whether there is
('87', 431, 13, 18, 631899) 1Vide “Interview to The Press”, 18 6 1945.
('87', 432, 0, 1, 631942) VOL. 87 : 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 433
('87', 432, 1, 2, 631985) something which they could suggest in this interim period, under the existing constitution, pending the formulation by Indians of their future constitutional arrangements which would enable the main communities and parties to co operate more closely together and with the British to the benefit of the people of India as a whole.
('87', 432, 2, 3, 632315) It is not the intention of His Majesty’s Government to introduce any change contrary to the wishes of the major Indian communities.
('87', 432, 2, 4, 632447) But they are willing to make possible some steps forward during the interim period if the leaders of the principal Indian parties are prepared to agree to their suggestion and to co operate in the successful conclusion of the war against Japan as well as in the reconstruction in India which must follow the final victory.
('87', 432, 3, 5, 632770) To this end they would be prepared to see an important change in the composition of the Viceroy’s Executive.
('87', 432, 3, 6, 632879) This is possible without making any change in the existing statute law except for one amendment to the Ninth Schedule to the Act of 1935. That Schedule contains a provision that not less than three members of the Executive must have had at least 10 years’ service under the Crown in India.
('87', 432, 3, 7, 633169) If the proposals I am about to lay before the House meet with acceptance in India, that clause would have to be amended to dispense with that requirement.
('87', 432, 4, 8, 633324) It is proposed that the Executive Council should be reconstituted and that the Viceroy should in future make his selection to the Crown for appointment to his Executive from amongst leaders of Indian political life at the Centre and in the Provinces, in proportions which would give a balanced representation of the main communities, including equal proportions of Muslims and caste Hindus.
('87', 432, 5, 9, 633715) In order to pursue this object, the Viceroy will call into conference a number of leading Indian politicians who are the heads of the most important parties or who have had recent experience as Prime Ministers of Provinces, together with a few others of special experience and authority.
('87', 432, 5, 10, 634003) The Viceroy intends to put before this conference the proposal that the Executive Council should be reconstituted as above stated and to invite from the members of the conference a list of names.
('87', 432, 5, 11, 634199) Out of these he would hope to be able to choose the future members whom he would recommend for appointment by his Majesty to the Viceroy’s council, although the responsibility for the recommendations must of course continue to rest with him, and his freedom of choice therefore remains unrestricted.
('87', 432, 6, 12, 634499) The members of his Council who are chosen as a result of this arrangement would of course accept the position on the basis that they would whole heartedly co operate in supporting and carrying through the war against Japan to its victorious conclusion.
('87', 432, 7, 13, 634752) The members of the Executive would be Indians with the exception of the Viceroy and the Commander in Chief, who would retain his position as War
('87', 433, 0, 1, 634897) 434 THE COLLETED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 433, 1, 2, 634938) Member.
('87', 433, 1, 3, 634946) This is essential so long as the defence of India remains a British responsibility.
('87', 433, 2, 4, 635030) Nothing contained in any of these proposals will affect the relations of the Crown with the Indian States through the Viceroy as Crown Representative.
('87', 433, 3, 5, 635181) The Viceroy has been authorized by His Majesty’s Government to place this proposal before the Indian leaders.
('87', 433, 3, 6, 635291) His Majesty’s Government trust that the leaders of the Indian communities will respond.
('87', 433, 3, 7, 635379) For the success of such a plan must depend on its acceptance in India and the degree to which responsible Indian politicians are prepared to co operate with the object of making it a workable interim arrange ment.
('87', 433, 3, 8, 635593) In the absence of such general acceptance existing arrangements must neces sarily continue.
('87', 433, 4, 9, 635685) If such co operation can be achieved at the Centre it will no doubt be reflected in the provinces and so enable responsible governments to be set up once again in those provinces where, owing to the withdrawal of the majority party from participation, it became necessary to put into force the powers of the Governors under Section 93 of the Act of 1935. It is to be hoped that in all the Provinces these governments would be based on the participation of the main parties, thus smoothing out communal differences and allowing Ministers to concentrate upon their very heavy administrative tasks.
('87', 433, 5, 10, 636281) There is one further change which, if these proposals are accepted, His Majesty’s Government suggest should follow.
('87', 433, 6, 11, 636397) That is, that External Affairs (other than those tribal and frontier matters which fall to be dealt with as part of the defence of India) should be placed in the charge of an Indian Member of the Viceroy’s Executive so far as British India is concerned, and that fully accredited representatives shall be appointed for the representation of India abroad.
('87', 433, 7, 12, 636752) By their acceptance of and co operation in this scheme the Indian leaders will not only be able to make their immediate contribution to the direction of Indian affairs, but it is also to be hoped that their experience of co operation in government will expedite agreement between them as to the method of working out the new constitutional arrangements.
('87', 433, 8, 13, 637106) His Majesty’s Government consider, after the most careful study of the question, that the plan now suggested gives the utmost progress practicable within the present constitution.
('87', 433, 8, 14, 637286) None of the changes suggested will in any way prejudice or prejudge the essential form of the future permanent constitution or constitutions for India.
('87', 433, 9, 15, 637438) His Majesty’s Government feel certain that given goodwill and a genuine desire to co operate on all sides, both British and Indian, these proposals can mark a
('87', 434, 0, 1, 637597) VOL. 87 : 29 MAY, 1945 29 AUGUST, 1945 435
('87', 434, 1, 2, 637640) genuine step forward in the collaboration of the British and Indian peoples towards Indian self government and can assert the rightful position, and strengthen the influence, of India in the counsels of the nations.

('87', 434, 3, 4, 637902) APPENDIX VII
('87', 434, 4, 5, 637915) LORD WAVELL’S NOTE ON HIS INTERVIEW 1
('87', 434, 5, 6, 637953) June 24, 1945
('87', 434, 6, 7, 637967) I began by making a short statement on the objects of the proposals of H. M. G., the spirit in which they were conceived and the spirit in which I hoped they would be accepted and worked.
('87', 434, 6, 8, 638155) I emphasized the necessity for full support of the war, and that it was essential that the political parties should put in their very best men, determined to concentrate on the economic and other problems of India, and not merely to enter the Government in a party spirit.
('87', 434, 7, 9, 638428) Mr. Gandhi then made a long, tortuous and prolix statement, which dealt with the history of the Congress, British rule in India, British character, the qualities of a good soldier, and many other more or less relevant subjects.
('87', 434, 7, 10, 638656) It lasted over half an hour, and ended with a sort of general blessing on the proposals, which he said he had recommended to the Working Committee.
('87', 434, 8, 11, 638804) He then went on, referring to some notes, to deal with certain other points.
('87', 434, 8, 12, 638881) I think this was a list prepared for him as a result of the discussions by Congress Working Committee.
('87', 434, 8, 13, 638984) The main points were as follows:
('87', 434, 9, 14, 639017) (a) That it would have been much better if I had ordered the release of all the political prisoners and not merely the Working Committee.
('87', 434, 10, 15, 639155) (b) That the term ‘Caste Hindus’ should not have been used, as his great aim was that there should be no question of caste inside Congress; he would have preferred the term ‘Non Scheduled Hindus’.
('87', 434, 11, 16, 639352) (c) He then went on to the question of coalitions in Provinces, obviously with the idea of trying to establish that the minorities should be represented by members of their body belonging to Congress.
('87', 434, 12, 17, 639553) (d) He referred to the matter of parity, and said he had been under very severe pressure as regards this, but that he was prepared to accept it.
('87', 434, 12, 18, 639698) He indicated that it would be open to Congress to put forward the names of Muslims or Scheduled Castes, and I agreed but said that the principle of parity between non Scheduled Hindus and Muslims must be maintained.
('87', 434, 13, 19, 639914) (e) He then digressed into a long story about members of the Indian Army who
('87', 434, 14, 20, 639991) 1 Vide “Letter to Lord Wavell”, 25 6 1945.

('87', 435, 1, 2, 640075) had wished to see him but had been compelled, like Nicodemus, to come to him by night and in mufti.
('87', 435, 1, 3, 640175) I said that the one thing which was disastrous for any government was if the army became political; that the Indian Army had a Commander in Chief in whom they had full trust; that their reputation never stood higher and that I could assure him that the Indian Army was on the whole a thoroughly contented body.
('87', 435, 1, 4, 640486) He agreed to all these statements.
('87', 435, 2, 5, 640521) (f) He then started on the question of the Indian States.
('87', 435, 2, 6, 640579) I said that the conference dealt entirely with British India, and that I was not prepared at this stage to enter into a discussion of the Indian States.
('87', 435, 2, 7, 640732) He agreed that it had nothing to do with the conference and was not appropriate for discussion at the moment.
('87', 435, 3, 8, 640842) I asked Mr. Gandhi at the end, whether he proposed to attend the conference in person.
('87', 435, 3, 9, 640929) He said that he represented nobody except himself, and that though he would be prepared to attend the conference if I wished, and sit in a corner, he strongly advised me that his presence at the conference was undesirable.
('87', 435, 3, 10, 641152) He said that he would hold himself at my disposal for as long as I wished, but that if I had nothing on which I had to consult him he would propose to leave Simla tomorrow.
('87', 435, 3, 11, 641325) I said that I would let him know.
('87', 435, 4, 12, 641359) The interview was mainly a discursive monologue by Mr. Gandhi, interspersed by numerous digressions, such as a most graphic description of the death of his Private Secretary and the relation of his carrying down the wounded General Woodgate from Spion Kop in 1899. My general impression of him was that he was friendly for the time being, but perfectly prepared to go back at any time on anything he had said.
('87', 435, 5, 13, 641769) Wavell: The Viceroy’s Journal, pp.

('87', 436, 1, 2, 641847) APPENDIX VIII
('87', 436, 2, 3, 641861) ABUL KALAM AZAD’S LETTER TO LORD WAVELL1
('87', 436, 3, 4, 641902) ARMSDELL, SIMLA, July 15, 1945
('87', 436, 4, 5, 641933) DEAR LORD WAVELL,
('87', 436, 5, 6, 641951) After announcing the failure of the Conference, you were good enough to ask for the support of all parties in ensuring a calm atmosphere.
('87', 436, 5, 7, 642089) I do not propose to reiterate the Congress view about the failure.
('87', 436, 5, 8, 642156) I expressed it sufficiently at the Conference.
('87', 436, 5, 9, 642203) But in fairness to you and to ourselves I must point out that co operation inevitably depends on the removal of obstacles to it.
('87', 436, 5, 10, 642332) Some of these obstacles are of a psychological nature with roots in the past relations between India and England.
('87', 436, 5, 11, 642446) These can only gradually disappear with a change in those relations.
('87', 436, 5, 12, 642515) But there are others of a more tangible kind which serve as constant irritants to our people and which affect our day to day activity.
('87', 436, 5, 13, 642650) They are continually before us.
('87', 436, 5, 14, 642682) In spite of this preoccupation, however, we did not think it desirable to raise this matter, except perhaps rather vaguely in the course of conversations with you, as we were anxious not to place any difficulties in your path when you were dealing with a delicate situation.
('87', 436, 6, 15, 642957) 2. But now that one chapter has ended and our minds, as well as yours, are turned to future possibilities of finding a way out, honourable to all concerned and leading to the objective of Indian freedom, these obstacles to co operation cannot be ignored.
('87', 436, 6, 16, 643212) I am taking the liberty, therefore, of pointing them out to you in the hope that you will have early steps taken to have them removed.
('87', 436, 7, 17, 643347) 3. The steps that I consider necessary and earnestly urge upon you are:
('87', 436, 8, 18, 643419) (a) The bans on all Congress and allied organizations should be removed at once.
('87', 436, 8, 19, 643500) It has not been possible to convene the A. I. C. C. because of its being an illegal organization.
('87', 436, 9, 20, 643598) (b) All detenus should be released without any condition being imposed upon them, whether the detention was imposed by the Central Government or the Provincial Governments.
('87', 436, 10, 21, 643771) (c) All restrictions on the movements of released detenus or prisoners should be removed.
('87', 436, 11, 22, 643861) (d) Cases of all prisoners convicted for political or like offences should be examined by a popular judicial tribunal, its verdict should be regarded as final by the
('87', 436, 12, 23, 644027) 1 Vide The letter bears corrections in Gandhiji’s hand.
('87', 437, 0, 1, 644083) 438 THE COLLETED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 437, 1, 2, 644124) Government.
('87', 437, 2, 3, 644136) (e) Extra legal restrictions on the freedom of the Press or on the movement or association of people should be removed so as to make the people feel that they are free to follow normal activities under democratic conditions.
('87', 437, 3, 4, 644361) (f) All pending sentences of hanging arising out of the disturbances of August 1942 should be commuted to life sentences.
('87', 437, 4, 5, 644483) (g) All pending arrests of ‘absconders’ should be cancelled.
('87', 437, 5, 6, 644544) (h) All prisoners who have served full fourteen years should be unconditionally discharged.
('87', 437, 6, 7, 644636) (i) What has been said above about prisoners applies equally, and with even greater force, to properties, movable and immovable, and frozen or confiscated.
('87', 437, 7, 8, 644792) 4. I have not endeavoured to argue out the justness of the foregoing requirements as I have no doubt that you will yourself appreciate the need for action along the lines indicated.
('87', 437, 7, 9, 644974) If India is on the eve of having a bona fide national representative Executive, leading to independence after the defeat of Japan, then the necessity for this approach is self proved and inevitable.
('87', 437, 8, 10, 645173) 5. There is another matter to which I should like to refer.
('87', 437, 8, 11, 645233) I need hardly say on behalf of the Congress that whatever the result of your promised effort the Congress is and has always been against the Japanese aggression.
('87', 437, 8, 12, 645395) Therefore, there will always be on the part of the Congress a desire for the defeat of Japan in her designs upon China or any other aggression on her part.
('87', 437, 8, 13, 645551) But the thought expressed in this paragraph will be incomplete if I did not inform you that, in the Congress estimation, the effort now being made on Indian soil will continue to be looked upon as a British and Allied effort, so long as there is not at the Centre a popular government assisted by provincial popular governments.
('87', 437, 8, 14, 645880) Yours sincerely, HIS EXCELLENCY VISCOUNT WAVELL VICEREGAL LODGE SIMLA
('87', 437, 9, 15, 645950) A.I.C.C. File No.

('87', 438, 1, 2, 646072) APPENDIX IX
('87', 438, 2, 3, 646084) MARRIAGE RITES 1
('87', 438, 3, 4, 646101) The marriage between Ganapat Narayan Mahadev Tendulkar and Indumati Nagesh Vasudev Gunaji is being solemnized and I perform the ceremony with God as witness.
('87', 438, 3, 5, 646259) Both of you should also do the same.
('87', 438, 3, 6, 646296) Those who are witness to this ceremony should keep their minds pure and thus help in the realization of the sacred wish of the couple getting married.
('87', 438, 4, 7, 646447) Now I shall recite a bhajan thanking God.
('87', 438, 4, 8, 646489) All of you should listen to it carefully.
('87', 438, 4, 9, 646531) (Bhajan “Aaj milkar geet gao”)
('87', 438, 5, 10, 646562) Q. Are both of you composed?
('87', 438, 6, 11, 646591) A. (Both to say :) Yes.
('87', 438, 7, 12, 646615) Q. Have you performed the seven yajnas 2 as described to you yesterday?
('87', 438, 8, 13, 646687) A. Yes.
('87', 438, 9, 14, 646695) Q. I hope that you know that this relationship is not for sexual gratification or enjoyment.
('87', 438, 10, 15, 646788) A. Yes.
('87', 438, 11, 16, 646796) Q. Are you entering the Grihastha Ashram in a spirit of duty, dedication and sacrifice?
('87', 438, 12, 17, 646884) A. Yes.
('87', 438, 13, 18, 646892) Q. And therefore you will not obstruct each other in his or her work of service, but assist each other?
('87', 438, 14, 19, 646996) A. Yes.
('87', 438, 15, 20, 647004) Q. Will you be always loyal to each other in thought, word and deed?
('87', 438, 16, 21, 647073) A. Yes.
('87', 438, 17, 22, 647081) Q. Will you try your best not to have children till India wins independence?
('87', 438, 18, 23, 647158) A. Yes.
('87', 438, 19, 24, 647166) Q. You do approve the idea of inter dining and inter marrying with the so called untouchables, don’t you?
('87', 438, 20, 25, 647272) A. Yes.
('87', 438, 21, 26, 647280) Q. You do believe that men and women have equal rights?
('87', 438, 22, 27, 647336) A. Yes.
('87', 438, 23, 28, 647344) Q. Both of you are friends and neither is a slave to the other.
('87', 438, 23, 29, 647408) Isn’t that correct also?
('87', 438, 24, 30, 647433) 1 Vide “Letter to D.B. Kalelkar”, 6 8 1945. 2 Vide “Letter to Dr. A. G. Tendulkar”, 18 8 1945.
('87', 439, 0, 1, 647528) 440 THE COLLETED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('87', 439, 1, 2, 647569) A. Yes.
('87', 439, 2, 3, 647577) Q. You understand, don’t you, that the seven yajnas mentioned in the second question are in place of the saptapadi?
('87', 439, 3, 4, 647693) A. Yes.
('87', 439, 4, 5, 647701) Now by this yarn spun by me I bind you in union.
('87', 439, 4, 6, 647750) You should preserve the yarn garland carefully and should resolve that you will never break this union.
('87', 439, 4, 7, 647854) Bear in mind the religious ceremony and pray to omnipotent God to help you in the fulfilment of the vows you have just taken.
('87', 439, 4, 8, 647980) Now we shall all together sing the Ramdhun.
('87', 439, 5, 9, 648024) August 18, 1945
